1601 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Canova v. McKell


C.A. No. 01A01-9803-JV-00113


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 124



February 25, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] NOT FOR PUBLICATION


PRIOR HISTORY: Juvenile Court. Davidson County. Hon. Andrew J. Shookhoff, Judge. Davidson Juvenile No. 9719-38503.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of a decision from the Juvenile Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), granting respondent's motion for summary judgment as to petitioners' suit seeking to establish visitation rights under the Grandparents Visitation Rights Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306 (1997).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, the grandparents and great-grandparents of respondent mother's son, challenged the juvenile court's grant of summary judgment to respondent as to petitioners' suit seeking visitation rights under the Grandparents Visitation Rights Act (GVRA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306 (1997). The child's father, petitioners' son and grandson, had never married respondent; he was subsequently killed in an automobile accident. On appeal, the court followed precedent set by another panel of the appeals court holding that the GVRA was an unconstitutional invasion of privacy rights under the Tennessee Constitution because the statute permitted grandparental visitation without a prior evaluation of whether the child's best interests would be harmed by a cessation in the grandparental relationship. The court affirmed the dismissal of petitioners' suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of petitioners' suit seeking court-ordered visitation with their illegitimate grandchild because a state statute permitting grandparental visitation without a prior determination that the child would be harmed by cessation of the grandparental relationship violated the mother's and child's privacy rights.

 

1602 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9707-CH-00338


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 90



February 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition for Rehearing Dismissed June 18, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 379. Application for Permission to Appeal Dismissed October 11, 1999.
Rehearing dismissed by Taylor v. State, 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 379 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 18, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL L. MCCOY, CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 96-859-11.
State v. Taylor, 668 S.W.2d 681, 1984 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 2498 (Tenn. Crim. App., 1984)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, convicted of murder, appealed an order from the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which dismissed his request for a declaratory judgment. As applied to felonies committed prior to the enactment of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-20-112, which made all felonies infamous crimes, plaintiff claimed that the provisions of the statute violated the ex post facto prohibitions of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was convicted of murder. On the date the crime was committed, murder was not an infamous crime. Subsequently, the Tennessee legislature amended Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-20-112 to make all felonies infamous crimes resulting in a loss of the right to vote. Plaintiff sought a declaration that the law, as applied to him, violated the ex post facto provisions of Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 17 and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. Plaintiff also relied on Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 5 and its guarantee of the right of suffrage. The trial court granted defendant state's motion to dismiss, disagreeing with plaintiff's argument that his crime must have been infamous at the time it was committed. The court held that plaintiff's act could be declared infamous as it was committed before enactment of the statute and prior to his conviction. The court also found that the laws disenfranchising convicted felons were simply remedial statutes that did not increase criminal penalties. Accordingly, the court held that such laws were not ex post facto laws within the prohibition of the state or federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting defendant state's motion to dismiss, and remanded. Defendant's murder offense could be declared infamous where it was committed prior to enactment of the statute making all felonies infamous crimes. Laws disenfranchising convicted felons were remedial statutes that did not increase criminal penalties. Because the laws were not criminal statutes, ex post facto prohibitions did not apply.

 

1603 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


MC Props., Inc. v. City of Chattanooga


C/A NO. 03A01-9807-CH-00216


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


994 S.W.2d 132; 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 51



January 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied July 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHANCERY COURT. HAMILTON COUNTY. HON. HOWELL N. PEOPLES, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city and defendant city council appealed an order of the Hamilton County Chancery Court (Tennessee) vacating defendants' denial of plaintiff development company's rezoning petition and requiring defendants to rezone the property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff development company requested defendant city and defendant city council rezone a tract of land. Defendants' order denying plaintiff's request was vacated by the trial court and defendants sought review. The court held that the trial court properly treated plaintiff's initial appeal of defendants' actions as a declaratory judgment action, admitting all evidence relevant to defendants' denial of plaintiff's rezoning request. But the trial court improperly determined that defendants' action was illegal, arbitrary, or capricious. Defendants' denial of plaintiff's rezoning request was not an abuse of discretion and was supported by several reasons. The trial court could not reverse defendants' decision merely because it disagreed with defendants' reasoning. Defendants did not have to provide the best use of the property and properly used their discretion to zone as they felt proper. Because there were beneficial uses available for the property at issue, there was no basis for a finding that there would be an unconstitutional taking of property absent rezoning. The court thus reversed the order vacating defendants' decision and reinstated their finding.


OUTCOME: The order vacating defendant city and defendant city council's denial of plaintiff development company's rezoning petition was reversed and defendants' decision reinstated, because defendants' decision was supported by valid reasons and was not arbitrary or capricious. Further, there was no basis for a finding that there would be an unconstitutional taking of the property absent rezoning.

 

1604 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Bowlin v. Walkup


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9805-CH-00246


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 48



January 27, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL L. McCOY, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from a judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which dismissed the petition for declaratory judgment filed by petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, an incarcerated prisoner, filed a petition for declaratory judgment against the attorney general of Tennessee and the Tennessee commissioner of corrections seeking to have Chapter 72, § 1 of the Public Acts of 1955 previously codified as Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-3901 declared unconstitutional. The lower court dismissed the petition because in light of the fact that the portion of the statute of which petitioner purported to complain was repealed five years prior to petitioner's indictment on the offenses for which he was incarcerated, there was thus no justiciable controversy and petitioner had neither standing nor interest in challenging the former statute. The court held that the holding of the lower court was clearly correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that there was no justiciable controversy, because the statute of which petitioner purported to complain was repealed five years prior to petitioner's indictment on the offenses for which he was incarcerated.

 

1605 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Tennessee Dep't of Correction


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9801-CH-00010


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 35



January 21, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied May 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 97-2523-I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Davidson County Chancery Court (Tennessee) denying petitioner's request for a correction of his sentence, arguing that, pursuant to the Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-101 et seq., he was being held unconstitutionally and illegally by respondent department of corrections for sentences arising out of his convictions for aggravated rape.


OVERVIEW: Following petitioner's convictions and sentences for aggravated rape, he petitioned respondent department of corrections for a correction of his sentences based on the Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989 (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-101 et seq. Petitioner contended that the Act, though passed following the imposition of his sentences, should have been applied retroactively to his case and would have provided a reduced sentence and an opportunity to receive good time jail credit. Respondent denied the request and the lower court affirmed. The court of appeals also affirmed, finding that petitioner was not entitled to retroactive application of the Act. The purpose of the Act was to address the issue of overcrowding and specifically limited application to persons who were not previously sentenced. Contrary to petitioner's assertion, the mere fact that the penalty was reduced by new legislation did not mean that his sentence under the old law was disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying petitioner's request for a correction of his sentence was affirmed because defendant was not entitled to retroactive application of a sentencing reform act.

 

1606 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Florence v. Florence


C. A. NO. 01A01-9802-CH-00085


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 40



January 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Chancery Court. Coffee County. HON. JOHN ROLLINS, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of decision from the Chancery Court, Coffee County (Tennessee), in an action by appellee wife, which sought an increase in child support. Appellant counterclaimed, challenging the constitutionality of the child support guidelines. The trial court denied relief to appellant, holding he had come into court with unclean hands. The court applied child support guidelines and entered judgment against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband sought review of decision in an action by appellee wife, which sought an increase in child support. Appellant challenged the constitutionality and application of the child support guidelines. The trial court entered judgment against appellant, applied the child support guidelines, and denied appellant relief on the grounds that he had come into court with unclean hands. The appellate court concluded that the matter should be remanded to the trial court for consideration of the new regulations. Changes in the child support guidelines became effective after a trial on the petition for increase in support, but prior to entry of the trial court's final order. The appellate court held the matter should be remanded in the interests of judicial economy. The doctrine of unclean hands, per se, was not sufficient to deny appellant the right to challenge the constitutionality of a statute, rule or regulation or its application. An unconstitutional statute or an amendment to a constitutional statute was void ab initio. The court held the same rule applied in its application to rules and regulations promulgated pursuant to governmental authority. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded in an appeal and counterclaim by appellant husband from a request by appellee wife for an increase in child support. The court held that the trial court could not deny appellant relief in his challenge of the constitutionality of the child support guidelines on the grounds of unclean hands. That doctrine was not sufficient to deny challenge to constitutionality of child support guidelines.

 

1607 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Holzinger v. Industrial Dev. Bd.


C.A. No. 01A01-9711-CV-00685


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 8



January 11, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court of Montgomery County at Clarksville. Honorable James E. Walton, Judge. Montgomery County Circuit Court No. C11-568.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate developer appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County at Clarksville (Tennessee) granting summary judgment to defendant industrial development board on defendant's counterclaim regarding the expiration of an option to purchase land for which plaintiff sought rezoning.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff real estate developer filed suit against defendants city council, city, and industrial development board, after the city council denied its request for a rezoning ordinance for land plaintiff had an option to purchase from defendant industrial development board. Defendant industrial development board counterclaimed against plaintiff to rescind the option to purchase and filed a summary judgment motion on the issue. Plaintiff appealed the grant of summary judgment arguing improper joinder of claims. The court agreed with plaintiff noting that the claims were different in nature because defendant's claim was a normal action as opposed to plaintiff's appeal of a denial of a zoning request by writ of certiorari. The court held that defendant's counterclaim should have been dismissed but that defendant could bring his claim in a separate action. The court therefore reversed the grant of summary judgment for defendant and dismissed the counterclaim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's granting of defendant's summary judgment motion was reversed and defendant's counterclaim dismissed because it was an original jurisdiction action brought in an appellate jurisdiction action and therefore improperly joined.

 

1608 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Sorrel v. Henson


Appeal No. 02A01-9609-JV-00212


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 852



December 18, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied May 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE JUVENILE COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE KENNETH TURNER, JUDGE. Shelby Juvenile No. H331.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order by the Juvenile Court of Shelby County at Memphis, Tennessee, which established his paternity of appellee mother's unborn child. Appellant argued that the paternity statutes violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellee mother filed a petition to establish appellant father's paternity of her unborn child. Testing showed that appellant was the father to a near certainty. Appellant requested the juvenile court to dismiss the action because the paternity statutes violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. His motion was denied and an order was entered establishing his paternity and directing payment of child support. On appeal of the denial of appellant's motion, the court recognized the constitutional protection afforded the right to procreate. However, the court found that that right was irrelevant to paternity actions, which resulted from the private acts of the biological parents and that any private wrong interfering with a man's procreational autonomy did not rise to the level of a constitutional violation. Rejecting appellant's claim that paternity actions violated equal protection guarantees, the court found that any different treatment accorded women after conception stemmed from the operation of nature rather than state law. Affirming the judgment, the court held that the paternity statutes did not violate the right to privacy or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court establishing appellant father's paternity of appellee mother's son. The court held that appellant's motion to dismiss on Fourteenth Amendment grounds was properly denied because the paternity statutes did not violate his rights to equal protection or to privacy.

 

1609 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Home Builders Ass'n of Middle State v. Maury County


Appeal No. 01A01-9706-CH-00259


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 846



December 15, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF MAURY COUNTY AT COLUMBIA, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE JIM T. HAMILTON, JUDGE. Maury Chancery No. 96-487.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homebuilders association filed an action against defendants, a county and the state attorney general, seeking a declaratory judgment that a county tax was unconstitutional, and seeking an injunction prohibiting the county from implementing or collecting taxes under the Maury County Adequate Facilities Tax Act (Tax Act). The Chancery Court of Maury County at Columbia, Tennessee denied defendants' motion to dismiss, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county commission ratified and set the tax, but it later declared that it would not be imposed at that time. The commission set the tax rate at $ 0.00 for both residential and non-residential development, and no tax had been collected under the Tax Act. The association filed its action under the Declaratory Judgment Act, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-14-101 to 113. Defendants maintained that the challenged tax had never been imposed, that there was no real threat that it would be imposed, and that the case did not involve a justiciable controversy. The court found that before the tax could be collected, it had to first be set above a rate of zero by the commission. There was no indication in the record that the commission would choose to raise the rate above zero and enforce the tax statute. The challenged tax had not been imposed, and there was no indication in the record that it would be imposed. Therefore, at the time of the lawsuit, a controversy existed only in a theoretical sense. Consequently, there was no justiciable controversy under the Tennessee Declaratory Judgment Act. The trial court erred in denying defendants' motion to dismiss, and the decision was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the cause to the trial court for entry of an order granting defendants' motion to dismiss.

 

1610 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Guardsmark, Inc. v. Borg-Warner Protective Servs.


Appeal No. 02A01-9409-CH-00207


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 743; 14 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1457



November 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE C. NEAL SMALL, CHANCELLOR. Shelby Chancery No. 104166-1.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant private security company sought review of the judgment of the Chancery Court of Shelby Count at Memphis (Tennessee) that granted plaintiff private security company's motion for summary judgment and issued an injunction against defendant, in plaintiff's action which alleged that defendant interfered with restrictive employment covenants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff and defendant were competitors. Plaintiff alleged that defendant interfered with its contractual relations by actively soliciting plaintiffs employees and by misrepresenting that the restrictive covenants, which plaintiff had its employees sign, were unenforceable. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss, granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, and issued an injunction. The injunction enjoined defendant from inducing former employees to breach the restrictive covenants in other states, from misrepresenting facts concerning the enforceability of the covenants, or from litigating or assisting others in litigating in other states regarding the enforceability of the restrictive covenants. On appeal, the court reversed the injunctive order, finding that the enforceability of the covenants depended on the factual circumstances and the laws and public policy of the state in which the employee was located. Consequently, the court determined that if defendant expressed the view that the covenant were not be enforceable in a given situation, the truth of the statement depended on the factual circumstances and the law in the state involved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of injunction issued by the trial court and remanded for a determination of whether plaintiff was entitled to summary judgment in the specific factual circumstances presented in two other states and whether the plaintiffs' employees were indispensable parties considering the doctrine of collateral estoppel under the laws of those other states.

 

1611 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Ellison v. Ellison


C.A. No. 02A01-9803-CH-00054


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


994 S.W.2d 623; 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 746



November 4, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied June 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE OBION COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM MICHAEL MALOAN, CHANCELLOR. Obion Chancery No. 20,453.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother challenged the judgment of the Obion County Chancery Court (Tennessee), which granted visitation rights as to her minor children pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306 (Supp. 1998) to plaintiff grandmother.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended, inter alia, that § 36-6-306 was unconstitutional because it authorized courts to order grandparent visitation upon a finding that such visitation was in the "best interest" of the child without first requiring the finding of a danger of substantial harm to the child. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court. The court observed that parents possessed a constitutional right of privacy in parenting decisions not subject to interference from the state absent a showing of substantial harm to the child. The court reasoned that there was no real difference between the rights of a single parent and both parents. The court held that the language of § 36-6-306, allowing reasonable visitation rights to grandparents upon a finding of the best interest of the minor child, constituted an unconstitutional invasion of privacy rights under the Tennessee Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which granted the grandmother visitation rights as to the mother's minor children, and remanded the case to the trial court.

 

1612 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Norton v. Campbell


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9709-CH-00557


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 715



October 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL L. MCCOY, CHANCELLOR. No. 97-206(II).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who was in the custody of the Tennessee Department of Correction (Department), petitioned the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee) for judicial review of the constitutionality of a statute that rendered him ineligible for early release from his sentence. The trial court dismissed the petition and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of rape of a child and sentenced to two concurrent 20-year terms. The inmate did not present any disputed facts, and his plea for relief rested on conclusions of law alone. Just as there was no requirement or need for a prior factual inquiry, there was no reason to remand the case to the Department. The inmate failed to demonstrate that he had standing to raise any issues related to the governor's pardoning power; the record did not reveal that he applied to the governor for leniency, and he did not allege that the governor had been prevented from pardoning him by virtue of the workings of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-523. The inmate was not entitled to have the challenged statute examined under the strict scrutiny standard; he was not a member of any suspect class by virtue of his post-1992 conviction of rape, and he had at least temporarily forfeited his fundamental right to personal liberty by virtue of a valid conviction and sentence, imposed through due process of law. The application of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-523 to the inmate's sentence was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

1613 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Sundquist


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9705-CV-00209


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 597



August 24, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Granted January 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE WALTER C. KURTZ, JUDGE. Davidson Circuit No. 97C-941.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, birth parents, adoptive parents, and adoption agency (parents), appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted the motion of defendants, governor and commissioner (state), to dismiss and denied the parents' motion for a temporary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The parents challenged an adoption law which allowed the release of identifying information to adult adopted children concerning their birth parents. The parents contended that the new law impaired prior vested rights, violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 20, and deprived them of their privacy rights and interests as guaranteed by the Tennessee Constitution. The parents unsuccessfully brought their case in federal court and then moved to state court, which granted them a temporary restraining order and then granted the state's motion to dismiss and denied the parents a temporary injunction. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the new law impaired a vested right in the confidentiality of identifying information in adoption files acquired under existing law. The court found that the law created a new right for adopted persons, so it was a substantive change in the law and not a procedural or remedial one. The court held that the parents relied on the confidentiality provisions of the law, and their interest in the confidentiality of identifying information was a proper interest for the state to protect. The court limited its holding to birth parents and not adoptive parents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granting the state's motion to dismiss and denying the parents' motion for a temporary injunction, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1614 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Planned Parenthood v. Sundquist


Appeal No. 01A01-9601-CV-00052


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 562



August 12, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 606.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE HAMILTON GAYDEN, JUDGE. No. 92C-1672.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctors sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that modified state abortion regulations, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-15-201, 39-15-202, that the doctors challenged as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff doctors challenged state abortion regulations, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-15-201, 39-15-201. The court held that the trial court improperly modified and interpreted the applicable statutory language. The court held the hospitalization requirement for pregnancies more than three months along was not unduly burdensome. The court held the statute's requirements that only the attending physician could provide patients with mandatory counseling, which had to include all of the options, available assistance agencies known to the physician should the patient chose to give birth, and risks associated with the abortion procedure, were not unduly burdensome. The court held that, in and of itself, the mandatory two day waiting period was not burdensome. However, the court held that the combined effect of the physician only counseling and the mandatory waiting period operated to unconditionally burden a woman's exercise of her procreational rights. The court also held that the medical emergency exceptions to the abortion regulations were unconstitutionally narrow because they failed to provide protection for a woman's health and only covered circumstances threatening a woman's life.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the modifications made by the trial court to the abortion statutes, and remanded. The court held the statutes were unconstitutional as written because the medical emergency exceptions to the abortion regulations failed to provide protection for a woman's health, and the combination of physician only counseling and the mandatory waiting period was unduly burdensome.

 

1615 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Eye Clinic, P.C. v. Jackson-Madison County Gen. Hosp.


Appeal No. 02A01-9707-CH-00143


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


986 S.W.2d 565; 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 488



July 24, 1998 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied January 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF MADISON COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE JOE C. MORRIS, CHANCELLOR. Madison Chancery No. 51932.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital district sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court of Madison County at Memphis, Tennessee, which granted summary judgment to plaintiff doctors after determining that the hospital district's business activities violated the Tennessee Constitution.


OVERVIEW: After defendant hospital district terminated plaintiff doctors' contracts and limited its provider network to certain clinics and specialists, the doctors brought an action. They alleging that the state constitution prohibited the district from co-owning provider networks and from operating preferred provider organizations (PPO) because the conduct resulted in a public entity engaging in private business and it denied the doctors due process and equal protection. The lower court awarded the doctors summary judgment and enjoined the district from operating PPOs and companies in which it owned stock. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the district's conduct was not prohibited under Tenn. Const. art. II, §§ 29, 31 because the district was not a county, city, or town, but was a quasi-municipal entity, and because the word "state" could did not include an arm of the state. Nor was the conduct prohibited under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8, because there was no law forbidding the district from operating a PPO, the doctors had no vested right to employment with the district, and the district had a rational economic basis for terminating the doctors' contracts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for appellee doctors because appellant hospital district's conduct was not unconstitutional. The district was not forbidden from operating a preferred provider organization because it was not a county, city, or town, and the word "state" did not encompass an arm of the state. The doctors had no vested right to work for the district, which had a rational basis for ending the doctors' contracts.

 

1616 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Todd v. Weakley County


Appeal No. 02A01-9708-CV-00197


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 479



July 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 628.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF WEAKLEY COUNTY AT DRESDEN, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM B. ACREE, JUDGE. Trial Court No. 2718.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor state sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Weakley County (Tennessee) dismissing plaintiff nursing home patient's medical malpractice action against defendants, nursing home aides, a nursing home administrator, and a nurse, on the ground that the exception for health care practitioners in the Tennessee Governmental Tort Liability Act (GTLA), codified at Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-20-310, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The nursing home patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendants pursuant to the GTLA after she was dropped while being moved from her wheelchair to her bed. Defendants moved to dismiss the action on the ground that the GTLA's exception for health care practitioners was unconstitutional. The state moved for leave to intervene for the sole purpose of defending the constitutionality of the GTLA. The trial court granted the state's motion to intervene and granted defendants' motion to dismiss the action. On appeal by the state, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court found that the challenged statutory provisions were constitutional. The court further found that the statutory term "health care practitioner" was not unconstitutionally vague and that the trial court erred in so ruling. Accordingly, the court determined that two of the defendants qualified as "health care practitioners" and two defendants did not.


OUTCOME: The order granting defendants' motion to dismiss the nursing home patient's medical malpractice action was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

1617 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Delaney v. Thompson


Appeal No. 01A01-9806-CH-00304


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 486



July 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected July 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ELLEN HOBBS LYLE, CHANCELLOR. No. 98-1048-I(II)(III).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, DISMISSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judge and defendants, State Coordinator of Elections and others, appealed a decision of the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which held that the Tennessee Plan's provision for selection and retention of state judges was unconstitutional. The action was brought seeking a permanent injunction against the Coordinator from conducting elections under it, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-4-101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The judge filed an action to enjoin an election for judicial seats under the Tennessee Plan, alleging that its provision for selection and retention of state judges was unconstitutional and that it virtually insured the name of the incumbent on the ballot, which eliminated the right for appellate judges to be elected by the qualified voters. The trial court held that the Tennessee Plan was unconstitutional because it drastically limited the group of persons who could become appellate judges. The Coordinator was permanently enjoined from following the procedures of the Tennessee Plan in conducting elections for the seats. Both parties appealed. The court reversed the decision, holding that the Plan was not unconstitutional. The Plan did not drastically limit the group of persons who could become appellate judges, it simply structured an application procedure designed to insure the quality of the judges while minimizing the politics of the process. The court also found that the Plan contained requirements that the incumbent serve satisfactorily in order to be on the ballet, which eliminated the automatic right to be included on the ballot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision that the election of appellate judges under the Tennessee Plan was unconstitutional. The action was brought by a judge challenging the constitutionality of the Plan and seeking to permanently enjoin the Coordinator from conducting elections under it.

 

1618 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Greene v. Tennessee Dep't of Correction


Appeal No. 01A01-9608-CH-00370


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 461



July 10, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 94-927-I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the decision of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted the summary judgment motion filed by respondent, the state Department of Corrections, and dismissed the petition for declaratory relief. The petition, filed under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-322, urged that the petitioner had accumulated enough good time credits to be eligible for immediate release from prison.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to 99 years in prison for first degree murder. After over 20 years in prison, he filed a petition for declaratory relief with the state Department of Corrections. Petitioner argued that under three different sentence credit programs, he had accumulated enough good time credits to be released. The department denied the petition, and the chancery court affirmed the department's decision. Petitioner argued on appeal that he was entitled to both good and honor time credits available when he was first incarcerated, as well as to the good conduct sentence credits authorized by Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-29-229. The court explained that § 41-29-229 replaced the older systems of earning sentence credits. Petitioner was entitled to the good and honor time credits earned before enactment of § 41-29-229 and to good sentence credits under the new statute thereafter. Petitioner's argument that the recalculation of his sentence violated the Ex Post Facto clause was meritless, because § 41-29-299 decreased petitioner's sentence. Finally, the court found that the department had correctly calculated petitioner's good and honor time. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's decision to deny the petitioner's request for immediate release from prison based on the number of good time credits he had accumulated.

 

1619 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Day v. City of Decherd


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9708-CH-00442


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 440



July 1, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF FRANKLIN COUNTY AT WINCHESTER, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE L. CURTIS SMITH, SITTING BY INTERCHANGE. Franklin Chancery No. 14,381.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners appealed a judgment of the Chancery Court of Franklin County at Winchester, Tennessee, dismissing their petition for common law certiorari alleging that appellee city acted arbitrarily and capriciously in refusing to rezone their property from residential to commercial.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased residential property and sought a zone change so that the property could be used for mini-warehouses. The planning commission recommended the change but apprised the owners of the fact that the ordinance would have to pass three readings before the board of mayor and aldermen. The ordinance passed the first two readings, but when moved for passage on third and final reading, it failed for lack of a second. The trial court found that the city's denial of the requested zoning change was supported by the record. On appeal, the owners argued that the board's action should be set aside because the board refused to re-zone the property solely on the basis of neighborhood opposition, and that the caselaw Hoover standard made the board's decision arbitrary. The appellate court held that the owners' reliance on the Hoover standard was fundamentally flawed, as it involved a board acting in an administrative or quasi-judicial capacity. The legislators of the city were not to be condemned for doing their job, and the common law writ of certiorari was not the appropriate vehicle by which to review the "purely legislative" acts of the legislative body.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the cause was remanded for any further proceedings necessary.

 

1620 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


McMurry v. Hancock County Election Comm'n


NO. 03A01-9804-CH-00148


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 306



May 6, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. HANCOCK COUNTY. HON. WILLIAM DALE YOUNG, Chancellor, By Interchange.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge, a nonlawyer, was elected to the position in a general election. The judge then timely filed a qualifying petition for a later primary election. The judge appealed appellee county election commission's determination that the judge was not qualified to hold the office and not entitled to seek it under Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-15-5005. The judge appealed the decision of the trial court (Tennessee), which died his request for injunction.


OVERVIEW: The judge sought election as a county general sessions judge. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's denial of injunctive relief and held that the judge was not qualified, pursuant to § 16-15-5005, to seek election. The court held that § 16-15-5005 required that all persons occupying the office of general sessions judge be licensed to practice law in the state. The court held that the legislature had the authority to require that a judge be a licensed attorney. The court held that the legislature was permitted to lawfully prescribe qualifications for judges that were reasonable and the requirement that a judge be a licensed attorney was upheld previously. The court found no denial of the right to suffrage and held that the voters were free to vote or not vote as they chose. The court held that the fact that the choice may have been limited did not invalidate the mandated requirement that the general sessions judge be a licensed attorney.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of injunctive relief and held that the judge was not qualified to seek election to the office of general sessions judge.

Harless v. City of Kingsport


C/A NO. 03A01-9707-CH-00289


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 207



March 25, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL AS OF RIGHT FROM THE SULLIVAN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. HONORABLE R. JERRY BECK, JUDGE, By Interchange.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the decision of the Sullivan Chancery Court (Tennessee), which affirmed the decision of appellee city's building official's determination that two structures owned by the property owner should be demolished.


OVERVIEW: The city's building official issued complaints for two structures that were owned by the property owner that alleged that the two structures were unfit for human habitation based on the dilapidated condition of the structures. A separate hearing was held on each complaint and the city's building official was the hearing officer in the hearings. The building official ordered that each of the structures be demolished pursuant to the Kingsport, Tenn. Code § 6-323(c). The trial court affirmed the building official's order. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the grant of investigative and adjudicative functions to the building official did not deny the property owner's due process rights because the property owner failed to meet his burden of proof on the issues and the record did not support that his due process rights had been denied. The court also held that the statutes that the city's code was based on were constitutional. The court concluded that the building official's decisions were supported by substantial and material evidence and were not illegal, arbitrary, nor capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which affirmed the decision of the city's building official's determination that two structures owned by the property owner should be demolished.

 

1622 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Ramsey v. Town of Oliver Springs


C/A NO. 03A01-9708-CH-00321


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 151



February 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied June 29, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 391.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL AS OF RIGHT FROM THE ROANE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. HON. FRANK V. WILLIAMS, III, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff district attorney general filed an action against defendant town officials in which he sought a declaration that the officials' blanket policy and practice of prosecuting state cases that arose in another county in its own court was unlawful. The Roane County Chancery Court (Tennessee) entered a judgment in favor of the officials. The attorney general appealed.


OVERVIEW: Portions of the town were located in three counties. The town's city court was located in Roane County. The officials would prosecute criminal cases in the city court regardless of which county they were committed in. The chancery court concluded that the officials could continue to prosecute state cases arising in Anderson County provided that it first obtained a waiver of the right to venue from each defendant. The attorney general contended that a criminal defendant did not possess a general, unconditional right to waive venue. He argued that a change or waiver of venue may only be accomplished pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 21(a) or Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-214, and when neither of these provisions applied, offenses committed in the Anderson County portion of the town must be tried in Anderson County. The court reversed the judgment. The court held that the town's blanket policy and practice of trying Anderson County cases in Roane County, premised, as it was, on the false proposition that a defendant had an absolute right to waive venue, constituted an unlawful expansion of a defendant's right to waive venue beyond that permitted by the provisions of Rule 21(a) and § 40-35-214.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which held that the town could continue to prosecute state criminal cases that arose in another county in its court, was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for the entry of an order enjoining the town officials from continuing to implement their prosecution policies.

 

1623 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Hooker v. Thompson


Consolidated Appeal No. 01-A-01-9709-CH-00533


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


978 S.W.2d 541; 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 147



February 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 196.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL L. McCOY, CHANCELLOR, THE HONORABLE ELLEN HOBBS LYLE, CHANCELLOR. No. 96-3601-II, No. 96-2847-III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a candidate for the United States Senate, filed two actions in the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee) alleging that defendant incumbent gave or received campaign contributions in violation of Tennessee law. The chancery court dismissed both actions. The candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The senatorial candidate argued that the Tennessee law applied because U.S. Const. amend. X reserved certain powers to the states, including the right to oversee elections within their borders. The court held that Federal Election Campaign Act (FECA), 2 U.S.C.S. § 431 et seq., controlled the issue along with the Supremacy Clause. The court found that Congress intended FECA to control and preempt state laws in the arena of federal elections. In affirming, the court held that U.S. Const. amend. X did not reserve to the states the power to regulate campaign financing for federal elections. The court held that the power to do so was specifically assigned to Congress, and Congress chose to exercise its power in the federal election arena to the exclusion of all other governments. The court held that a valid and legal contribution allowed by FECA could not be prohibited by state law, just as such a contribution made illegal by FECA could not be made legal by state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the action for further proceedings. The court taxed the costs on appeal to the candidate.

 

1624 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. Mansfield


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9705-CH-00222


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 107



February 13, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY AT FAYETTEVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE LEE RUSSELL, SITTING BY INTERCHANGE. Lincoln Chancery No. 10,743.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed a complaint against defendant county officials to enjoin enforcement of a county resolution that required them to remove stock gaps on a road that crossed their farm. The Chancery Court of Lincoln County at Fayetteville (Tennessee) dismissed the property owners' complaint and granted the county officials' counterclaim to enjoin the owners from willfully allowing their cattle to roam at large along the road.


OVERVIEW: The property owners raised cattle. They placed stock gaps (cattle guards) at the point where the subject road crossed their property. Because the pastures on both sides of the road were unfenced, the cattle crossed the road at will, especially when they were fed near the road. The county officials passed a resolution that required all property owners in the area to remove the cattle guards. The property owners refused to abide by the resolution because they argued that the road was private, and the county had no right to regulate it. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the road was a public road under the theories of either an implied dedication and acceptance by the county and/or a prescriptive right obtained by adverse use for more than 20 years. The court found that the record contained ample evidence of twenty years of continuous, open, visible and uninterrupted use of the road by the public and by the employees and agents of the county. The court also held that the county had the right to require the property owners to keep their cattle off of the road.


OUTCOME: The chancery court's judgment, which dismissed the property owner's complaint and granted the county officials' counterclaim to enjoin the property owners from willfully allowing their cattle to roam at large along the road, was affirmed.

 

1625 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


McGlothlin v. Bristol Obstetrics, Gynecology & Family Planning Inc.


C/A NO. 03A01-9706-CV-00236


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 104



February 11, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] LAW COURT. SULLIVAN COUNTY. HON. JOHN McLELLAN, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mother and daughter, filed an action against defendants, abortion clinic and a doctor. Plaintiffs charged that defendants performed an abortion on the daughter, a 17 year-old, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-202, and committed malpractice and battery. The Law Court of Sullivan County (Tennessee) dismissed the violation of statute claim and granted summary judgment on the remaining causes of action. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was a 17 year old minor when she contracted for an abortion. Section 39-15-202, a criminal statute, required that if a person was under 18 years of age that the attending physician would inform that person's parents of the contemplated procedure two days prior-to the abortive procedure being performed on the minor. The trial court held that portions of § 39-15-202 were unconstitutional. Plaintiffs appealed the grant of summary judgment on their malpractice and battery claims. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that under the rule that an appellate court will only consider constitutional issues if the matter may not otherwise be resolved, no private civil right of action existed for the alleged violations of the remainder of the statute. Summary judgment in favor of defendants was proper for the battery and malpractice claims because: (1) plaintiffs failed to rebut the doctor's affidavit regarding the applicable medical standard of care, and (2) plaintiffs failed to rebut the presumption, for the battery claim, that the daughter was presumed to have the capacity to consent to the abortion.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which dismissed plaintiffs' claims regarding the violation of statute and granted summary judgment in favor of the abortion clinic and the doctor on the battery and malpractice claims, was affirmed.

Underground II v. City of Knoxville


C. A. NO. 03A01-9709-CH-00425


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 78



February 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. KNOX COUNTY. HON. SHARON BELL, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff proprietor's action that challenged the validity of Knoxville, Tenn., Code § 4.2, defendants, a city, a mayor, a chief of police, and other city officials, sought review of a judgment by the Chancery Court, Knox County (Tennessee), which held § 4.2, which prohibited the practice of "brown bagging" was valid.


OVERVIEW: The proprietor contended that § 4.2, which prohibited the practice of bringing your own alcoholic beverage into restaurants and clubs during certain business hours, was invalid. The court held that the authority over beer and other beverages not falling within the definition of "alcoholic beverage" might have been controlled and regulated by local governmental agencies. In reversing and remanding, the court held that § 4.2 placed the onus upon a proprietor of an affected business to ascertain whether his customers were in possession of alcoholic beverages upon entering the business premises. Intent or knowledge that a customer was in possession of alcohol was not a part of the ordinance. Therefore, simple possession by a patron of an alcoholic beverage or beer on the premises of the business subjected a proprietor to liability. Thus, the court concluded that § 4.2 as written was overly broad to the extent that it was unduly and overly vague. The ordinance did not establish minimal guidelines or for that matter any guidelines for its enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment.

Watson v. Tennessee Dep't of Correction


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9707-CH-00360


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


970 S.W.2d 494; 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 13



January 9, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied May 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DAVIDSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL L. McCOY, CHANCELLOR. Rule Number 96-1581-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Davidson County Chancery Court (Tennessee), which dismissed the inmate's petition for a declaratory judgment pursuant to the Declaratory Judgment Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-101 to -113 brought against appellees, Tennessee Department of Correction (TDC), Tennessee Board of Paroles (TBA), Correction Corporation of America (CCA), and individual state official.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a petition for declaratory order pursuant to the Act. The chancery court granted the CCA's motion to dismiss and granted motions to dismiss filed by the TDC and TBP alleging that the inmate did not meet the jurisdictional requirement of Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-224. The issues were: 1) whether a party can bring an action pursuant to the Act against the State; 2) whether a party can bring a declaratory judgment action against TBP; and 3) whether a party must comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-225(b) before filing an action for a declaratory order. The court found that the chancery court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because there was no evidence that the Tennessee General Assembly affirmatively authorized suits against the State when it enacted the Act. The court held that the inmate could not bring a declaratory judgment action against TBP under either the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-106(c), or the Act. The court affirmed the chancery court's decision because the inmate never filed a petition for a declaratory order to support his claim against the TDC.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's decision, which granted the CCA's, TBP's, and TDC's motions to dismiss the inmate's petition for a declaratory order.

State v. Ford


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9704-JV-00171


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 795



November 14, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied February 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. App. LEXIS 87.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PUTNAM COUNTY JUVENILE COURT AT COOKEVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE JOHN HUDSON, JUDGE. Juvenile Court No. 215.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged an order from the Putnam County Juvenile Court at Cookeville, Tennessee, which was entered terminating their parental rights.


OVERVIEW: A prior court filed an order allowing appellee Department of Human Services to remove the parents' children from their home and granting the Department temporary care and custody. The prior court subsequently found that the children were dependent and neglected and ordered the Department to retain temporary legal custody. The Department filed a petition for termination of parental rights in the juvenile court. The juvenile court found there was clear and convincing evidence requiring the termination of parental rights. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the juvenile court lacked jurisdiction to terminate parental rights. The evidence was vague with regard to where the children were residing. The petition for termination of parental rights was to be filed where the children and the foster parents intended to reside. That county was the one in which the original removal petition had been brought. There was insufficient evidence to prove that the children resided in the county where the juvenile court was located except temporarily. The juvenile court lacked jurisdiction because the jurisdiction of the prior court had attached for the purposes of dealing with the children.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court terminating parental rights. The action was remanded for an order dismissing the Department's petition for lack of jurisdiction.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Tennessee), which denied the husband's motion to terminate alimony to defendant wife pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-101(a)(2)(B) after the wife remarried.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife were divorced and the wife was awarded benefits from the husband's military retirement and alimony. The wife remarried a retired minister whose entire income was social security benefits. The husband subsequently filed a motion to terminate the alimony and benefits pursuant to § 36-5-101(a)(2)(B). The husband's sole argument was directed to the applicability of § 36-5-101(a)(2)(B), which could not be given retrospective effect.

Morris v. Correctional Enters.


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9612-CH-00543


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 740



October 29, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 96-705-I.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant government employee challenged a decision of the Chancery Court of Davidson County, Tennessee, which dismissed the employee's petition for review against appellees, employer, Tennessee Civil Service Commission (CSC), and commissioner of state department of personnel. Appellees denied the employee a termination hearing.


OVERVIEW: When the employee was terminated, he claimed that he was a career service employee that was entitled to a termination hearing and other grievance procedures. Appellees claimed that the employee had been in an executive service position, and therefore, was not entitled to a hearing before the CSC. The court vacated the order dismissing the employee's petition. The court held that the proper procedure for a state employee to obtain an authoritative answer to the question of his employment status was the filing of a declaratory order with the commissioner pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-223. The employee was given 30 days to comply with the proper procedure. The court also held that there was no basis for a § 1983 action until there had been a determination that the employee was a career service employee with a federally secured property interest in his position. The court further held that once the declaratory order action before the commissioner was final, the employee was entitled to join a § 1983 claim for attorney's fees with his petition for chancery court review of the issue that he, as a career service employee, was denied due process.


OUTCOME: The chancery court's order of dismissal was vacated, and the employee was given 30 days to properly filed for a declaratory order before the commissioner to determine the employee's status.

Rodgers v. City of Knoxville


C.A. NO. 03A01-9704-CV-00150


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 728



October 29, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied May 11, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 283. Concur in results only. Rehearing Denied September 21, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 497.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIRCUIT COURT. KNOX COUNTY. HON. HAROLD WIMBERLY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial property owners sought to have annexation ordinances passed by appellee city declared void on numerous grounds. The Circuit Court of Knox County (Tennessee) ruled adversely to the property owners on both their motion for summary judgment and the motion for summary judgment filed by the city. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners asserted that the ordinance was invalid, as it touched the municipality boundaries only on the area of a right-of-way previously annexed. Hence, the annexation of their property was invalid, as their property did not adjoin the municipal boundaries. Additionally they charged that the annexed area contained no "residents," as required by the enabling legislation and that, as the county elected to adopt a "home rule charter" form of government, it was a municipality within the meaning of the enabling statute, and thus, its territories were not subject to annexation. The appellate court held that, as counties, home-rule or otherwise, were not included in the definition of "municipality" or "municipalities" in the definitions section of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51, which related solely to changes in municipal boundaries, it seemed clear that there was no merit in the contention of the property owners that the county was a municipality, as that term related to annexation. To hold otherwise would have meant that municipalities located within a county that adopted home-rule government would be proscribed from exercising any annexation authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs were assessed to the property owners, and the cause was remanded to the trial court.

Leedom v. Bell


C.A. NO. 03A01-9704-CV-00136


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 742



October 29, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Circuit Court. Knox County. HON. DALE C. WORKMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a father and his new wife, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Knox County (Tennessee), which ruled in favor of defendants, the father's ex-wife and their daughter's psychologist, for defamation, intentional infliction of emotional distress, outrageous conduct, and for interference with the father's constitutionally protected right to his familial relationship with his daughter, and for malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The ex-wife brought her daughter to the psychologist for evaluation. The psychologist determined that the girl's father had sexually abused her and the ex-wife brought a petition to suspend the father's visitation rights. In support, the psychologist issued a letter regarding her concerns for the girl. The father brought a defamation and malpractice action. The trial court ruled in favor of the ex-wife and psychologist. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision, with the exception of the father's claim for libel. The court held that the psychologist was required by law to report her suspicions of child abuse and was immune from such a lawsuit based on the allegations of her report of suspected sexual abuse. There was no evidence of bad faith or malicious intent, nor of outrageous conduct, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and interference with their constitutionally protected right to a familial relationship based on the immunity granted. However, because the psychologist sent copies of her letter to two other parties, the court reversed on the libel count, and the court tolled the statute of limitations because the father was unable to obtain a copy of the letter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the ex-wife and the psychologist on all claims, except that the court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the psychologist on the libel claim.

 

1633 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Family Golf v. Metropolitan Gov't of Nashville


Appeal No. 01A01-9612-CH-00557


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


964 S.W.2d 254; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 688



October 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied April 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. No. 95-3832-I.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff operator of a recreation center sought review of a decision from the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which denied the operator's action for declaratory judgment and ruled in favor of defendant Metropolitan Government of Nashville and Davidson County (government), striking down a zoning ordinance that permitted the operator to construct a go-cart track.


OVERVIEW: After the planning commission refused to amend a zoning map in accordance with an amendment to an ordinance which would have allowed for the recreation park operator to build a go-cart track, the operator brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment regarding the amendment's validity. Instead, following a bench trial, the trial court struck down the ordinance, reasoning that it conflicted with the general plan of the city and the county. Upon appeal, the court held that the amendment was valid as long as it was passed in accordance with the super-majority requirements of the metropolitan charter and, accordingly, remanded the case for a definitive factual determination of that issue. The court stated that any zoning ordinance that conflicted with the general plan or that had been disapproved by the planning commission was nevertheless valid if it was enacted in accordance with the super-majority requirements of Nashville, Tenn., Metro. Charter § 18.02. The court vacated and remanded to determine whether the ordinance was enacted in compliance with Nashville, Tenn., Metro. Charter §§ 5.02, 18.02.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment striking down the zoning ordinance, remanded the matter to the trial court to determine whether the ordinance was enacted in compliance with the super-majority requirements of the local governmental charter. If it was enacted in compliance, then the trial court was directed to enter a judgment upholding the validity of the ordinance.

 

1634 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. McAllister v. Goode


Appeal No. 01A01-9510-CV-00452


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


968 S.W.2d 834; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 634



September 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied April 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SUMNER COUNTY AT GALLATIN, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE THOMAS GOODALL, JUDGE. No. 3846-C.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Sumner County at Gallatin, Tennessee, which declined to give effect to a side agreement between the father and the mother to reduce the father's child support obligation and determined that the father was in willful civil contempt and ordered him to pay an arrearage per plaintiff state's petition.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother had entered into a side agreement to reduce the father's child support payments. Neither party sought to modify the final divorce decree to reflect the side agreement. The state sought to hold the father in contempt for failing to pay the support required by the divorce decree. The trial court found him in contempt, ordered him to pay the arrearage, and declined to consider reducing the child support because the father had not filed a petition seeking such reduction. The trial court then denied the father's subsequent petition to reduce the amount. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the side agreement was not legally enforceable as the parties could not alter or amend the child support order by private agreement. The court found that the father was entitled to a prospective reduction of child support where his current obligation was 15 percent higher than the amount required by guidelines unless he was voluntarily underemployed. The court found that the parties entered into the side agreement in good faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the father owed the arrearage. The court reversed the trial court's finding that the father was in willful civil contempt and remanded the case for further proceedings to set the prospective child support.

Laney v. Campbell


Appeal No. 01A01-9703-CH-00142


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 498



July 18, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL L. McCOY, CHANCELLOR. No. 96-1282-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged a judgment from the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, which denied the prisoner's request for a declaratory judgment stating that the prisoner was entitled to earn retroactive prisoner sentence reduction credits for the time he was on death row.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was sentenced to death for the first degree murder of a grocer. At the time the prisoner was incarcerated, he was ineligible to earn sentence credits because he had been convicted of a Class-X offense. The prisoner was later allowed to participate in the educational program, so long as he signed a written waiver stating that he understood that his death sentence prevented him from earning sentence reduction credits. Eleven years later, the prisoner's death sentence was vacated by a criminal court, and he was resentenced to life imprisonment. The prisoner alleged that he was entitled to retroactive credits for the time he had been on death row. In affirming the trial court's judgment that denied relief to the prisoner, the court ruled that appellee prison warden did not abuse his discretion by declining to award the prisoner sentence credits for his activities while he was on death row. He was not constitutionally entitled to such credits, and such denial did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the federal and state constitutions. Those Clauses prevented the enactment of laws that increased criminal punishments beyond those prescribed when a crime was committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Dean v. Campbell


C.A. No. 02A01-9704-CV-00077


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 495



July 17, 1997, OPINION FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 11, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 558.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Circuit Court of Lauderdale County at Ripley. Honorable Joseph H. Walker, Judge. No. 4881.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of the dismissal of his complaint by the Circuit Court of Lauderdale County at Ripley (Tennessee) that alleged that defendants, the Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Corrections and others, improperly took the inmate's personal items, including a prayer rug, in violation of his civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was in the custody of the Tennessee Department of Corrections when he was transferred to different facilities. During the transfers several items of his personal property was missing, including a prayer rug. When he reported the loss, the Commissioner told the inmate that the rug was to be of a certain size, have a fire retardant label, and have a nonskid back. The inmate alleged that prayer rugs were not made with such a label or a nonskid back. He then brought an action against defendant for a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb et seq. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the claim, and the court affirmed that judgment. The court held that because the inmate failed to show that the prayer tug was essential or a central tenant to the practice of his religion, the reasonable restrictions placed of their use did not violate the inmate's constitutional rights. Moreover, neither the State nor its officials were "persons" within the meaning of § 1983. Finally the court noted that the U.S. Supreme Court had declared the Act unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of dismissal and taxed the costs of the appeal to the inmate.

 

1637 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Reynolds


Appeal No. 01A01-9510-CH-00484


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 462



July 2, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY, AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR. No. 92-2644-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from a judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County, at Nashville (Tennessee), which granted defendant Tennessee Department of Correction summary judgment in his action over the calculation of his sentence reduction credits.


OVERVIEW: This case was previously appealed and remanded. It concerned the way in which the Department of Correction calculated the inmate's good conduct sentence credits. The Department offered different probationary parole dates in affidavits and did not explain the differences between them and why their dates were different than the dates in the earlier proceeding. The court rejected the inmate's argument that the various good conduct credit statutes were applied in an ex post facto way. Including the inmate in new sentence credit programs under Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-229, -230 did not increase his punishment. The inmate provided the trial court with his own calculations. The Department filed affidavits containing the results of its calculations without the calculations themselves. The court found this filing inadequate because it did not enable the court to determine how the Department arrived at its figure. There were too many variables in the calculation of the sentence credits to accept the results of the Department's calculations on their face. The concern was underscored by the fact that the Department's and the inmate's calculations produced different and unexplained results.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment dismissing the inmate's ex post facto claims and vacated the remaining portions of the summary judgment. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings without prejudice to the parties submitting proper evidence and records demonstrating the proper calculation and application of all applicable credits to the inmate's sentence.
