Jaami v. Conley


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9609-CH-00425


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


958 S.W.2d 123; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 420



June 11, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FORM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ELLEN HOBBS LYLE, CHANCELLOR. No. 95-3539-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed a judgment from the Chancery Court of Davidson County and Nashville, Tennessee, which dismissed his petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, his warden and the Department of Correction, to change his security classification so that he could be transferred to a minimum security annex or to a community corrections center.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of committing a rape while on parole from a conviction for another sexual offense. When the prisoner was sentenced, the Department apparently had a policy that allowed all inmates to be considered for minimum custody classification if they were within 10 years of their earliest release date and met certain other conditions. However, a new policy was implemented that did not permit the transfer of sex offenders to minimum custody until they were within 10 years of the expiration of their sentences. The prisoner sought a writ of mandamus to compel the Department to change his security classification, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the Department's new policy did not constitute forbidden ex post facto punishment because the length of the prisoner's sentence was unchanged by the new policy. The court also found that the policy did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. Treating prisoners differently based on their offenses did not violate the Equal Protection Clause where the treatment was related to a legitimate state interest of protecting the public from sexual offenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Mirage Casino-Hotel v. Pearsall


Appeal No. 02A01-9608-CV-00198


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 367



May 27, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE KAY S. ROBILIO, JUDGE. Shelby Circuit No. 74546 T.D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant gambler appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which granted plaintiff casino's motion to enforce a foreign money judgment obtained after several checks that the gambler executed and made payable to the casino were dishonored.


OVERVIEW: The gambler wrote several checks at the casino's establishment in Nevada to purchase game chips. After the checks were dishonored, the casino obtained a money judgment against the gambler in Nevada. The casino then filed a motion in a Tennessee trial court to enforce the Nevada judgment. The trial court granted the motion, and the gambler appealed. The court affirmed. The constitutional mandate of the Full Faith and Credit Clause of the United States Constitution required credit to be given to a money judgment rendered on a civil cause of action in another state, even though the forum would have been under no duty to entertain the suit on which the judgment was founded. Where an action was brought on a judgment rendered by a court of a sister state, the Full Faith and Credit Clause prohibited an inquiry into the merits of the original cause of action. The court further found that none of the recognized exceptions to the application of the Full Faith and Credit Clause were present here.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the casino's motion to enforce a foreign money judgment was affirmed.

Overton v. Olmstead (In re Estate of Overton)


03A01-9701-PB-00025


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 345



May 21, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] SCOTT COUNTY. HON. JAMES L. COTTON, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, children and next of kin of the deceased, sought review of a judgment of the General Sessions Court, Probate Division for Scott County (Tennessee) which first denied their motion to dismiss the petition for probate filed by appellee sibling of the children. The trial judge thereafter found that it was appropriate for the estate to be probated and granted letters of administration to a licensed attorney.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died in 1980, and no petition seeking to administer his estate was filed until October 17, 1996, some two weeks after his widow's death. The trial court overruled appellants' motion to dismiss. Appellants argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-1-110(4) was in full force and effect from the date of the decedent's death until repealed some 13 years later and that it would be an unconstitutional application of the repealing statute to hold it invalid under the facts of the case. The court found that a probate proceeding was a unique one and for the most part unadversarial. For that reason the court declined to equate a daughter's right not to have her father's estate probated with the right of a wrongdoer not to be sued. The suit was also not barred by the catchall provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-3-110(3). The court found that the issue of letters to administer a decedent's estate was a unique proceeding to be distinguished from the types of adversarial causes of actions contemplated by § 28-3-110. Also, the legislature did not repeal the provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-1-110(4) so the exact statutory period of Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-3-110(3) would become effective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause so that the estate could be fully administered.

Memphis Publ. Co. v. Tennessee Petroleum Underground Storage Tank Bd.


C. A. NO. 01A01-9607-CH-00300


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 316



May 9, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville. Honorable Irvin H. Kilcrease, Chancellor. Docket No. 92-1435-I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Tennessee Petroleum Underground Storage Tank (TPUST) Board challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee) that entered a judgment declaring that appellee company was eligible for reimbursement from the TPUST fund (fund) for remediation expenses incurred as a result of a release from its underground storage tank that occurred prior to the enactment of the TPUST Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The court held that the Act was intended to cover fund reimbursement requests for all releases regardless of date. Upon remand, the trial court held the court's decision was "law of the case," and entered a judgment declaring that the company was eligible for reimbursement from the fund for remediation expenses incurred as a result of a release from its underground storage tank that occurred prior to the Act's enactment. The court affirmed, concluding that the supreme court's denial of the board's permission to appeal by concurring with the results only did not preclude the decision from becoming the law of the case because the disposition simply precluded publication of the opinion. The law of the case doctrine applied even though the constitutional issues were decided by implication because it was clear that the issues were indeed decided where failure to decide them would have rendered the prior decision meaningless and resulted in an incomplete resolution of the issues before the court. The cause was remanded with directions to remand to the board for a determination regarding the reasonableness and necessity of the company's claimed expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with costs, the judgment that declared that the company was eligible for reimbursement from the fund for remediation expenses incurred as a result of a release from its underground storage tank that occurred prior to the enactment of the Act. The action was remanded.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner appealed an order from the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, which denied his petition for declaratory judgment that the recalculation of his parole date by defendant Tennessee Department of Correction pursuant to Tenn. Two years later, the prisoner was taken before a grand jury where he was convicted pursuant to Tenn. The court affirmed the dismissal and imposed costs on the prisoner.

Profill Dev. v. Dills


C. A. NO. 01A01-9607-CH-00326


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


960 S.W.2d 17; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 288



April 25, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville. Honorable Robert S. Brandt, Chancellor. No. 95-1748-III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landfill operator challenged a decision from the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to appellees, Tennessee Department of Environment and Conservation, its Commissioner, and intervenor, on some claims in appellant's declaratory action and entered judgment at trial on the remaining claims that Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-211-701 et seq. (1989) (Part Seven) did not apply to him and was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant applied for a permit to construct and to operate a landfill in the county. Under Part Seven, local governments were permitted to approve or disapprove landfill proposals. The Tennessee Department of Environmental Conservation ceased review of appellant's application because the county opted-in to Part Seven. The agency denied appellant's request for a declaratory order regarding the validity and applicability of Part Seven and waived jurisdiction. Appellant filed a declaratory judgment action against appellees. The trial court, which disposed of the case by summary judgment and trial, found for appellees on all issues. The court held that Part Seven's expiration date was removed by amendment so that it did not expire when another statute was implemented. The court held that the Tennessee Solid Waste Disposal statutes were not preempted by federal acts because states were specifically granted the right to enact more stringent requirements. The court held that appellant did not enjoy a property interest or entitlement in his permit application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and the entry of judgment after trial to appellees in appellant's declaratory judgment action.

Wolf v. Sundquist


Appeal No. 01A01-9505-CV-00209


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


955 S.W.2d 626; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 278



April 23, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE HAMILTON V. GAYDEN, JR., JUDGE. No. 94C-4094.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prospective jurors appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, that found in favor of defendant state officials, and dismissed the jurors' declaratory judgment action, which alleged that excluding persons from serving on juries in capital cases because of their religious opposition to the death penalty violated the state constitution. The jurors also sought injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The jurors class action sought a declaration that in capital cases the exclusion of persons from serving on juries based upon their religious opposition to the death penalty violated Tenn. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 4, 6, and 8 and Tenn. Const. art. M, § 8. They also sought to enjoin the use of challenges for cause to exclude such prospective jurors. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the action. The court determined that the practice of excluding jurors whose religious principles prevented them from considering the death penalty regardless of the law and the evidence was not an unconstitutional religious test, did not violate the jurors' constitutionally protected freedom of religion, and did not unconstitutionally discriminate against the jurors. The court noted that the right to trial by jury secured by the state and federal constitutions necessarily contemplated that an unbiased and impartial jury. The jurors were properly excluded because they stated, in effect, that they were not impartial and unbiased. The public had a right to expect that juries in capital cases did not contain jurors who were unable or unwilling to follow the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in the juror's declaratory judgment class action against the state officials, which held that excluding persons from serving on juries in capital cases because of their religious opposition to the death penalty was not unconstitutional. The court remand the action to the trial court for whatever other proceedings may have been required.

Whitaker v. Whitaker


C.A. No. 02A01-9512-CH-00286


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


957 S.W.2d 834; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 266



April 22, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY. THE HONORABLE D. J. ALISSANDRATOS, CHANCELLOR. No. 24236-3.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed a decree of the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which granted a divorce to plaintiff wife and which awarded the wife custody of the parties' two children.


OVERVIEW: The wife sought a divorce on the ground that the husband engaged in inappropriate marital conduct. Based on the manner in which the husband practiced his religious beliefs, the wife was granted a divorce. The trial court's decree required the husband to enroll in a program of anger management, and the husband's visitation rights were conditioned upon the approval of a guardian ad litem. The decree also provided that before the husband could obtain visitation rights, a petition had to be filed by the guardian. Upon appeal, the trial court's decree was modified, and as modified it was affirmed. The court held that although a trial court had no authority to grant a divorce based on religious beliefs alone, it could grant a divorce based upon the manner in which the husband practiced his religion. The court ruled that it was improper for the trial court to condition the husband's visitation rights upon the guardian's approval; approval of visitation was a function of the trial court. The court also held that Tenn. Const. art. I, § 17 guaranteed that Tennessee's courts were to be open to all. Thus, the husband's right to petition the trial court could not be limited.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decree by holding that the approval of any request for visitation was a function of the trial court and not the guardian and by holding that the husband had the right to petition the trial court to obtain visitation rights. As modified, the trial court's decree was affirmed.

Newton v. Cox


C. A. NO. 02A01-9604-CH-00086


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


954 S.W.2d 746; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 229



April 7, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 275.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Chancery Court of Shelby County at Memphis. Honorable Joe C. Morris, Sp. Chancellor. No. 95025-3 R.D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client challenged a judgment from the Chancery Court of Shelby County at Memphis (Tennessee), which found in favor of the client in his action against defendant attorney to recover excess fees charged in a medical malpractice action. The trial court had reduced the award for the amount of the medical malpractice judgment awarded to the client's ex-wife. The client also challenged an order denying his claim for prejudgment interest.


OVERVIEW: The attorney represented the client in a medical malpractice action. Pursuant to the contingent fee arrangement, the attorney received 50 percent of the settlement. The client and his wife divorced, and she was given a portion of that award for her loss of consortium. The client instituted an action against the attorney, alleging that the contingency fee violated Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-120 (1980), which limited contingency fees to 33 1/3 percent. Following two appeals, the trial court awarded the client the excess fee but deducted one-fourth as the share awarded to the client's ex-wife. On appeal, the court modified and affirmed the judgment, holding that under the doctrine of unjust enrichment, the client was entitled to the full amount of the excess fees. The court found that the attorney would be unjustly enriched if he were permitted to retain the benefit of the ex-wife's portion of the excess fees. The court denied the client's claim for prejudgment interest, holding that although the attorney's fee was certain, it was unclear whether the dispute of his obligation was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court modified the award by permitting the client to recover the full amount of the excess fees charged by the attorney and affirmed the judgment as modified. The court affirmed the order denying the client prejudgment interest. The court awarded the client post-judgment interest.

Chattanooga Metro. Airport Auth. v. Thompson


C/A NO. 03A01-9610-CH-00319


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 209



March 24, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. HAMILTON COUNTY. HON. R. VANN OWENS, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant operator of licensed taxicabs appealed a judgment from the Chancery Court, Hamilton County (Tennessee) declaring Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1006 unconstitutional under Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8 in this declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiff airport authority.


OVERVIEW: The airport authority brought a declaratory judgment action seeking to have Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1006 declared unconstitutional. On appeal, the operator of licensed taxicabs contended that there was no justiciable controversy and that the trial court erred in declaring Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1006 unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1006 unconstitutional under Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. The trial court acted properly in resolving the dispute between the parties. An act which suspended the general law violated Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8 unless there was a reasonable or rational basis for the exclusion. The Tennessee Passenger Transportation Services Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1001 et seq., was "general" for the purposes of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8.There was no rational basis for the exemption provided in Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1006.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring a statute unconstitutional in this declaratory judgment action brought by the airport authority.

 

1648 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Winchester City Council


APPEAL NO. 01-A-01-9609-CV-00419


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 149



March 5, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FRANKLIN COUNTY AT WINCHESTER, TENNESSEE, THE HONORABLE J. CURTIS SMITH, JUDGE. Franklin Circuit No. 9745-CIV.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Franklin County at Winchester (Tennessee), which quashed a writ of certiorari suspending the decision of appellee, the Winchester City Council, allowing intervening petitioner applicant permission to sell fireworks within the city and denying appellant permission to do so.


OVERVIEW: Winchester, Tenn., Mun. Ord. 7-501, which was passed in 1983 and amended in 1996, prohibited the sale of fireworks within the city. Although the Council denied the request of appellant, who had previously sold fireworks within the City one year without permission, it granted permission to intervening petitioner, who had sold fireworks for 19 years on land that was annexed by the City in 1987, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208 as a preexisting nonconforming use. The court held that: (1) the trial court did not err in holding that the Council's actions in denying appellant a fireworks permit were neither arbitrary nor capricious because the ordinance did not contain any exceptions; (2) the trial court was without jurisdiction to determine whether the Council's decision as to intervening petitioner was an abuse of discretion because the constraints of the writ of certiorari limited the trial court's jurisdiction to the single issue of whether the Council's decision as to appellant exceeded the council's jurisdiction or whether the council acted illegally, fraudulently, or arbitrarily; and (3) the ordinance was not a zoning ordinance because it was in no way connected to the land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment insofar as it quashed the writ of certiorari and held that the Council's actions in denying a fireworks permit to appellant were neither arbitrary nor capricious, reversed the judgment insofar as it held that the Council did not abuse its discretion in allowing intervening petitioner a variance to sell fireworks and that the ordinance was a zoning ordinance, and remanded the matter.

 

1649 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Department of Human Servs. v. Hooper


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9605-CV-00231


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 139



February 28, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DICKSON COUNTY AT CHARLOTTE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ROBERT E. BURCH, JUDGE. No. 8015.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dickson County at Charlotte, Tennessee, which entered summary judgment establishing defendant's paternity as a matter of law based upon Tenn. Code Ann. § 24-7-112(b)(2)(B), and ordered defendant to make child support payments, in a paternity action filed by plaintiff state, as assignee of the mother of a minor child.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an action to obtain a judgment of paternity and support payments against defendant. A DNA test established a 99.71 percent of probability of defendant's paternity of the child. Although defendant contested the action, the trial court granted the state's summary judgment motion based on the statute which, among other things, established a conclusive, irrebutable presumption of paternity in cases in which scientific tests showed the statistical probability of an individual's paternity to be 99 percent or greater. On appeal, the court held that the statute violated defendant's right to due process of law under the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 8, because both the child and a defendant in a paternity action had a compelling interest in the accuracy of a paternity determination, which outweighed the state's interest in easing its administrative burden; and the irrebutable presumption of paternity effectively denied a putative father a meaningful opportunity to be heard. The court concluded that the state's motion for summary judgment should have been denied and the matter should have been permitted to proceed to trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court to provide defendant the opportunity to rebut the presumption of paternity attached to a 99.71 percent probability of paternity.

Davis v. Sundquist


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9610-CH-00498


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


947 S.W.2d 155; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 130



February 26, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 13, 1997. Permission to Appeal Dismissed June 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE, THE HONORABLE ELLEN HOBBS LYLE, CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 95-1090-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates appealed an order from the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which granted the motion to dismiss that was filed by respondents, the governor and the attorney general, and dismissed the inmates' petition in which they sought a declaratory judgment finding Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-20-112 unconstitutional because it contravened Tenn. Const. art. 2, § 17.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were in the custody of the Tennessee Department of Corrections when they filed a petition, seeking a declaratory judgment finding that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-20-112 was unconstitutional because it encompassed more than one subject in contravention of Tenn. Const. art. 2, § 17. The governor and attorney general filed a motion to dismiss, which was granted. The inmates appealed, contending that the trial court should amend its judgment because the inmates had complied with Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-223. The court disagreed, holding that the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act provided that the inmates had not first sought a declaratory judgment from the controlling agency, that the court lacked jurisdiction to review an agency's actions through a declaratory judgment proceeding without the agency first addressing the inmates' issues, and that the judicial declaratory judgment action was premature because the inmates proceeded directly to judicial review without first seeking an administrative determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which had dismissed the inmates' petition for a declaratory judgment, and the cause was remanded for any further necessary proceedings.

Hilliard v. Hilliard


C. A. NO. 02A01-9609-CH-00230


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 105



February 12, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Weakley County at Dresden. Honorable William Michael Maloan, Chancellor. No. 13598.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of Weakley County at Dresden (Tennessee) that granted visitation rights to appellee, his son's maternal grandmother.


OVERVIEW: The father and appellee mother were divorced approximately one and a half years after the birth of their son. Temporary custody was awarded to the grandmother. Upon his petition for modification, the father was awarded custody of the child and the grandmother was granted visitation with the child every other weekend. On appeal the issue was whether the grandmother was entitled to visitation with child. Although the grandmother had custody, her visitation was first ordered in the order that was the subject of the appeal, the change of custody from her to the father. Once the father was granted custody, he had the right to decide whether the grandmother could have visitation. The statement of the evidence on the hearing on the father's petition to modify the decree to award him sole custody of the child indicated that the father and the grandmother had some disagreements over his visitation with the child as well as payment of child support. The record did not indicate whether the trial court made any determination as to whether a denial of visitation to the grandmother with the child would have resulted in a substantial danger of harm to him.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for a threshold determination of whether cessation of the relationship between the child and his maternal grandmother presented a substantial danger of harm to the child and, if such harm was found, to determine whether visitation with the maternal grandmother was in the child's best interest.

Helms v. Greene


Appeal No. 01A01-9505-CH-00194


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 61



January 31, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 92-3515-I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed from the order of the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which reviewed the actions of defendant Commissioner of Safety and upheld the constitutionality of the forfeiture statutes and the validity of a summary forfeiture proceeding in which the police mailed notice of the proceeding to the owner's last known address although they knew he had moved.


OVERVIEW: A criminal court judge entered an ex parte order that directed a bank to freeze the owner's accounts because there was probable cause to believe that the money was traceable to illegal drug trafficking. The police mailed notices of a forfeiture proceeding under Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-451(a)(6)(A) (1996) to the owner's address at the time of arrest although he had moved. A postal forwarding order was in effect and the owner received one of two notices. On appeal, the court held that due process required authorities to exert reasonable efforts to provide notice to persons who might have an interest in the property and the method of notice must be reasonably calculated to appraise all interested persons of the proceeding in order to enable them to present their claims or objections. The court found that the use of the old address alone would not have been sufficient, but the change of address form supported the conclusion that the method was reasonable. The court held that there was no requirement of actual delivery since many persons avoided acceptance of certified mail and noted that the evidence here indicated that the owner had purposely attempted to avoid notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that upheld the constitutional sufficiency of the notice of forfeiture proceedings mailed to the owner of seized bank accounts.

Sanford v. Metropolitan Gov't


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9606-CV-00251


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 46



January 24, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected February 7, 1997. Petition to Rehear Granted February 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 121.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE HAMILTON GAYDEN, JUDGE. Davidson Circuit No. 93C-260.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a woman injured in a shootout by appellee police officers, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, which dismissed two of the officers and her constitutional deprivation claim, ordered appellee, the metropolitan government of Nashville and Davidson County (metro), to pay only 20 percent of her discretionary costs, and allocated fault against her.


OVERVIEW: When shots were fired by the officers during a disturbance at a neighbor's home, the woman was injured when a bullet struck her in the face. The woman brought an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging constitutional violations, as well as negligence. The trial court found that the reckless, now deceased, neighbor was more at fault and the fault should be apportioned to the officers and the woman. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that: (1) the woman was not negligent for looking at the disturbance from her storm door because that it was reasonable for a person to watch a person being arrested for disturbing the peace; (2) the actions of the neighbor were too remote to require the allocation of 75 percent of the fault because no injuries would have resulted but for the negligent actions of the officers who improperly entered a home with their guns drawn, without investigating the circumstances or announcing their presence, in violation of the metro guidelines; and (3) the metro violated the woman's Fourteenth Amendment due process rights because it failed to properly train the officers, which was customary, and such failure caused her injuries.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court dismissing the woman's constitutional claim and the officers and assessing fault. The cause was remanded for further necessary proceedings including the proper assessment of damages and a hearing on the merits of the § 1983 claim.

Jordan v. Tenn. Bd. of Paroles


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9607-CH-00347


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 27



January 15, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 95-3201-III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee Tennessee Board of Paroles and dismissed the inmate's petition for a writ of certiorari that challenged the Board's refusal to grant him parole.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pleaded guilty to aggravated rape, armed robbery, and second degree murder. His request for parole was denied. The Board cited high risk and the seriousness of his offenses as its reasons for the decline of the inmate's request for parole. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of certiorari, and the chancery court's dismissed the inmate's petition on the basis that it was not filed within the jurisdictional time limit that was required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-9-102. The court affirmed the chancery court's judgment because § 27-9-102 required that a petition for a writ of certiorari was to filed within 60 days of the entry of the Board's decision. The time limit did not begin to run until the Board's decision became final. The scope of a writ of certiorari was limited to an inquiry of whether the Board exceeded its jurisdiction of if it acted illegally, fraudulently, or arbitrarily. Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-503 provided that the Board was allowed to take into account the seriousness of the inmate's crimes in making a parole determination. The Board was not required to make a detailed statement of the Board's reasons for denying the inmate's request for parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's judgment and remanded the case to the chancery court.

Thompson v. Young (In re Estate of Thompson)


03A01-9602-PB-00075


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


952 S.W.2d 429; 1997 Tenn. App. LEXIS 2



January 6, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] BLOUNT COUNTY. HON. HUGH E. DeLOZIER, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant son sought review of an order of the Circuit Court (Tennessee), which dismissed the son's petition to remove the executors of his father's estate and awarded damages in favor of appellee executors.


OVERVIEW: The probate court sua sponte ordered the clerk to certify the son's petition to the circuit court for further proceedings. The circuit court dismissed the son's petition to remove the executors of his father 's estate on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction to grant the relief requested. On appeal, the court vacated the dismissal. The court found that the executors conceded that the probate court had authority to hear the issues raised in the instant dispute, but that it did not have jurisdiction to empanel a jury or hear other matters. The court reasoned that because the probate court had jurisdiction over certain issues raised in the instant case, the court was entitled to resolve all issues ancillary thereto. The court noted that the probate court chancellor had discretion to refuse a jury trial should the court determine that the resolution of factual issues involved complicated accounting.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the dismissal of the son's petition to remove the executors and remanded.

Smith v. Schneider


C. A. NO. 02A01-9608-CH-00193


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 783



December 11, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Henderson County at Lexington. Honorable Joe C. Morris, Chancellor. Henderson County Chancery Court No. 7166.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandparents challenged a decision of the Chancery Court, of Henderson County at Lexington (Tennessee), which denied their petition seeking visitation rights with their grandson.


OVERVIEW: The paternal grandparents sought visitation rights to their grandchild. They claimed that they visited weekly with the child until appellee mother said they couldn't see the child anymore. The trial court denied their petition for visitation rights. On appeal, the grandparents claimed that the test to be applied in determining whether they were entitled to visitation rights was the best interest of the child standard. The court affirmed the denial of visitation rights and held that parents possessed a constitutional right of privacy in parenting decisions that was not subject to interference from the State absent a showing of substantial harm to a child's welfare. Further, without a showing of substantial harm to the child, a court could not constitutionally impose its own notions of the best interest of the child. In the instant case, although the court appreciated the desires of the grandparents to continue their relationship with the child, there was no evidence of substantial harm to the child and, therefore, no compelling state interest to justify state interference with the right of the mother to prevent contact between the child and the grandparents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the grandparents' petition seeking visitation rights with their grandson.

AT&T Communs. v. Greer


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9512-BC-00556


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 776



December 6, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE TENNESSEE PUBLIC SERVICE COMMISSION FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 95-02615.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national communications company sought review of a decision by the Tennessee Public Service Commission for Davidson County (TPSC) implementing a price regulation plan for a local telephone company. The communications company contended that the TPSC failed to follow proper standards and procedures when it addressed the application of the local company to elect a price regulation plan pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 65-5-209.


OVERVIEW: A communications company challenged the TPSC's implementation of a price regulation plan for a local telephone company. The communications company contended that the TPSC failed to follow proper procedures when it addressed the application of the local company to elect a price regulation plan. The communications company also contended that Tenn. Code Ann. § 65-5-209(c) deprived it of its due process right to be heard as to the justness and reasonableness of rates to which its was to be subject. The court dismissed the communication company's appeal for lack of jurisdiction and concluded that ratepayers, such as the communications company, had no due process rights to the charging of particular rates. As such, the company was forbidden from challenging the legislation at issue because the company could object to the charging of a particular rate. The court found that the communications company had failed to set forth any statutory or constitutional provisions which required the TPSC to provide the company with an opportunity to be heard before the implementation of the price regulation, thus, the proceeding was not a contested case as defined in Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-103(b).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the national communications company's appeal challenging the TPSC's implementation of a price regulation plan for a local telephone company. The court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction and remanded the cause to the Tennessee Regulatory Authority for any further necessary proceedings.

Jones v. Greene


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9505-CH-00187


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


946 S.W.2d 817; 1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 772



December 4, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 93-3580-I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of a judgment of the chancery court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which upheld the Tennessee forfeiture statutes and which upheld appellee Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Safety's order for the forfeiture of money seized during the search of a house for illegal drugs.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the money seized was subject to forfeiture under Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-451(a)(6)(A). Tenn. Const. art. I, § 6, which guaranteed the right to a trial by jury, did not apply to claims or proceedings established after the adoption of the Tennessee Constitution and did not limit the General Assembly's power to establish new claims and remedies that did not require a trial by jury. Therefore, Tennessee's administrative forfeiture statutes, which did not provide for a jury trial, did not run afoul of Tenn. Const. art. I, § 6. The court also held that the forfeiture proceedings did not violate the claimant's due process rights because neither the commissioner nor his department could have benefited from the forfeiture proceeding since the money at issue was seized by a local law enforcement agency and because the 41 month delay between the seizure of the money and the forfeiture hearing did not undermine his ability to present his claim. The claimant's inability to describe the money accurately and to prove that he had the means to accumulate the money supported the commissioner's decision that the claimant had not proved that the seized money was his.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment concerning the forfeiture of money.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals sought review of a judgment of the Humphrey County Chancery Court of Waverly, Tennessee, which dismissed the individuals' action against defendants, county and board of commissioners (board), in which the individuals sought to challenge the board's denial of the individuals' application for a permit to construct a landfill.


OVERVIEW: The individuals filed suit contending that the board's denial of their permit application was arbitrary and illegal. The trial court dismissed the complaint, holding that the board did not act arbitrarily or illegally in denying the application and that there was sufficient evidence to support the board's decision to disapprove the proposed location of the landfill. The individuals appealed on numerous grounds. The court affirmed, first holding that the board had the authority under the Local Approval Law, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 68-701-708, to pass a resolution accepting the authority to approve or disapprove the application. The court also held that the board's decision was supported by substantial evidence and was therefore not arbitrary, capricious, or illegal. Finally, the court sustained the constitutionality of the Local Approval Law and the board's decision thereunder.

State ex rel. Commissioner ex rel. Said Dep't

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a condemnation proceeding instituted by plaintiff State, defendant landowners sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Hardeman County (Tennessee), which awarded $ 55,000 to the landowners as compensation for the taking of a portion of the landowners' property. The landowners challenged the amount of the compensation awarded.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an order of the trial court, the State was given legal possession of 1.42 acres of a 2.27-acre tract of land owned by the landowners. During the trial held to determine the sufficiency of compensation, both parties introduced expert testimony as to the value of the land taken and incidental damages to the remaining property. In re Crawford


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9602-CV-00070


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 669



October 18, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE THOMAS W. BROTHERS, JUDGE. No. 94C-2407.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a mother and her husband, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee) denying their motion to dismiss and granting petitioner putative father's petition for legitimation. Respondents argued that the trial court erred in denying the motion to dismiss and entering judgment for the putative father without the mother's consent, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-202 (Supp. 1995).


OVERVIEW: The mother was married when the putative father claimed that they had an affair. The putative father filed a petition for legitimation. The trial court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-202 (Supp. 1995) was constitutional on its face under the state and federal constitution. However, the mother's erratic relationship with her husband was a mockery of lawful wedlock and that the putative father was allowed to file his petition for legitimation. The court reversed because the putative father lacked standing to bring the legitimation action. The statute only allowed the petition to be filed as to children not born in wedlock. The general assembly intended the statute to apply to the children of unmarried women. The restrictive interpretation was necessary to preserve the integrity of families and the same protections did not extend to putative fathers. The statute did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment when the putative father had no common-law right to legitimate the child. It did not violate the putative father's right to equal protection when any constitutionally cognizable interest the putative father had was outweighed by the competing public interest of preserving the family.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the putative father's petition to legitimate the minor child. It remanded the case to the trial court.

Smith v. Smith


C. A. NO. 03A01-9603-CV-00078


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 655



October 11, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court of Knox County at Knoxville, Div. IV. Honorable Bill Swann, Judge. No. 65563.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Knox County at Knoxville (Tennessee), which found the father guilty of two counts of criminal contempt and entered judgment for appellee mother by suspending the father's visitation rights with his child.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father were divorced. Custody of the minor child was awarded to the mother. The father agreed to not subject the child to cigarette smoke during visitation. The father was also prohibited from being around the mother's residence. The mother testified that she witnessed the father around her house on a certain date. Moreover, she alleged that the child smelled like smoke after returning from visitation. The child also suffered a cigarette burn on her hand during a visit with her father. The trial court found the father guilty of criminal contempt and suspended his visitations. In affirming, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding of contempt beyond a reasonable doubt. Therefore, the court was not permitted to disturb the final judgment of the trial court. Moreover, the father was not able to challenge the validity of the no-smoking rule because he did not object at the trial court level. Finally, the court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in suspending the father's visitation rights. The father's conduct clearly jeopardized the child's physical condition by subjecting her to cigarette smoke.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the father's convictions. The court also affirmed the suspension of his visitation rights.

 

1664 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Malik v. Malik


Appeal No. 02A01-9604-CH-00070


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 627



October 3, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE NEAL SMALL, CHANCELLOR. Shelby Chancery No. 21988-1 R.D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of a decision of the Chancery Court of Shelby County at Memphis (Tennessee), which ordered him to cash out and/or borrow against his pension and retirement funds in order to satisfy the chancery court's prior distribution of marital property to appellee former wife.


OVERVIEW: The chancery court entered a final decree awarding the wife rehabilitative alimony, a portion of the parties' equity in the marital residence, and amounts contained in husband's retirement and pension accounts. After the trial court ruled in favor of the wife, the husband appealed. The husband contended on appeal that the trial court erred in ordering him to cash out the funds in his two annuity accounts because the accounts were part of his optional retirement program and as such, were exempt from execution or any other process pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-5-501, 8-36-111, and 26-2-104. The husband conceded that the pension funds were martial assets. The wife responded that the order was directed solely to husband, rather than to the state or its agencies. The court agreed and noted that Tenn. Code Ann. § 26-2-104(a) prohibited the "execution, attachment, or garnishment" of state pension funds. However, the trial court ordered husband to cash out and/or borrow against the funds. Therefore, the funds were not subject to "execution, attachment, or garnishment," or any other judicial process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1665 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Evans v. Steelman


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9511-JV-00508


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 625



October 2, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected October 4, 1996. As Corrected November 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE JUVENILE COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ANDREW J. SHOOKHOFF, JUDGE. No. 9419-13267.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the order of the Juvenile Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition to legitimate a child born to appellee mother.


OVERVIEW: The father, who had a child with a woman who was married to another man, brought a petition to legitimate the child. The juvenile court dismissed his petition finding that he did not have standing to bring the action. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that when the legislature amended Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-202 in 1992, and again in 1994, it did not change the language of the statute to include children born to married women. The court found that the statute was not defective on due process grounds because it created rights rather than taking them away. The court determined that the father's equal protection rights were not violated by the state giving the right to legitimate a child to a man who fathers a baby by an unmarried woman while denying that right to men whose children were the product of a liaison with a married woman. The court found that a man seeking to legitimate a child born to a married woman was in a fundamentally different position from a man seeking to legitimate a child born to an unmarried woman. The court found that the state's interest in preserving the family justified the state's decision to give the right of legitimation to one and not the other.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court's dismissal of the father's action to legitimate the child.

 

1666 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Young v. Young


Appeal No. 02A01-9506-GS-00133


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 596



September 25, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE GENERAL SESSIONS COURT OF HARDIN COUNTY, AT SAVANNAH, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE MAX SEATON, JUDGE. Hardin General Sessions No. 3469.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife appealed a judgment from the General Sessions Court of Hardin County, at Savannah (Tennessee), which denied her amended motion to set aside a final decree of divorce. The divorce decree gave custody of the parties minor child to plaintiff husband, required the wife to pay child support to the husband, awarded the marital property to the husband except for the wife's car, and required the wife to pay all the marital debts.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed an amended complaint in which he alleged that the wife had left the state and that, as a nonresident, process should be served by publication. Notice was published pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 21-1-204 in a local paper. No other attempts at service of process were made. The husband knew the address and phone number of the wife's parents, but he made no attempt to contact them to let the wife know of the impending divorce proceedings. A default judgment was entered against the wife. On appeal, the wife argued that the decree was void because the method of serving process upon her violated her rights to due process. The court found that the husband verbally informed the wife that he had obtained a restraining order and was going to file for divorce. However, in the context of a relationship in which there was active mistrust between the parties, the verbal statement was not sufficient to relieve the husband of his obligation to make a reasonable effort to ascertain the wife's whereabouts and serve notice on her. Because the husband failed to take appropriate measures to give the wife notice of the divorce proceedings, the divorce decree was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court, set aside the divorce decree and the award of custody of the minor child, and remanded the case to consider the divorce and the appropriate forum for custody determination.

 

1667 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Newman v. Phillips


C/A NO. 03A01-9602-CV-00056


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 526



August 27, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CIRCUIT COURT. McMINN COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN B. HAGLER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, COMPLAINT DISMISSED, REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the Circuit Court of McMinn County (Tennessee), which found visitation to be in the best interests of the mother's minor child and, acting pursuant to the Grandparents' Visitation Act (GVA), awarded visitation to appellees, the maternal grandparents, in the grandparents' petition for visitation rights.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents filed a petition seeking visitation with their minor granddaughter. The mother, who had been awarded full custody in her divorce suit, opposed the petition. The mother remarried. Her new husband was not a party to the action. The petition did not allege that the mother was an unfit parent or that she had engaged in any parental misconduct. The trial court, after a non-jury hearing, found visitation to be in the child's best interests, and, acting under the GVA, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-302, awarded visitation. On appeal, the mother raised the issue of whether the grant of visitation rights to her parents, made over her objection and with no showing of injury to the child or parental unfitness, violated her right to privacy under the Tennessee Constitution. In reversing and remanding, the court held that, absent a finding of substantial harm to the child, the state could not constitutionally interfere with a parent's right to make child-rearing decisions by ordering grandparents' visitation against a parent's wishes. Thus, the trial court erred in ordering visitation over the mother's objection when no allegations of harm to the child were made in the present case.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the original petition was dismissed with costs below being assessed to the grandparents. The court also assessed the costs on appeal to the grandparents. The case was remanded to the trial court for the collection of the costs below, pursuant to applicable law.

Hoover, Inc. v. Rutherford County


Appeal No. No. 01A01-9601-CH-00004


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 433



July 26, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF RUTHERFORD COUNTY AT MURFREESBORO, TENNESSEE. HONORABLE ROBERT E. CORLEW III, CHANCELLOR. Rutherford Chancery No. 93CV-924.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff stone quarry operator appealed a summary judgment of the Chancery Court of Rutherford County at Murfreesboro (Tennessee) dismissing its suit against defendants, a county, the county clerk, and the Tennessee Attorney General, seeking refund of mineral severance taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The operator sought to recover taxes paid to the county under protest on stone removed from the quarry from March 8, 1993, to May 31, 1993, on the ground that the enabling legislation for the tax was unconstitutional under Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. Relying on a decision holding that exclusion of counties from a Tennessee severance tax law based on population violated Tenn. Const. Art. I, § 8 and Tenn. Const. Art. XI, § 8, the operator argued that 1983 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 111, authorizing the collection of severance tax by the county was unconstitutional. The court found that the operator's argument that the decision invalidated the county's severance tax collections between March 8, 1993, and May 31, 1993, was misplaced. That decision did not hold that the Tennessee General Assembly could not enact a private act permitting a particular county to levy a local tax for local purposes. There could not be a successful challenge of the validity of the tax authorized by the General Assembly and levied by the county commission for the period in question. Constitutional requirements of uniformity in taxation did not apply to special legislation authorizing counties to levy taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1669 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Vineyard v. Hood (In re Hood)


C/A NO. 03A01-9508-JV-00296


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


930 S.W.2d 575; 1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 348



June 10, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] JUVENILE COURT. BLOUNT COUNTY. HONORABLE WILLIAM TERRY DENTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court, Blount County (Tennessee) granted a motion to dismiss filed by respondents, a mother and the maternal grandparents, in petitioner putative father's action to legitimate and establish a parent-child relationship with his alleged daughter. The putative father appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mother and maternal grandparents objected to the putative father's petition to establish a parent-child relationship with his alleged daughter under Tenn. Code. Ann. § 36-2-202(c). The statute provided that a putative father could not legitimate a child without the mother's consent. The state attorney general certified to the court his conclusion that the statute was unconstitutional to the extent that it allowed an unmarried woman to prevent a putative father from legitimating his alleged biological child. The court reversed the dismissal of the father's petition. The father was entitled to the custody, companionship, and care of his child and could not be deprived of those rights except by due process of law. The father had a constitutionally protected right to attempt to create a legal parent-child relationship with his natural daughter. The logical avenue through which he may accomplish this was by filing a petition to legitimate his child. The state could not authorize the mother to veto the legitimation process without demonstrating a compelling interest. However, the attorney general had acknowledged that the state failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment dismissing the putative father's action to establish the parent-child relations with his daughter and remanded for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

County of Shelby v. McWherter


C.A. No. 02A01-9601-CH-00015


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


936 S.W.2d 923; 1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 340



June 3, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY. THE HONORABLE FLOYD PEETE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Shelby Chancery No. 104609-2.



DISPOSITION: VACATED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the decision of the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-2-201(c) was unconstitutional. Intervenor county board of education was allowed to defend the provision's constitutionality.


OVERVIEW: The county brought an action against the state seeking an interpretation and declaration of the constitutionality of parts of the Educational Improvement Act of 1992, Title 49 of the Tennessee Code Annotated. The county argued that the statute violated the state constitution by abolishing the county superintendent position, that parts of the statute were unconstitutional, being void for vagueness. The court found that provisions of a county's home rule charter which conflicted with a general law of the state did not supersede the general law, regardless of the fact that those provisions related to matters in which the county acted in a governmental or political capacity. Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-2-201(c), pertaining to the eligibility of residents to serve on school boards in counties with populations of 700,000 or more, was general in form and effect, and was not unconstitutional, therefore, local approval of the provision was not required. The judgment holding Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-2-201(c) unconstitutional was vacated, but in other respects affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding the educational act in question unconstitutional was vacated.

OVERVIEW: The mother filed a petition to establish paternity. She named appellant as the natural father of her minor child. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination that appellant was the natural father of the mother's minor child.

Arnold v. Tennessee Bd. of Paroles


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9508-CH-00375


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 272



May 8, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR. No. 94-3223-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the order of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which granted the motion of appellee Tennessee Board of Paroles to dismiss the inmate's petition on the ground that it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6). The inmate sought review of the Board's denial of parole after the Board denied his request for a review hearing.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was granted a parole hearing. A hearing officer recommended denying his parole because of the seriousness of the offense for which he was being held and to continue with aftercare. The Board adopted the recommendation. Affirming, the court determined that the inmate had no right to judicial review of the correctness of the decision. The common law writ of certiorari allowed the review of the Board's actions to determine whether it exceeded its jurisdiction or acted illegally, fraudulently, or arbitrarily. The Board had discretion to decide whether new evidence entitled the inmate to an appeal hearing. The Board was authorized, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-503(b)(2), to deny parole if release would depreciate the seriousness of the offense. The Board was specifically exempted from the contested case provisions of the Administrative Procedures Act, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-106(c). The Open Meetings Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101, et seq., applied to the Board. The Board could adopt the recommendations of a hearing officer who held an open meeting, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-105(d), without holding another open meeting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for any further, necessary proceedings.

White v. Tennessee Dep't of Correction


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9602-CH-00071


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 273



May 8, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. No. 95-1598-III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a declaratory judgment action against respondent Tennessee Department of Correction in the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee). He asserted that the Department had failed to provide a timely hearing on a petition requesting a declaratory order concerning his sentence. The inmate appealed after the chancery court dismissed the action.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was incarcerated for several different crimes. A trial court imposed consecutive sentences upon him; the Department was unable to calculate the sentence expiration date for that conviction because it did not have any information about the prior sentence that was to run first. The inmate filed a petition pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-224 (1991) seeking a declaratory order from the Department; he sought a final determination of his sentence expiration date, his parole eligibility date, and his sentence reduction credits. The Department notified the inmate of the process that he had to follow in order to receive an order. Rather than supplying the Department with requested information and contacting his counselor as instructed, the inmate filed the action in the chancery court. The court agreed that the controversy was not ripe for adjudication because the inmate had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The Department was unable to issue the requested declaratory order because the inmate had not met the prerequisites for requesting a declaratory order nor had he documented his attempts to resolve his questions through the proper administrative channels.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court for further necessary proceedings. It assessed costs against the inmate.

State v. First Trust Money Servs.


Appeal No. 01A01-9508-CH-00344

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment of the Davidson County Chancery Court at Nashville (Tennessee) dismissing their counterclaim and approving issuance of subpoenas duces tecum under the Tennessee Financial Records Privacy Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 45-10-106(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the trial court erred in dismissing its counterclaim, because appellee's investigation order was arbitrary and capricious and interfered with their constitutionally protected property interest in their business, and because they had properly stated a cause of action for civil rights violations. The court found that appellee had met the burden of proof by showing that the records sought were relevant to a legitimate investigation of possible securities violations, that appellee did not already have the records, and that all administrative procedural requirements had been satisfied.

Hussey v. Hussey


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9504-PB-00181


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 219



April 10, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE PROBATE COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE MARIETTA M. SHIPLEY, JUDGE. No. 85D-1084.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the judgment by the Probate Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which denied the husband's petition to terminate or reduce the alimony which the husband was required to pay to appellee wife.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into an agreed divorce settlement. The husband received the parties' extensive commercial property holdings, and the wife received a lump sum payment and weekly, monthly and yearly payments in futuro. In addition, the husband agreed to pay the wife a sum every three years for a new car, to terminate if she should remarry. The wife remarried, and the husband filed a petition for termination or reduction of alimony. The wife argued that the weekly, monthly and yearly payments were contractual and did not terminate upon her remarriage. The trial court denied the petition. The husband appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-101(a)(2)(B), which terminated alimony in futuro upon the recipient's remarriage did not apply, because the agreement to make the periodic payments to the wife was contractual and was to reimburse her for her share of the parties' property. The court held that although the husband's financial condition had been reduced, he had not shown a substantial change in circumstances and was still able to provide the payments to the wife.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied the husband's petition to terminate or reduce alimony payments to the wife.

In re S.M.


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9506-JV-00233


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 199



March 29, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE JUVENILE COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AT CLARKSVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE CAROL CATALANO, JUDGE. No. 57-29.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An 11 year-old child was removed from appellant parents' home after it was determined that his father had sexually abused him. Temporary custody was awarded to appellee Department of Human Services. Approximately two and one-half years later, the Juvenile Court for Montgomery County at Clarksville, Tennessee, terminated the parental rights of the parents pursuant to an amended version of Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-159. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that application of the amended version of § 37-1-159 violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws and unconstitutionally deprived them of a vested right to a de novo trial in circuit court. The parents also challenged the evidentiary support for the decision. The court affirmed. First, the court held that the parents were afforded a constitutionally adequate hearing in the juvenile court. The parents' reliance on the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws was misplaced because Tenn. Const. art. I, § 11, applied exclusively to criminal offenses. Second, the amended version of Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-159(a) did not curtail the parents' appellate rights nor did it come at such an advanced stage of the proceeding that it undermined their substantive rights. The amendment left intact the parents' right to appeal and did not unconstitutionally hinder their ability to present their case in the juvenile court or their ability to seek appellate review of the decision. Third, the evidence demonstrated clearly and convincingly that the child's physical safety and psychological maturation was best served by terminating the parental rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the termination of the parental rights of the parents.

Boone Vanderpool v. Boone


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9508-CH-00358


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 183



March 27, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF CHEATHAM COUNTY AT ASHLAND CITY, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ALLEN W. WALLACE, CHANCELLOR. No. 5583.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court of Cheatham County at Ashland City (Tennessee), which granted a petition for contempt by the mother of the visitation provisions of a divorce decree and for enforcement of petitioner grandmother's visitation rights, ordered the mother to pay the grandmother's attorney fees, and denied the mother's counter-petition to terminate the earlier visitation order.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the mother's divorce decree, the grandmother was granted visitation privileges in her home with her grandchild. After an incident when the father appeared at the grandmother's home while the child was there, the mother would not permit the child to go to the grandmother's house. The grandmother filed a petition for contempt and for enforcement of the ordered visitation. The mother filed a counter-petition for termination of the ordered visitation. The trial court granted the grandmother's petition, denied the mother's counter-petition, and ordered the mother to pay the grandmother's attorney fees. The mother appealed, and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that trial court did not err in holding the mother in contempt because she did not have the right to ignore a lawful court order or to unilaterally change that order. The trial court properly denied the mother's counter-petition because there was no material change of circumstance adequate to justify a change in the original visitation order. The court found that the award of attorney fees was improper because the statute authorizing punishment for contempt did not mention such a sanction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling which granted the grandmother's petition for contempt by the mother of the visitation provisions of a divorce decree and for enforcement of her visitation rights and denial of the mother's counter-petition to terminate the earlier visitation order. The court reversed the trial court's ruling which ordered the mother to pay the grandmother's attorney fees. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the mother.

Laidlaw Envtl. Servs. v. Metropolitan Bd. of Health


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9507-CH-00310


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


934 S.W.2d 40; 1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 161



March 13, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. No. 94-2747-III.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff waste disposal plant appealed from an order by the Chancery Court of Davidson County, Tennessee, which affirmed defendant the Metropolitan Board of Health for Nashville and Davidson County's reversal of the renewal of six permits previously issued for operation of the waste disposal plant. Defendant food services company and recycling organization also defended the action of the Board.


OVERVIEW: The board renewed six permits for the waste disposal plant's operation after entering into a settlement agreement in which the waste disposal plant agreed to make expensive improvements. The board later reversed the permit renewal, and the waste disposal plant appealed to the trial court, which affirmed. The court reversed and vacated the trial court's affirmance, holding that the reversal was arbitrary and capricious in light of the settlement agreement, which stated that so long as the waste disposal plant was proceeding with its improvements it would be deemed in compliance with the emission control ordinance of Nashville, Tenn. Metropolitan Code § 10.56.170. To abrogate the terms of the agreement before it could be carried out under its terms was not unjust and indecent. The court also held that § 10.56.170 was not unconstitutionally vague; there was no merit to the waste disposal plant's challenge of the application of Nashville, Tenn. Metropolitan Code § 10.56.040(A) to the facts of the case; and the board was authorized to consider the location and surrounding area of the source of pollution in exercising its powers, but the exercise of its powers must be reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the affirmance of the board's action without prejudice to other remedial actions. The court remanded the case to the trial court for entry and enforcement of a judgment in conformity with the court's opinion.
