Roddy v. Volunteer Medical Clinic


CA No. 03A01-9506-CV-00194


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


926 S.W.2d 572; 1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 110



February 26, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIRCUIT COURT. KNOX COUNTY. HON. WHEELER ROSENBALM, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, patient and her mother, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Knox County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, medical clinic and physician, in an action alleging medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The patient, a young pregnant girl, sought an abortion from the clinic. She moved suddenly during the procedure and a rupture occurred. The patient and her mother brought an action for medical malpractice, as well as for violation of a state act, which was found to be unconstitutional. The trial court granted the motion of the clinic and physician to dismiss the extraneous allegations in the complaint. After discovery, the clinic and physician then brought a motion for summary judgment alleging that they had performed all care in conformance with the recognized standards of acceptable medical practice. The trial court granted their motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision because the patient's appeal was based on the ground that she did not have the capacity to consent to the abortion, which constituted a battery rather than the alleged malpractice. Further, there was no allegation of relief sought. She never amended her complaint to allege failure of consent. The patient failed to rebut the presumption that she was a mature minor having the capacity to consent, and she presented no testimony that she suffered as a proximate cause of negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the clinic and the physician in the patient's action alleging medical malpractice.

Campbell v. Sundquist


C.A. No. 01A01-9507-CV-00321


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


926 S.W.2d 250; 1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 46



January 26, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended February 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WALTER C. KURTZ, JUDGE. No. 93C-1547.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, governor, attorney general, and district attorney general, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to appellee homosexuals. Appellees had sought a declaratory judgment, pursuant to the Declaratory Judgment Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-101 et seq. (1980), that § 39-13-510 of the Homosexual Practices Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-510 (1991), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee homosexuals challenged the constitutionality of § 39-13-510 of the Homosexual Practices Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-510 (1991), in the circuit court. Appellees sought a declaratory judgment, pursuant to the Declaratory Judgment Act (DJA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-101 et seq. (1980), that § 39-13-510 was unconstitutional. The circuit court granted summary judgment to appellees. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The court held that appellees had standing to maintain their action under the DJA, as appellees had a distinct interest in the Act that was not shared by the general public; private sexual activity between consenting adults of the same sex was protected by the state constitutional right to privacy; appellants, governor, attorney general, and district attorney general, had failed to show a compelling state interest sufficient to prohibit private sexual activity between consenting adults of the same sex; and that the Act was overbroad in that it prohibited behavior which was constitutionally protected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment to appellee homosexuals in appellees' constitutional challenge to the Homosexual Practices Act (Act). The court held in part that appellees had standing to maintain the action under the Declaratory Judgment Act and that the Act was overbroad in that it prohibited behavior that was constitutionally protected.

 

1681 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Smith


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9508-CH-00354


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 35



January 19, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF OVERTON COUNTY AT LIVINGSTON, TENNESSEE. HONORABLE VERNON NEAL, CHANCELLOR. No. 02-192.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED, DISMISSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother sought review of a judgment entered in the Chancery Court for Overton County (Tennessee) that regulated visitation of the respondent's two children with petitioners, the children's' paternal grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the trial court's order, requiring her and the adoptive father to submit to visitation with the deceased father's parents violated the parents' rights under Tenn. Const. art 1, § 8 and the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The court agreed with the mother and reversed and vacated the trial court's judgment. The court noted that Tenn. Code. Ann. § 36-6-301(a) precluded grandparent visitation with a child who had been adopted by any person other than a relative of the child or a stepparent of the child. The court noted that the state constitution protected the privacy interest of the parents in child rearing decisions so long as their decisions did not substantially endanger the welfare of their children. The court pointed out that the trial court could not engage in a best interest of the child analysis without first determining whether the parents had substantially endangered the welfare of the child. In this case, the deceased father's parents failed to show that the children were in danger of substantial harm, thus, the trial court's order violated the mother's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the trial court's judgment that required the mother to submit her minor children to visitation with the deceased father's parents and remanded for entry and enforcement of a judgment in conformity with the court's opinion.

Drozd v. Hermitage Villa Condos. Homeowners Ass'n


NO. 01A01-9408-CV-00366


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1996 Tenn. App. LEXIS 26



January 17, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTH CIRCUIT COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE THOMAS W. BROTHERS. No. 91C-189.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixth Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) held that the Tennessee Uniform Residential Landlord and Tenant Act (act) was constitutional, dismissed a portion of plaintiff injured person's complaint for personal injury and subsequently granted partial summary judgment for defendants, a homeowners association, a property management company, and intervenor State of Tennessee. The injured person appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first agreed to consider the injured person's argument that the act applied to the unique circumstances of the condominium at issue, notwithstanding that the specific issue had not been raised before the trial court, because the injured person had generally sought to apply the act at trial. The court then held that the act did not apply, despite the fact that many of the condominium units had never been sold by the developer, because the injured person had purchased her condominium unit and continued to own it. The court further held that the act, which distinguished between landlords and tenants on the one hand, and condominium owners and developers on the other hand, was constitutional, because there was a difference between the two relationships, in that a condominium unit owner's responsibilities with regard to the property was much greater than that of a tenant. The court also affirmed the trial court's holding that two municipal ordinances were not applicable to the premises in question, because the court could not take judicial notice of a municipal ordinance, and the injured person had failed to prove the applicability of the ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which dismissed a portion of the complaint for personal injury and granted summary judgment on another portion, and remanded the cause for trial upon the remaining issues.

Kentucky-Tennessee Clay Co. v. Huddleston


Appeal No. 01A01-9508-CH-00347


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


922 S.W.2d 539; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 835



December 29, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. No. 93-2669-III.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of Revenue for the State of Tennessee sought review of a decision of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which ruled in favor of plaintiff mining company in its action against the Commissioner for assessing mineral severance taxes against the mineral company pursuant to 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts 137.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner assessed mineral severance taxes against the mineral company pursuant to the Act. The mineral company brought an action against the Commissioner that alleged that the Act was repealed by Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-7-209 on the ground that the Act directly conflicted with Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-7-201 et seq. The trial court ruled in favor of the mineral company. On appeal ,the court reversed the trial court's decision and held that the mineral severance tax could properly be levied against the mineral company. The court ruled that the Act was constitutional and was not repealed by the general law. The court held that there was no manifest repugnance or irreconcilable conflict between the Act and § 67-7-201 et seq. because taxes could not be assessed under the private act when the counties in which the special school district was located levied taxes on the minerals. The court ruled that the legislature's intent in enacting the Act was to impose taxes only on those minerals that were not taxed under the general law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and held that the mineral severance tax could properly be levied against the mineral company.

Wyatt v. A-Best Prods. Co.


C/A NO. 03A01-9502-CV-00066


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


924 S.W.2d 98; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 830



December 28, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: 924 S.W.2d 98 at 107.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIRCUIT COURT. KNOX COUNTY. HONORABLE WHEELER A. ROSENBALM, JUDGE.

Original Opinion of November 30, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 770.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL OPINION MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured individuals and two of the amici curiae filed petitions for rehearing of the court's decision to affirm the order of the Circuit Court of Knox County (Tennessee), which granted appellees, manufacturers and distributors, their motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The individuals, in their petition for rehearing, argued that the court failed to take into account a recent decision of the Tennessee Supreme Court wherein the individuals also were the plaintiffs, just as in this action. They also argued that the court was incorrect in stating in its opinion that it was undisputed that none of appellees sold or distributed any asbestos-containing products relevant to this action within the effective date of the original enactment of the TPLA. The court held that the referred to Tennessee Supreme Court decision was not controlling in this case because its focus was on the issue of when a cause of action accrued, a concept that that was immaterial to the issue in this case, the expiration of the statute of repose. The court then concluded that it was incorrect when it stated that the parties were in agreement that all of appellees ceased to manufacture and distribute asbestos-containing products more than 10 years prior to July 1, 1978, the effective date of the TPLA. This was only correct as to one of appellees. Because the record was factually deficient as to the other appellees, this was fatal to their summary judgment motions.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petitions for rehearing as to all except one of appellees. The court modified its opinion and judgment so that it found and held that only one manufacturer, who did not manufacture and distribute asbestos-containing products more than 10 years prior to the effective date of the TPLA, was entitled to summary judgment. The court vacated the summary judgments as to the other appellees.

France v. Bradley


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9508-CH-00335


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


922 S.W.2d 118; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 811



December 15, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. No. 94-3278-III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee) dismissing his action against defendants, the Commissioner of Department of Correction, the Governor, the Attorney General, and the Department of Correction, that sought a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief to allow him to transfer to a place of confinement where he could earn sentence reduction credits.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to six years in the custody of the Tennessee Department of Correction. He requested the opportunity to serve the sentence in the Cocke County Jail where he could earn sentence reduction credits by engaging in work programs. The request was denied, and the inmate filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, alleging that his equal protection rights were violated by the unequal treatment in his ability to earn sentence reduction credits. The trial court found that the inmate had no constitutional right to receive the credits nor a constitutional right to serve his sentence at any particular place, and the trial court dismissed the action. The inmate appealed, and the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found that the inmate's complaint failed to state a claim for which relief could be granted. His demand for equal opportunity for sentence credits was inextricably included in the assignment to a place of incarceration. However, the inmate had no constitutional right to incarceration in a particular institution. Nor did he have a constitutional right to receive sentence credits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter.

 

1686 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Grashot v. Lawson


C.A. No. 02A01-9409-CV-00222


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 809



December 14, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ROBERT L. CHILDERS, JUDGE. No. 51398.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alleged injury victims appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) dismissing their personal injury action against defendant corporation. The trial court found that the action was barred by the one-year statute of limitations set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-3-104 (Supp. 1994).


OVERVIEW: The victims were injured in an accident involving a van owned by the corporation and brought an action against the driver and the corporation's owner. An amended complaint was filed adding the corporation as a defendant. The victims voluntarily dismissed the action and filed another action against all three defendants. The trial court dismissed the second action. On appeal, the court noted that if the amendment in the first action related back to the initial filing date under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 15.03, the voluntary dismissal of the action allowed the victims one year within which to institute a new action against the corporation and the second action was timely filed. For R. 15.03 to apply, it was essential for the corporation to have notice of the lawsuit within the statutory period. The corporation did not have such notice, and the court held that its notice of the accident was immaterial. The court also held that the doctrine of estoppel could not be invoked to preclude the corporation from asserting the statute of limitations as a defense. The court did not entertain the victims' argument that R. 15.03 violated equal protection, as the issue was not raised in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings, if necessary.

Wyatt v. A-Best Prods. Co.


C/A NO. 03A01-9502-CV-00066


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


924 S.W.2d 98; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 770; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,433



November 30, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified on Grant of Rehearing December 28, 1995; Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 830. Application for Permission to Appeal Denied May 28, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 371.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIRCUIT COURT. KNOX COUNTY. HONORABLE WHEELER A. ROSENBALM, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Knox County (Tennessee), which granted appellee manufacturers' motion for summary judgment in the injured's action to recover for asbestos related injuries and held that the injured's action was time-barred by the 10-year statute of repose found at Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-28-103(a), a part of the Tennessee Products Liability Act of 1978 (TPLA).


OVERVIEW: The injured worked as a carpenter and claimed employment-related exposure to products containing asbestos that were manufactured and/or sold by the manufacturers. It was undisputed that none of the manufacturers sold or distributed any asbestos-containing products within 10 years of the effective date of the original enactment of the TPLA. However, within one year of the date he discovered that he was suffering from an asbestos-related lung disease, he filed an action. The circuit court held that his action was time-barred. The court affirmed and held that the 10-year period established by § 29-28-103(a) was a statute of repose and thus, barred the injured's action on the date the TPLA became effective. Further, the asbestos exception could not be applied retroactively to revive the injured's already-barred cause of action and the decision to classify asbestos-related claims differently from other latent-injury claims was not so patently arbitrary as lacking any rational basis and thus, did not offend Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the manufacturers on the injured's action for asbestos related injuries.

Fox v. Tennessee Bd. of Paroles


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9506-CH-00263


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 746



November 17, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. No. 94-2505-III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged a decision from the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendant, the Tennessee Board of Paroles, in the inmate's petition for a common-law writ of certiorari that sought to challenge the Board's denial of parole to him.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of a brutal rape, and the conviction was affirmed on appeal. After a parole hearing, a Board member commented that the inmate was a "very violent person." The inmate was then notified that the entire Board declined to parole him. After exhausting his administrative appeals, the inmate filed a petition for common-law writ of certiorari, which was dismissed. The court affirmed the dismissal. First, the Board's motion under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(1) was in error and the court construed it as a motion under Rule 12.02(6); that is, the issue was not jurisdictional. Rather, it went to the sufficiency of the complaint. A common-law writ of certiorari permitted a court to review the manner in which the Board reached its decision but not to review the intrinsic correctness of the decision itself. The inmate challenged the decision only. He did not contend that the Board's decision was beyond its jurisdiction or that it was illegal, fraudulent, or arbitrary. The inmate's challenge to the individual Board member's comment failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. Last, inmates in Tennessee did not have a protected liberty interest in being paroled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted the Board's motion to dismiss the inmate's petition for a common-law writ of certiorari.

Rowe v. Board of Educ.


C/A NO. 03A01-9506-CH-00179


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 698



October 31, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Permission to Appeal Granted March 25, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 214.
Appeal granted by Rowe v. Board of Educ., 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 214 (Tenn., Mar. 25, 1996)
Reversed by, Cause dismissed by Rowe v. Board of Educ., 938 S.W.2d 351, 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 713 (Tenn., 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] HAMILTON COUNTY. CHANCERY COURT. HONORABLE R. VANN OWENS, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART VACATED IN PART REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Hamilton County (Tennessee), which found in his favor in his declaratory judgment action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 complaining that a policy adopted by appellees, a city board of education and a superintendent of schools, was unconstitutional, but which determined that the teacher's constitutional rights were not violated by the policy, so he was not entitled to back pay.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was employed by the board until he was discharged for cause. After his discharge, the teacher worked as a substitute and performed satisfactorily. A board policy prohibited the rehiring of any employee who was discharged for cause, inefficiency, or immorality. Thus, when the teacher reapplied for full-time employment, his application was denied. The teacher filed an action alleging that appellees' refusal to consider him for a position violated his due process and equal protection rights. The trial court declared that the policy was invalid but that the teacher did not prove that he would have been hired in the absence of the policy. The teacher appealed, and the court affirmed the holding that the policy was invalid but vacated the rest of the judgment. Although the teacher did not have a protected property interest in being employed by the board, he had a protected liberty interest in pursuing his chosen occupation. The evidence showed that the board relied on the unconstitutional policy, that the teacher's constitutionally protected liberty interest in pursuing his chosen profession was infringed, and that he was entitled to but was denied procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the judgment of the trial court finding the board's policy unconstitutional. The court vacated the remainder of the judgment below, and it remanded the case for a hearing to determine the damages, if any, to which the teacher was entitled.

Teague v. Campbell County


C/A NO. 03A01-9507-CH-00210


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


920 S.W.2d 219; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 702



October 31, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 20, 1995. Petition for Rehearing or Reconsideration Denied November 30, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 783. Application for Permission to Appeal Denied April 29, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tenn. LEXIS 295.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHANCERY COURT. CAMPBELL COUNTY. HON. BILLY JOE WHITE, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Campbell County (Tennessee) and the Campbell County Board of Education (Tennessee), challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court of Campbell County (Tennessee), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff teachers in the teachers' action for tenure as supervisors and for supervisors' pay. The construction and application of the grandfather clause contained in 1982 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 295, § 2 was dispositive of the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The teachers had acquired tenure as teachers when 1982 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 295, which permitted the school superintendent to replace a supervisory employee by changing the employee to a teaching position, became effective. A grandfather clause in 1982 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 295, § 2 provided that the replacement provision did not apply to supervisors who were tenured when the law became effective. The teachers later were transferred to positions as supervisors, but they were eventually transferred back to the classroom as teachers. The teachers brought an action against the County and the Board. The trial court determined that the teachers were entitled to tenure as supervisors under 1949 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 384, §§ 1-2 and that they were entitled to supervisors' benefits and to back pay for the differential in salaries. The court stated that a grandfather clause had to be construed strictly against a party who sought to come within the exception. The grandfather clause contained in 1982 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 295, § 2 applied only to those who had attained tenure as supervisors in 1982. The teachers did not fall within the clause because they were not tenured supervisors in 1982.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the teachers' action.

Forrest City Grocery Co. v. Tennessee Dep't of Revenue


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9505-CH-00198


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


917 S.W.2d 247; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 673; 1995-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P71,170



October 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR. No. 93-239-II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Davidson County Chancery Court at Nashville (Tennessee), which held that the Unfair Cigarette Sales Law, Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-303, did not violate the Sherman Antitrust Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 1-7, and that it did not violate due process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the Unfair Cigarette Sales Law, Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-303, which prohibited selling cigarettes below cost with intent to injure competitors or destroy competition, was unconstitutional because it violated the Sherman Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 1-7. Appellee argued that the statute was immune from attack under the Parker state action doctrine because the legislature itself created the anticompetitive scheme. The court noted that the state could not give antitrust immunity to an agency by allowing them to fix prices, but found that such exception to Parker immunity did not apply where the legislature created the scheme. The court also found that the portion of the statute making evidence of below cost sales prima facie evidence of intent to injure competitors did not violate due process because it gave rise to a permissive inference rather than a mandatory presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the Unfair Cigarette Sales Law was immune from antitrust attack under the Parker state action doctrine and that making evidence of below cost sales prima facie evidence of a violation gave rise to permissive inference that did not violate due process.

King v. Taylor


Appeal No. 02A01-9504-CV-00091


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 666



October 17, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE D'ARMY BAILEY, JUDGE. No. 56526 T.D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to appellee mother in the mother's action to establish the paternity of her child. The action was transferred to the trial court from a juvenile court upon the father's request for a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The parties submitted to a blood test, and the results established that appellant had a 99.65 percent probability of being the child's father. The trial court granted the wife's motion for summary judgment, relying on the blood test and Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-7-112(b)(2) (amended 1994), which established a conclusive presumption of paternity where the probability of paternity was 99 percent or greater. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in its retrospective application of amended § 27-7-112(b)(2) and that the application of amended § 27-7-112(b)(2) violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court affirmed, holding that the mother was entitled to judgment as a matter of law because the retrospective application of amended § 27-7-112(b)(2) was proper where it was procedural in nature. The conclusive presumption of paternity, where the probability of paternity was 99 percent or greater, merely expedited the resolution of paternity disputes. The father's constitutional challenge was not reviewed because he did not give notice to the Tennessee State Attorney General as required under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 24.04 and Tenn. R. App. P. 32.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1694 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Lewis Ford Inc. v. Huddleston


Appeal No. 02A01-9410-CH-00235


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 664



October 17, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE D. J. ALISSANDRATOS, CHANCELLOR. No. 103501-3 R.D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commissioner of Revenue of the State of Tennessee, sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which held that a shortened statutory time frame under which appellee car dealer could seek a refund on taxes paid was an unconstitutional denial of due process.


OVERVIEW: The dealer collected sales tax on extended warranty contracts purchased by its customers and remitted those taxes to the Commissioner. It filed a claim for refund of the taxes collected and remitted during a given year. The claim was denied by the Commissioner because it was not timely filed. Under ch. 80, § 3, 1991 Tenn. Pub. Acts, no sales tax paid prior to the date of the statute could be refunded unless filed within 30 days after the effective date of the enactment of the statute. The provision applied notwithstanding the fact that under the refund statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-1802, claims for the refund of taxes collected could be filed within three years. The trial court ruled that the shortened period was unreasonable and, therefore, was a denial of due process. The Commissioner appealed, and the court upheld the judgment. The court ruled that the lack of notice arose from the fact that the 30-day limitation was never codified and was never included in § 67-1-1802. Further, the court held that, although the enactment of ch. 80, § 3, 1991 Tenn. Pub. Acts did not eliminate the post-deprivation procedure for refunds, it was so inhibitive that it accomplished that objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1695 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


City of Tullahoma v. Bedford County


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9503-CH-00086


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 507



July 28, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition to Rehear Denied August 18, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 543. As Amended September 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF BEDFORD COUNTY AT SHELBYVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 17,515. HONORABLE CORNELIA A. CLARK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two cities, an environmental service, a casket company, and an iron company, sought review of an order from the Chancery Court of Bedford County (Tennessee), which dismissed an action filed by appellants against appellees, a county and its clerk, seeking a declaration that 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 was unconstitutional, and an injunction preventing the collection of a landfill tax.


OVERVIEW: The two cities filed an action against the county and its clerk seeking an injunction against the county's collection of a landfill tax authorized by 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52. The two cities also sought a declaration that 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 conflicted with Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 68-211-101 et seq., 67-1-602 and therefore violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 and Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. The environmental service, the casket company, and the iron company intervened in the action. The trial court entered partial summary judgment that 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 was constitutional, and then dismissed the action. Appellants sought review and argued that 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 was in conflict with the general state law, and that the privilege tax was arbitrary, capricious, and wholly unreasonable, and thereby unenforceable. The court found that there was no showing that 1991 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 52 encroached upon the provisions of the general law, and that there was no ground for holding the Act unconstitutional. The court also found that the privilege tax was not in conflict with state mandated fees because the tax and the fees were not the same.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision and remanded for any necessary further proceedings.

 

1696 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Floyd v. McNeely


App. No. 02A01-9408-CH-00187


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 443



July 5, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Gibson County at Trenton. Docket No. 10082. Honorable George R. Ellis, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff paternal grandmother sought review from a decision entered in the Chancery Court of Gibson County (Tennessee), which granted defendant mother's motion to dismiss the paternal grandmother's petition to enforce a consent visitation order related to the paternal grandmother's visitation with her grandchildren.


OVERVIEW: The paternal grandmother argued that the grandparent visitation statute, Tenn. Code. Ann. § 36-6-301, was constitutional as applied to her. She also argued that the prior order of the trial court was enforceable and the trial court should have set specific visitation for the paternal grandmother. In essence, the paternal grandmother argued that her grandchildren's best interest that they have access to their natural heritage and family history. The court rejected the argument of the paternal grandparent and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court noted that the paternal grandmother's petition sought to contravene the mother's decision to restrict visitation between her children and the paternal grandmother, which was a direct challenge to the fundamental privacy interest of the mother. The court noted that the paternal grandmother did not allege that a substantial danger of harm had threatened the children or, that the mother was not a fit parent. The court concluded that under the circumstances presented and under the prevailing law, the parent had a fundamental right to prevent contact between her children and the paternal grandmother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that dismissed the paternal grandmother's petition to enforce a court order for visitation with her grandchildren.

 

1697 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


O'Dell v. Board of Comm'rs of Johnson City


03A01-9412-CV-00430


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


910 S.W.2d 436; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 375



June 2, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied November 6, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 678.


PRIOR HISTORY: WASHINGTON COUNTY. HON. THOMAS J. SEELEY, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged an order of the Law Court for Washington County at Johnson City, Tennessee, which ruled that appellee board of commissioners' agreed order providing that a city would re-zone the owner's property did not constitute illegal contract zoning.


OVERVIEW: An agreed order and ordinance provided that a city would re-zone an owner's property from single-family residential to arterial business. The owner filed an action against the commissioners alleging that the agreed order constituted impermissible contract zoning. The trial court determined that the agreed order wad not illegal. The court affirmed and held that the commissioners' imposition of conditions as a requirement of rezoning were reasonable and a valid exercise of their police power. The commissioners put forth the conditions they had to have in their development of the general concept for that area. The conditions were imposed to regulate traffic, and they were for the safety of the public. There were no facts or law that supported the owner's position that there was illegal contract zoning. There was no bilateral negotiation, and there was no bargaining.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment ruling that the commissioners' agreed order providing that a city would re-zone the owner's property did not constitute illegal contract zoning and remanded the cause for collection of costs.

 

1698 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Haynes v. State


C.C.A. # 03C01-9402-CR-00054


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 346



May 25, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied November 6, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 685.


PRIOR HISTORY: MORGAN COUNTY. Hon. E. Eugene Eblen, Judge. (Habeas Corpus).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a dismissal by the appeals as of right from a dismissal by the Criminal Court for Morgan County (Tennessee) of his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been convicted of and sentenced for assault with the intent to commit murder in the first degree, aggravated kidnapping, aggravated rape, armed robbery, and first degree burglary. Appellant filed a petition for habeas corpus relief and contended that his convictions were unconstitutional, that he had received ineffective assistance of counsel, and that there were errors in the jury instructions. The trial court denied appellant's petition and appellant sought review of the denial. The court found that appellant was not entitled to habeas relief because his convictions were arguably voidable not void and because he was not being held under an expired sentence. The court determined that defendant's allegations were better classified as petitions for post conviction relief and that there applicable three year statute of limitations as to such actions had expired. The court affirmed the prior denial of habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the prior denial of appellant's petition for habeas corpus relief.

 

1699 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Oldham v. American Civil Liberties Union Found.


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9411-CH-00527


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


910 S.W.2d 431; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 327



May 19, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Rehear Denied June 9, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 389.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SUMNER COUNTY AT GALLATIN, TENNESSEE. No. 93C-142. THE HONORABLE TOM E. GRAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a high school principal, appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court of Sumner County at Gallatin (Tennessee), which dismissed his complaint against defendant civil liberties group. The complaint sought a declaratory judgment pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-101 et seq. to declare constitutional a state statute authorizing prayer at graduation ceremonies.


OVERVIEW: The civil liberties group had written a letter to the principal warning him that if he permitted prayer at graduation ceremonies, the group might bring a legal action against him if requested by parents or students at the school. The principal filed this action against the civil liberties group seeking a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of the statute permitting prayer, Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-6-1004(c). On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal, holding that neither party had the requisite interest to justify a declaratory judgment. A declaratory judgment under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-103 required: (1) a real, not theoretical question; (2) a real interest in the person seeking the declaration; and (3) a real interest in the party opposing the declaratory judgment. The court noted that the statute in question did not require the principal to take any action or to refrain from any action. The civil liberties group had not initiated any legal action and had only indicated that it would do so if contacted by parents or students at the school if a prayer was permitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1700 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. Huddleston


C.A. No. 02A01-9404-CH-00079


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


914 S.W.2d 501; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 297



May 8, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY. Shelby Equity # 103702-1. THE HONORABLE NEAL SMALL, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensed attorney filed a refund claim with defendant Tennessee Department of Revenue for a privilege tax assessed against him under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-1701-Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-1708 (1994) (the Act). He claimed that the tax was unconstitutional. The refund claim was denied. The Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) granted summary judgment to the State. The attorney sought review.


OVERVIEW: The attorney practiced in the State. He objected to the payment of a privilege tax because it violated the separation of powers established in Tenn. Const. art. II and the grant of judicial power in Tenn. Const. art. IV. He claimed it was an invasion by the Legislature into the role, domain, and function of the judicial branch of the government. Upon review, the court found that the Act specifically provided that the tax was not a regulatory fee under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-1705. The failure to pay the tax was not grounds for discipline. The court held that a license to practice law issued by the State did not grant immunity to attorneys from the privilege tax. There was nothing in the Act that conflicted with the authority of the Supreme Court of Tennessee to control the bar. The practice of law was a privilege granted by an issuance of a license from the Supreme Court. The State Legislature had the power to tax attorneys for that privilege under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 28(c). There was no reason the practice of law should not have been subject to a privilege tax like other occupations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for the State in the attorney's claim for a refund.

 

1701 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smoky Mountain Secrets


Appeal No. 02A01-9310-CH-00230


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 284



May 3, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. No. 102358-3 R.D. THE HONORABLE D. J. ALISSANDRATOS, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State of Tennessee appealed from a decision of the Chancery Court of Shelby County at Memphis (Tennessee), which found portions of the Tennessee Charitable Solicitations Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-3-501 et seq., to be unconstitutional and violative of the Equal Protection Clauses of both the United States and Tennessee Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the Act impermissibly discriminated against professional solicitors. In partially affirming and partially reversing, the court held that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 48-3-507(b), 48-3-507(c), 48-3-507(d), 48-3-513(g)(4), 48-3-513(j)(3), as they applied to professional solicitors and not in-house solicitors, were unconstitutional and violative of equal protection. The court determined that Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-3-513(m), which prohibited charities and professional solicitors not complying with the requirements of the Act from engaging in charitable solicitations, was constitutional because it was merely an enforcement provision and applied to charities and professional solicitors alike. The court also found the exemptions under Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-3-502(a)(1), (3) for certain organizations from the Act's application did not violate equal protection because they were not similarly situated to charitable organizations governed under the Act. Finally, the court held that the Act did not violate free speech protections because it was narrowly tailored to withstand First Amendment scrutiny and did not serve as a prior restraint on speech.


OUTCOME: The court partially affirmed and partially reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

1702 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


A T & T Communications v. Cochran


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9409-BC-00427


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 261



April 26, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition to Rehear Denied June 7, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 388.


PRIOR HISTORY: RULE 12 PETITION FOR REVIEW OF THE ORDER OF THE TENNESSEE PUBLIC SERVICE COMMISSION AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. Davidson County No. 93-07799. HONORABLE MACK H. CHERRY, ADMINISTRATIVE JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant long distance telephone providers sought review of an order of appellee Tennessee Public Service Commission, which required the providers to render free service to a particular group of telephone users with respect to a particular class of telephone calls.


OVERVIEW: The providers furnished long distance telephone connections between local exchanges. They competed for the patronage of the local telephone subscribers who designated their choice among available long distance providers. The providers were compensated by billing the local customer through the local exchange. Some intra-county telephone calls in certain counties required the long distance connection between local exchanges. The Commission adopted a policy of eliminating long distance telephone calls within a single county. The Commission claimed it had the power under Tenn. Code Ann. § 65-5-201 to distribute the load of the utility costs by lowering rates charged to one class of customers because of the profits it derived from another class of customers. Upon review, the court found that the Commission did not have that authority. The order of the Commission was a taking, not for public use, but for private use of an individual at the individual's demand. Under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 21, the providers were entitled to just compensation for that taking. Thus, the Commission's order was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order that required the providers to provide free service to certain telephone users and reversed the decision. The court remanded the cause to the Commission for further proceedings.

 

1703 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Beer Bd.


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9308-CV-00389


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


908 S.W.2d 941; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 271



April 26, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR DICKSON COUNTY AT CHARLOTTE, TENNESSEE. No. CV-114. THE HONORABLE LEONARD W. MARTIN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a city beer board, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dickson County at Charlotte (Tennessee), which held that a city ordinance prohibiting the sale of beer of Sunday to be unconstitutional. The lower court reduced the beer board's suspension of appellee, a store owner's, permit for selling beer from 60 to 30 days.


OVERVIEW: The beer board of a town in Tennessee suspended the permit of a store owner to sell beer for 60 days after finding that the store owner had allowed beer to be sold to minors and on Sunday in violation of two town ordinances. The store owner filed an appeal of the beer board's decision to the trial court, alleging that the town ordinance prohibiting the sale of beer on Sunday was an unconstitutional violation of Tenn. Const. art. I, § 3, which was analogous to the Establishment Clause of the U.S. Constitution. The trial court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional and reduced the suspension to 30 days. The appellate court held that although the prohibition against sale of beer on Sunday was rooted exclusively in religion, the prohibition had taken on a secular meaning and did not run afoul of Tenn. Const. art. I., § 3. The appellate court also rejected the store owner's arguments that the beer board's decision violated the due process clause of the Tennessee Constitution. As such, the trial court's decision was reversed and the 60 day suspension was reinstated against the store owner.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the decision of the trial court that held a city ordinance unconstitutional and reinstated the 60 day suspension entered against the store owner for allowing the sale of beer to minors and allowing the sale of beer on Sunday.

 

1704 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Lufkin v. Tennessee Dep't of Revenue


03A01-9410-CH-00388


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 249



April 20, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] KNOX COUNTY. HON. FREDERICK D. McDONALD, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Knox County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant Tennessee Department of Revenue (TDR) in the attorney's action seeking to permanently enjoin the TDR from attempting to collect an occupational privilege tax from him.


OVERVIEW: The attorney refused to pay his occupational privilege tax to TDR. The attorney alleged that the grant of a license to practice law was a contract, and that his contract obligations were impaired by the tax. The attorney also claimed that the tax deprived him of the guarantees of equal protection. On appeal, the court held that granting a license to practice law did not create a binding contract between the attorney and the State. The court noted that there was no reason to determine that a license to practice law was a contract while a license to practice medicine was not. The court found that in order for the attorney's equal protection argument to have succeeded, he had to establish that there was no legitimate state interest in treating different professionals differently. The court rejected the attorney's argument that physicians, photographers, and school teachers were so similarly circumstanced that the legislature could not tax them differently without risking a lawsuit claiming a violation of equal protection. Further, the court ruled that there were reasonable bases for the legislature to classify different professionals differently.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the TDR.

 

1705 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


American Tel. & Tel. Co. v. Proffitt


C/A NO. 03A01-9409-CV-00325


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


903 S.W.2d 309; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 201



March 30, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied July 3, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 361.


PRIOR HISTORY: LAW COURT. GREENE COUNTY. HON. W.L. JENKINS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged a judgment from the Greene County Court (Tennessee), which ruled in appellee telephone company's favor in an action for condemnation to lay underground fiber optic telephone cable. Damages were awarded to the landowners, who contended that Tenn. Code Ann. § 65-21-204 required the telephone company to fail in obtaining a right of way by consent, contract, or agreement as a condition precedent to condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The Tennessee Valley Authority, which established above-ground transmission towers on an easement from an earlier condemnation proceeding, was willing to run cable jointly with the telephone company, which decided instead to install underground, which the landowners contended exceeded public necessity. On review, the court found no fraud, bad faith, or gross abuse of discretion in the telephone company's condemnation proceeding. The court asserted that the telephone company had a legitimate technological reason for the underground installation, and once the cable was buried, it would be less intrusive, not visibly interfering with using and enjoying the land and requiring less maintenance. The court observed that the tower easement included rights to lay foundations, obviously extending them downward into the land to some depth, similar to underground cable. The court found the landowners' statutory construction overly narrow and contrary to legislative intent delegating eminent domain power to telecommunications companies and utilizing the statute as technology developed. The court found the statute rationally related to a conceivable public purpose and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the telephone company and remanded this eminent domain proceeding.

 

1706 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Douglas v. State


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9409-CH-00450


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 182



March 22, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 91-2759-I. HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner dentist appealed an order of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee) affirming a decision of the trial court, which affirmed a decision of the Tennessee State Board of Dentistry reprimanding the dentist for improper advertising of his dental practice, a violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-5-124 and Tenn. Bd. Dentistry R. 0460-7-.05(2).


OVERVIEW: Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-5-112 provided that a dentist should not hold himself out to the public as a specialist until he had completed the additional requirements established by the Board. The dentist argued that the statutes and regulations violated his right to free speech and due process, and that his business cards were not advertisements under the Board's rules. The court reversed on the first issue and vacated the Board's reprimand. Commercial speech held a qualified protection under the First Amendment. The Board bore the burden of justifying its restriction on commercial speech. There was no evidence that any actual person was misled or harmed by the dentist's advertisement. The Board failed to take administrative knowledge, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-313(6)(A)(C), of the fact that a person would assume that a dentist offering specialized services was certified in the area. The fact that a person could be harmed from seeking orthodontic treatment from a dentist not certified in the speciality was not so well known among the general public that it was a subject for judicial notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the Board's order reprimanding the dentist. It assessed all costs of the appeal against the Board. The court remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a judgment.

 

1707 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Town of Carthage v. Smith County


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9308-CH-00391


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 142



March 8, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR SMITH COUNTY AT CARTHAGE, TENNESSEE. No. 4928. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM H. INMAN, SENIOR JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, cities and mayors, sought review of a judgment after a bench trial in the Chancery Court for Smith County (Tennessee), which dismissed their action for an injunction prohibiting defendant county from charging allegedly unconstitutional "tipping fees" for the use of its landfill.


OVERVIEW: The county opened a landfill in which residents and cities could deposit solid wastes. The county charged fees to persons and entities using the landfill. The cities brought an action against the county seeking a declaratory judgment that the fee was an unconstitutional tax-shifting device that imposed a heavier tax burden on city residents than on county residents. The mayors of the cities intervened in the action as individual property owners and taxpayers. After a bench trial, the chancery court entered judgment in favor of the county. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that (1) the mayors and one city did not file a timely notice of appeal identifying themselves as parties as required by Tenn. R. App. P. 3(f) and were not properly before the court; (2) the cities were exempt from the county's taxes and lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the fees under Tenn. Const. art. 2, § 28 and the Equal Protection Clause; (3) Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-19-103 permitted the county to open the landfill without a single resolution defining its program; and (4) the fee was not a tax because residents could avoid it by refraining from using the landfill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the judgment dismissing the cities' action for an injunction prohibiting the county from charging fees for the use of its landfill. The dismissal of the mayors' action also was upheld.

 

1708 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Cumberland v. Wilkinson


C.A. NO. 03A01-9409-CV-00351


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 80



February 13, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CIRCUIT COURT. ROANE COUNTY. HON. RUSSELL SIMMONS, JR. JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Cumberland Utility District of Roane and Morgan Counties, Tennessee, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Roane County (Tennessee) dismissing its petition to condemn property owned by appellees, a landowner and a trustee. The trial court held that the Utility District did not comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-302(g) by agreeing with nearby municipalities to supply water or notifying them of its intent to serve the area.


OVERVIEW: The Utility District argued that the trial court erred in failing to award it possession of the property after appellees did not question its right to take within five days. It contended that the trial court erred in holding that it did not comply with the service provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-302(g). The court agreed that the trial court should have given a writ of possession when there was no defect in the service process. Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-305 gave the Utility District the power of eminent domain to supply water within its district. It was to follow the procedures set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-17-801 et seq. and Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-301. The condemnation petition met all the formal statutory requirements. Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-82-302(g) gave municipalities the prior right to extend water utilities into an area within three or five miles of their corporate limits. The benefits of the statute only inured to the benefit of the municipalities that were within the specified area and not to an individual. Appellees lacked standing to use as a defense a statute that dealt with corporate powers. The court remanded for an order of immediate possession.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for an immediate order of possession of the property.

 

1709 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Doane v. City of Oak Ridge


C/A NO. 03A01-9409-CH-00337


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


898 S.W.2d 728; 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 7



January 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 3, 1995. Petition for Rehearing Denied February 14, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. App. LEXIS 99. Application for Permission to Appeal Denied May 8, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 233.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHANCERY COURT. ANDERSON COUNTY. HON. FRANK V. WILLIAMS, III, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court of Anderson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to defendant City in a declaratory judgment action seeking to enjoin the City from issuing capital outlay notes to finance the construction of a municipal golf course.


OVERVIEW: The City undertook to acquire land to construct a public golf course. The City selected a Texas firm to design and construct the course. The City also decided to issue capital outlay notes to finance the project. The City and the firm were to enter into a land lease agreement providing that the firm was to lease a portion of land where it was to construct, operate, and maintain certain practice facilities. The facilities were to be open to the public and turned over to the City upon expiration of the lease term. The City granted the firm an option to purchase certain remaining portions of land. The court concluded that the state constitution and statutes did not proscribe the proposed agreements and that they fell within the ambit of Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-21-107. The issuance of the notes was not an unconstitutional lending of the City's credit to the firm. The proceeds of the notes were to have been used to finance the construction of the course only, which the City would have owned and operated upon completion. Nor had the City entered into an implied partnership arrangement with the firm amounting to an unconstitutional lending of the City's credit to the firm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with costs of appeal assessed to plaintiffs.

 

1710 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Jenkins


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9407-PB-00311


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 739



December 16, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE PROBATE COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 99940. THE HONORABLE JAMES R. EVERETT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the executors of a decedent's estate, sought review of a decision by the Probate Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which overruled the executors' objections to a master's report finding that appellee creditor had filed a timely claim against the decedent's estate and that the executors had failed to comply with Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-306(E) by not sending notice to the readily ascertainable creditor.


OVERVIEW: The creditor had obtained a judgment against the deceased and the parties had agreed on the terms for paying that judgment prior to the decedent's death. The executors made the first payments under the agreement but then refused to make any other payments because the creditor had not made a timely claim against the estate under Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-307(a)(1). The creditor admitted that he did not file his claim within six months after the first publication of the general notice to creditors but claimed that the failure was not fatal because the executors admitted that they failed to mail him the notice required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-306(e). The court held that: (1) the legislature intended to bar unfiled claims against estates by imposing the requirement of mailed notice to creditors; (2) the executors had personal knowledge of the creditor's claim, so § 30-2-307 was inapplicable, and § 30-2-310 was the applicable barring statute; and (3) the creditor's claim was not barred by § 30-2-310 because mailed written notice was not given as required by § 30-2-306(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1711 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Nolichuckey Sand Co. v. Huddleston


C/A NO. 03A01-9406-CH-00189


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


896 S.W.2d 782; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 676



November 29, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied April 3, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 157.


PRIOR HISTORY: GREENE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. HONORABLE DENNIS H. INMAN, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought against appellee Commissioner of Revenue to challenge the constitutionality of the county option mineral severance tax, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-7-201, appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision from the Chancery Court of Green County (Tennessee), which held that the doctrine of elision could be used to strike the unconstitutional portions and to save the constitutional portions.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted a mineral severance tax, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 67-7-201 et seq., which allowed counties to levy taxes on minerals. The taxpayer challenged the statute and contended that classifications based on population were unconstitutional and that the entire statute was unenforceable. The trial court found that a portion of the act was unconstitutional but that that the doctrine of elision could be used to save the invalid portions. The taxpayer sought review. The court affirmed. It found that the population classification section violated the privileges and immunities clause, Tenn. Const. art. 11, § 8 because it acted an as impermissible suspension of general law. The court also found that the population classifications violated the equal protection clause in Tenn. Const. Art. 1, § 8 because the classifications lacked a rational basis. The court further found that the doctrine of elision could be used to save the remaining portions of the tax law because when the legislature included a severability clause, the legislature manifested an intent to have the valid parts of the statute in force if some other portion of the statute was declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision rendered in favor of the Commissioner and remanded the action for collection of costs.

 

1712 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Cannon v. Bristol Bd. of Educ.


NO. 03A01-9401-CH-00025


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 667



November 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. SULLIVAN COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher challenged the decision of the Chancery Court of Sullivan County (Tennessee), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendant board of education (board) on the grounds that the teacher's action seeking to review his termination was res judicata.


OVERVIEW: After notice and a hearing, the board fired the teacher for unprofessional conduct and insubordination. While the teacher's petition for review was pending, he filed a complaint in federal court alleging that his discharge violated his federally protected rights to due process and freedom of speech. The federal court decided the issues against the teacher. The board argued, and the lower court agreed, that the teacher's claims were res judicata. The court affirmed the dismissal of the teacher's action. Not only were his claims barred by res judicata, it was evident that the teacher's aggressive actions and statements were intolerably disruptive of the school system and were markedly unprofessional. His statements were destructive of the board's responsibility in fulfilling its obligation to operate a school system. This obligation outweighed the teacher's interest in exercising his right of free speech.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the teacher's action against the board seeking review of his termination was affirmed.

 

1713 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. Board of Dentistry


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9405-CH-00207


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 631



October 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 92-3108-II. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff petitioner sought review of a judgment by the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, which affirmed an interlocutory administrative order by defendant, Tennessee Board of Dentistry, that held that the Board had the authority to subject the petitioner to civil penalties under Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-134 although he was not licensed by the Board.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was charged with violating Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 63-5-107, 63-5-121 by operating a dental clinic and practicing dentistry without a license. The trial court reviewed the administrative interlocutory order and considered the supplemental record, which the court held that the review of the extraneous evidence was admissible in support of a defense of res judicata or judicial estoppel. The court held that practicing dentistry and operating a dental clinic are crimes under the laws of Tennessee, for violation of which the board is not qualified to determine guilt or punishment. The court found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 63-1-134 authorized any board attached to the "division of health related boards" to assess a civil penalty for each violation of a "statute, rule, or order pertaining to such board." The application of that provision to acts otherwise declared to be state criminal offenses would have been unconstitutional. To the extent that said act may have been so applied, it was unconstitutional. Thus the court held that the board had no authority over the offenses involved in the appeal and reversed and vacated the order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, rendered, and remanded the order.

 

1714 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. McCormick v. Burson


Appeal No. 01A01-9404-CH-00171


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


894 S.W.2d 739; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 622; 4 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 126



October 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DAVIDSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 93-2724-II. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ward appealed a judgment of the Davidson County Chancery Court at Nashville, Tennessee, which upheld the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 34-11-101 et seq. and 34-13-101 et seq. of the state's conservatorship statutes.


OVERVIEW: The ward was judged incompetent after a serious head injury severely impaired his mental ability. After the ward's condition improved, he remained involuntarily hospitalized. He filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus and for release from the hospital and the conservatorship, and asked the trial court to permanently enjoin enforcement of the conservatorship laws. The ward claimed the laws violated his due process and equal protection rights. The trial court dissolved the conservatorship and found the laws constitutional. On appeal, the court held that the laws at issue provided extensive procedural safeguards at the time of the conservator's appointment and that wards had unlimited rights to meaningful review hearings at which they may prove regained capability. Because the ward could contact a court or file a petition, the laws did not restrict the ward's liberty on the ground of substantive due process. The court found that the state's interest in protecting incompetents survived strict scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding the conservatorship laws to be constitutional.

 

1715 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Barry v. Commissioner of Commerce & Ins.


Appeal No. 01A01-9404-CH-00156


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 515



September 9, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE WILSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT AT LEBANON, TENNESSEE. No. 9233. THE HONORABLE C. K. SMITH, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff architect sought review of an order from the Chancery Court for Wilson County at Lebanon (Tennessee) granting defendants', the commissioner and the state board, motion to dismiss his declaratory judgment action seeking injunctive relief permitting him to remodel a building.


OVERVIEW: The architect sought to remodel a building located in Wilson County. Thereafter, the architect received a stop work order from the state fire marshall and an order from the board to cease the unlicensed practice of architecture and engineering. The architect responded by filing a declaratory judgment action whereby he sought injunctive relief to allow him to finish the remodeling. The commissioner and the board responded with a motion to dismiss for improper venue. The motion was granted, and the architect appealed the order. The architect argued that venue was proper in the county where the property was located according to Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-4-107. The court noted, however, that a lawsuit brought against a state officer in his or her official capacity, such as the commissioner and the board, must have been brought in the county of the officer's official residence. Therefore, venue was improper in Wilson County, and the motion was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1716 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Hitson v. Bradley


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9403-CH-00129


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 442



August 12, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Adams v. Oliveira, 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 442 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY, AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 92-3429-II. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff inmate one sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court for Davidson County, at Nashville (Tennessee) that denied his cross-motion for summary judgment and dismissed his action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief with regard to an increase in his release eligibility date (RED). Plaintiff inmate two challenged the dismissal of his action for review of the revocation of his parole eligibility.


OVERVIEW: Both inmates had previously entered a guilty plea to the disciplinary offense of escape. They argued that the extension of their REDs violated their due process and equal protection rights. Affirming the dismissal of their actions, the court stated that the REDs were extended pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-501(i) and Tennessee Department of Corrections (TDOC) policy number 502.02, which provided for the extension of an inmate's RED for violations of certain disciplinary rules. The TDOC policy was not a rule within the meaning of Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-102(10) in that the policy addressed internal management of the TDOC and did not affect the rights of the public at large. The trial court properly dismissed the inmates' petitions and held that they were not entitled to a declaratory judgment as a matter of law. The court stated that the inmates' petitions failed to allege any due process right violation. Further, no violation of the inmates' equal protection rights was found as the challenged policy was closely related to a legitimate state interest in preventing the escape of inmates, and there was no showing of any arbitrary discrimination against any class of inmates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and remanded the cases for any further proceedings that may have been necessary.

Ball v. Lawson


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9402-CH-00075


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 446



August 12, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Chancery Court. Davidson County. No. 92-819-III. Hon. Robert S. Brandt Chancellor



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner vehicle owner appealed from a decision of the Chancery Court, Davidson County (Tennessee), which affirmed the seizure of the owner's vehicle by respondent Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Safety pursuant to the Tennessee Drug Control Act.


OVERVIEW: The vehicle belonged to the owner, and was in his possession at the time of his drug-related arrest. At the time of the seizure, the owner was given a document from the state setting forth the requirements to request a hearing for return of the automobile. The owner mailed his petition for a hearing regarding the seizure, but the petition was not received by the Commissioner within the time set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-201. The Commissioner therefore denied the request for a hearing. In affirming the trial court's decision to affirm the Commissioner, the court held that because the owner's petition was not received on time, and because the owner did not file either a bond or a pauper's oath as required by § 53-11-201(c), the Commissioner properly denied the owner's request for a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
