Carruth v. City of Etowah


No. 03A01-9311-CV-00407


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


892 S.W.2d 833; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 425



August 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied January 7, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tenn. LEXIS 3.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Circuit Court of McMinn County at Athens. Honorable John B. Hagler, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of McMinn County (Tennessee), which directed a verdict for appellees, city and police officers, for unlawful arrest, false imprisonment, outrageous conduct, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and violating his civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The individual had been drinking. His uncle prevented him from leaving and an altercation ensued. The individual's mother called the police. The officers entered the premises and gave the individual the choice of going home with his uncle, staying at the apartment with his uncle, or going to jail. He left with his uncle. En route, he jumped out of the vehicle. The officers found him and arrested him for public drunkenness and disorderly conduct. He was found guilty. The individual contended that the officers unlawfully searched his home, evicted him from his home, and arrested him. Upon review, the court found that the city was immune from liability on the state law claims. The court found that the record was devoid of any evidence suggesting a policy or custom of the police to ask citizens to leave town. The court found that considering the individual's actions, the officers acted reasonably under the circumstances and did not violate his rights as a matter of law. Under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-17-305(a)(1) and 39-17-310(a), the individual's arrest was valid. There was no evidence to support the state law claims against the officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the directed verdict for appellees in the individual's action for for unlawful arrest, false imprisonment, outrageous conduct, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and violating his civil rights under § 1983.

Short v. Short


CA No. 03A01-9402-CH-00065


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 366



July 5, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. SULLIVAN COUNTY. HON. RICHARD E. LADD, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother filed a child support enforcement action against appellant father. The Chancery Court of Sullivan County (Tennessee) found the father to be in arrears and ordered the father to pay a certain amount per month for child support plus an amount to be applied to the arrearage. The husband appealed the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: After the parties were divorced, the wife filed an action to enforce the husband's child support obligation. The husband raised the issue of the child's paternity, but the trial court found that the issue was barred by res judicata. The trial court found the husband to be in arrears in child support payments and ordered the husband to pay a certain amount per month for child support plus an amount to be applied to the arrearage. On appeal, the court held that: (1) Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-101(a)(5) did not violate any fundamental constitutional right because it had a rational basis and it was reasonably related to a legitimate state purpose; (2) res judicata barred the husband's argument on the paternity issue because his claim did not show a change in facts but merely newly discovered evidence; and (3) the trial court did not commit an abuse of discretion in determining that relief under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 60 was not appropriate because the husband failed to note the specific grounds for relief and he failed to disclose the nature of the evidence suggesting that he was not the child's father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for execution of its judgment and collection of costs as provided by law.

Boles v. City of Chattanooga


03A01-9402-CH-00070


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


892 S.W.2d 416; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 367



July 5, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied October 24, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 308.


PRIOR HISTORY: HAMILTON COUNTY. HONORABLE HOWELL N. PEOPLES, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant City that involved zoning issues. The Hamilton County Court (Tennessee) found in favor of the property owners. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: This was a declaratory judgment action that involved zoning. The property owners and others had operated an adult book and video store at their location since the early 1970's. In 1977, the City amended its zoning ordinance to add new regulations that governed adult-oriented establishments. Under the amendment, the property was no longer zoned for an adult-oriented establishment, but such a use there was permitted as a pre-existing non-confirming use under the grandfather provision of the ordinance. In 1987 the attorney general filed a suit against the property owners that sought to abate the public nuisance. The criminal court issued a temporary injunction that restrained the property owners from continuing the operation. The city then took the position that the property owners had abandoned their business and were no longer grandfathered in. The court affirmed the lower court and held that the zoning ordinance was held to a strict construction. The court held that the term abandoned did not apply to involuntary closing of the business by the criminal court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings to collect costs, assessed against the city.

Morris v. Snodgrass


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9401-CH-00018


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


886 S.W.2d 761; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 317



June 15, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 93-1491-I. HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county officials sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee) that entered summary dismissal in favor of appellee State officials in an action for declaratory relief. The county had requested the trial court to declare Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-103 and Tenn. Code Ann. § 45-25-129 unconstitutional and that the State was obligated to share the expense resulting from said statutes.


OVERVIEW: One of the statutes at issue dealt with the imprisonment of persons convicted of the offense of driving while intoxicated. The county asserted that the mandatory imposition of minimum jail sentences had placed a heavy burden of expense upon the county to feed and house the prisoners, which additional expense the State was obligated to share by Tenn. Const. art. II, § 24. The State contended that the legislature made statutory provision for the State's sharing of the increased expense of keeping prisoners and that the amount of such provision was a legislative matter and not subject to judicial review. The court agreed with the State and affirmed the judgment. The court concluded that the legislature was constitutionally empowered to elect what the share of the State would be in the subject expenses. The share enacted by the legislature was substantial and was not an ineffective compliance with the constitution. Because the statute was constitutional, the county could not complain of its terms.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and remanded the cause for any necessary further proceedings.

Rayford v. State


Davidson Chancery No. 01A01-9311-CH-00489


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 305



June 3, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment from the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which dismissed the inmate's petition challenging a Parole Eligibility Review Board (Board) decision to deny him a new release eligibility date. Upon respondent State's motion to dismiss, the petition was dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and failure to state a claim on which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of aggravated rape. He was sentenced to life as a habitual offender under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-1-801, which was repealed and superseded by the Criminal Sentencing Reform Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-101 et seq (1990). The Board notified the inmate that a proposed amendment to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-602(a) would prohibit the Board from reviewing the sentences of offenders whose triggering offense was an crime against the person. The proposed amendment did not pass and the Board decided not to consider granting the inmate a new release eligibility date. The inmate argued that the trial court erred in dismissing his petition for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and failure to state a claim. The inmate also argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-602 was unconstitutional because it created a class of offenders to whom a new release eligibility date was not available. The court dismissed the inmate's constitutional claims as meritless because he merely alleged the Board made a mistake in not granting him a release eligibility date. The court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-602(c) clearly provided that the Board's decision was not subject to judicial review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: After his request for parole was denied, the inmate filed an action against the Board requesting that the Board be required to show cause why it did not grant the inmate parole. Nelson v. McMinn County


CA No. 03A01-9312-CH-00428


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 222



April 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. McMINN COUNTY. HON. EARL H. HENLEY CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged an order of Chancery Court of McMinn County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to appellees, board of commissioners and others, on the owner's declaratory relief action to force his donation of property.


OVERVIEW: The owner's property was adjacent to an airport. As a pilot, the owner sought to run his aviation business by directly accessing the airport. The owner's request to operate from his property to the airport through a fence was denied by the board, as was his request to donate and lease the property back. The claimant filed an action for declaratory relief. The lower court granted summary judgment to the board. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment, concluding that the board's action was not wide of any reasonable remark. Rather, the uncontroverted facts showed that the board rejected the owner's offer to donate his property for safety reasons. Thus, no constitutional violation occurred. Nor did the board act illegally, arbitrarily, or capriciously. Thus, the court was precluded from substituting its judgment for that of the board. To hold otherwise was to infringe on the authority of local government entities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed. The matter was remanded.

Deweese v. Board of Funeral Directors & Embalmers


No. 01A01-9310-CH-00433


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 213



April 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville. Honorable C. Allen High, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In cases consolidated for trial, defendant, the Board of Funeral Directors and Embalmers of the State of Tennessee, challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff industry representatives in the representatives' actions challenging the Board's promulgation of Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0660-6-.01.


OVERVIEW: The representatives filed two separate actions challenging the Board's authority to promulgate Rule 0660-6-.01, which required that unlicensed assistants only perform their duties in the presence and under the personal supervision of a licensed funeral director. The actions were consolidated for trial, and the trial court granted summary judgment to the representatives, holding that the Board's promulgation of Rule 0660-6-.01 exceeded its legislative authority. The Board appealed. The representatives contended that the Board's promulgation of Rule 0660-6-.01 was an unlawful attempt to legislate. The court observed that an administrative agency's rules or regulations could not be inconsistent with a constitutional provision or other law on the subject, nor could the rules affect or create a substantive right. The court held the Board's attempt to define the phrase "under the direction and supervision" to be an impermissible alteration or enlargement of the legislature's enactment of Tenn. Code Ann. § 62-5-313. The court further found that Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 0660-6-.01, if allowed to stand, would have affected the substantive rights of the representatives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Owens v. Truckstops of Am.


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9305-CV-00208


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 189



April 6, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE SECOND CIRCUIT COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 88C-3054. HONORABLE MARIETTA M. SHIPLEY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: FIRST APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART. SECOND APPEAL: REVERSED AND VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party filed a negligence action against defendant restaurant. The restaurant filed a third-party complaint against third-party defendant stool manufacturer and retailer. The manufacturer and retailer sought interlocutory review of a decision of the Second Circuit Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which denied their motions to dismiss, and which granted leave to the injured party to amend his complaint to include them.


OVERVIEW: A stool on which the injured party was sitting while in the restaurant collapsed, injuring him. The stool manufacturer and retailer contended that the McIntyre decision announcing the rule of comparative negligence required reversal of the trial court's decision denying their motions to dismiss because the type of indemnity or contribution sought by the restaurant was abolished by the decision. The court, affirming in part and reversing in part, held that the third-party complaint did not state an action under the Uniform Contribution Among Joint Tort Feasors Act, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-11-101-106 (1980), because pursuant to McIntyre, the rule of pro-rata distribution of liability among joint tortfeasors was defunct. However, the court also held the additional allegation of the third-party complaint for breach of implied warranty or indemnity was not properly subject to a motion to dismiss. With regard to the second appeal the court reversed the trial court's order after it concluded that using Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-1-119 to revive an action that was already time-barred, as were the injured party's claims against the manufacturer and retailer, violated Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part as to the manufacturer's and retailer's appeal of the trial court's denial of their motions to dismiss. Further, in the appeal by the manufacturer and retailer of the grant of leave to the injured party to amend his complaint to include them, the court reversed and vacated.

Brittain v. Metropolitan Gov't


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9309-CV-00402


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 140



March 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 89C-2694. THE HONORABLE MARIETTA SHIPLEY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, which awarded appellee homeowners damages in their inverse condemnation action.


OVERVIEW: The city hired a contractor to install a sewer line in a county. The contractor cut in half a culvert that was designed to direct storm water away from the homeowners' property, but it failed to repair the broken culvert. The homeowners noticed settling problems on their property. They filed an inverse condemnation action against the city. The trial court awarded them damages, and the court affirmed. The court held that between the affected homeowners and the city's citizens, the users of the public improvement, the latter had to absorb the losses. The existence of a possible alternate remedy did not deprive the homeowners of the right to pursue their constitutional protections under the procedures outlined in the inverse condemnation statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-16-123. Under the discovery rule, the statute of limitations did not run until the negligent injury was or should have been discovered. The homeowners did not suspect that their problem was related to the city's sewage project until a contractor they had hired crawled into the culvert and found it blocked by a wall of rock. They promptly notified the city, which then repaired the culvert.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order awarding the homeowners' damages in their inverse condemnation action against the city and remanded the case to the trial court for whatever further proceedings were required.

 

1728 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


American Tel. & Tel. Co. v. Huddleston


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9307-CH-00318


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


880 S.W.2d 682; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 141



March 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 89-1157-II. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Commissioner of Revenue (commissioner) denied the petition of appellant affiliated corporations for a variance and request to file their tax returns on a combined basis, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-812(c). The corporations sought a refund for taxes paid based on the denial of their petition. The Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee) ruled in favor of the commissioner. The corporations appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporations claimed that they were a unitary enterprise and entitled to combine their tax reporting for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-811, which provided for apportionment of multi-state businesses under the Uniform Division of Income for Tax Purposes Act of 1976. The commissioner argued that the apportionment had to be based on treating the corporations as separate entities. The commissioner had denied the corporations' petition for a variance because there was no evidence to support a combined reporting. The court affirmed the chancery court's judgment that denied the corporations a tax refund. The court held that § 67-4-811 was unambiguous, and its apportionment provision was not designed for a unitary group. There was nothing in § 67-4-811 that required the commissioner to adopt an alternative formula. The evidence showed that the apportionment formula fairly related to the corporations' business activity in the state, and the corporations failed to meet the burden required to justify departure from the normal formula.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the chancery court, which denied the corporations' request for a refund.

 

1729 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


McClain v. Kingswood Homeowners' Ass'n


No. 01A01-9304-CV-00187


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 134



March 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville. Honorable Hamilton Gayden, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenants challenged the judgments of the Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which granted appellees, homeowners' association and management company, a credit for the tenants' settlement with the tortfeasor's estate and denied their motion for prejudgment interest in the tenants' negligence action to recover damages for loss of personal property in a condominium fire.


OVERVIEW: The tenants lost personal property in a fire in their condominium complex that was started by a tortfeasor's negligent operation of a charcoal grill on his home's balcony. The tenants filed a negligence action against the homeowners' association, management company, and the tortfeasor's estate. The tenants settled with the estate. A jury that applied comparative fault principles found the association and company totally responsible for the tenants' damages. The trial court reduced the judgment by the amount of the settlement and denied the tenants' motion for prejudgment interest. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that the association and the company were entitled to a credit in the amount of the settlement with the tortfeasor's estate to reduce the judgments entered against them in accordance with Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-11-105(2)(b). The Uniform Contribution Among Tort-Feasors Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-11-101 et seq., remained in effect despite the state's newly adopted system of comparative fault. The tenants waived the issue of prejudgment interest by failing to move for a new trial as required by Tenn. R. App. P. 3(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the tenants' motion for prejudgment interest and the order that granted the homeowners' association and the management company credit for the settlement received from a tortfeasor's estate.

 

1730 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Bible v. Hamblen County ex rel. Hamblen County Beer Bd.


CA No. 03A01-9309-CV-00305


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 112



March 7, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. HAMBLEN COUNTY. HON. DENNIS H. INMAN CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant filed an action against respondents, a county beer board and a county executive, for a writ of certiorari pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 57-5-109(d) to review the board's action in denying his application for a beer permit. The Chancery Court for Hamblen County (Tennessee) granted respondents' motion for summary judgment and denied the applicant's motion. It dismissed the petition for certiorari. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The application was denied despite the fact that the applicant had complied with Tenn. Code Ann. § 57-5-105 and the county beer ordinance. The board did not give a reason for the denial, but after the applicant filed his action for a writ of certiorari, the county amended its zoning ordinance to state that beer sales would not be permitted within 300 feet of a residence provided that the resident appeared before the board and objected. The court stated that under § 57-5-105, a beer board had to issue a license to anyone who met the requirements of the statute. It could not prescribe conditions for the issuance of a permit in addition to those set out in the statute. Next, the court held that the trial court erred in finding that the amendment of the ordinance to include the "300 foot rule" was grounds for denial of the permit. In a proceeding for review under Tenn. Code Ann. § 57-5-109(d), statutory law at the time of the commission of the act applied, and the trial court erred in applying the rule retroactively because it was not only procedurally remedial in nature. Moreover, even if the rule had been in effect, no residential owner had objected to the issuance of the permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision. It remanded the case to the trial court for the entry of a decree in accordance with the court's opinion and for the trial court to order that the applicant be issued a beer license.

Haynes v. City of Pigeon Forge


CA No. 03A01-9309-CV-00309


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


883 S.W.2d 619; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 98



March 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied July 25, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 241.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIRCUIT COURT. SEVIER COUNTY. HON. WILLIAM R. HOLT, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee operators filed separate actions seeking to have an ordinance of appellant city invalidated. The actions were heard together, and the city filed a motion for summary judgment. The Circuit Court of Sevier County (Tennessee), sua sponte, entered judgment in favor of the operators and declared Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208(f) unconstitutional. The city appealed, and the actions were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The operators provided helicopter services on a commercial basis. After annexation in 1977 and 1978, the operators were permitted to operate their respective helicopter businesses as a pre-existing nonconforming use under the city's zoning ordinance. Subsequently, the city enacted City of Pigeon Forge, Tenn., Ordinance 411, which prohibited any existing helicopter operation to land or take off from land within the corporate limits of the city by a certain date. The operators filed their actions in response. The trial court, sua sponte, ruled Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208(f) was unconstitutional, and thus City of Pigeon Forge, Tenn., Ordinance 411 was invalid. On appeal, the court affirmed the action invalidating the Ordinance 411, but pretermitted the constitutional issue because the failure of the city to submit Ordinance 411 to the planning commission rendered it fatally defective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the operators, taxed costs to the city, and remanded the action to the trial court.

Hourglass Lounge v. City of Johnson City


CA No. 03A01-9311-CH-00383


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE


879 S.W.2d 860; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 102



March 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied June 20, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tenn. LEXIS 201.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] WASHINGTON CHANCERY. HON. THOMAS J. SEELEY, JR., CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Johnson City sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court for Washington County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee strip club in its declaratory action initiated against the City contending that the City's ordinance, which prohibited the sale of alcoholic beverages to any strip places, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The City enacted the ordinance prohibiting the sale of alcohol in strip clubs. The strip club contended that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it failed to follow the procedures set forth in the City's charter regarding the enactment of amendments to legislation. The trial court found in favor of the strip club, and the City sought review. Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-20-214, no ordinance was to be amended except by a new ordinance. However, the court found that an ordinance did not become an ordinance until after its third reading. The court determined that what constituted a material or substantial change in an ordinance between the date of its first and final reading was dependent upon the circumstances of each case. The court held that, if nothing new was added to the ordinance or if what was taken had not rendered it misleading in its fundamental concept, the alteration was not material as to characterize the ordinance different from the previous reading. The court held that the ordinance had not been materially changed between readings. The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded and found that, because the ordinance had not been materially changed between its first and third readings, as required by the City's charter, it was constitutional.

 

1733 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Witcher v. Bilbrey


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9210-CV-00428


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


878 S.W.2d 567; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 103



March 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 16, 1994. Application for Permission to Appeal Denied June 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MACON COUNTY AT LAFAYETTE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE BOBBY CAPERS, JUDGE. No. 3483



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Macon County at Lafayette (Tennessee) in favor of appellee special judge in his action for mandamus to compel the county to compensate him for his services in filling a temporary vacancy that resulted from an incumbent judge's disability.


OVERVIEW: The special judge brought a successful action for mandamus to compel the county to compensate him for replacing the disabled incumbent judge. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment for the special judge and found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-2-116, which authorized the governor to appoint temporary general sessions court judges, was constitutional. In addition, the county had a statutory obligation to pay the judge's salary because Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-2-117(a) (1980) provided that special judges drew the same salary as the regular judge. Even though the statutes did not specifically assign responsibility for paying the salary, the court found that the county was responsible because state law required it to fund the entire operation of its general sessions courts, including the judge's salary. Making financial provisions to replace a disabled general sessions judge was a necessary and foreseeable part of the county's operation of that court. Mandamus was a proper remedy because the judge had no other specific or adequate remedy. The county did not meet its burden of proving that the judge was not properly serving as a special general sessions court judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded the matter for whatever further proceedings were required.

Church v. Church


Shelby Equity No. 02A01-9312-CH-00266


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 36



February 3, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR SHELBY COUNTY AT MEMPHIS, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE NEAL SMALL, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a decision from the Chancery Court at Shelby County (Tennessee), which ruled that the parties were required, pursuant to Knox County, Tenn., Ch. Ct. R. 15(g), to attend a counseling session before their divorce proceeding could be heard by a judge or jury. The husband asserted that Rule 15(g) was unconstitutional under both the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The wife filed a petition for divorce against the husband; however, the trial court refused to allow their case to be heard until the couple complied with Rule 15(g) requiring that they attend a counseling session because they had two children. The husband appealed, asserting that Rule 15(g) violated both the state and federal constitutions. The court reversed the judgment, holding that Rule 15(g) did violate the separation of powers doctrine as provided in Tenn. Const. art. II, § 1 and 2. The court held that the function of court rules was to regulate practice of the trial court and facilitate the transaction of its business, but no court rule could enlarge or restrict jurisdiction or abrogate or modify substantive law. The court noted that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-4-101-104 (1991) authorized the judiciary to grant divorces for cause which the legislature specifically stated within the statute, and Rule 15(g) improperly modified the substantive law enacted by the legislature by requiring or conditioning the parties' right to a divorce on their submission to counseling.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which ruled that the parties' divorce proceeding could not be heard by a judge or jury until they attended a counseling session.

Gay v. City of Somerville


No. 02A01-9303-CH-00054


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


878 S.W.2d 124; 1994 Tenn. App. LEXIS 33



January 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Chancery Court of Fayette County of Somerville. Honorable Joseph H. Walker, Judge (By Interchange)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former city chief of police (chief) sought review of an order of the Chancery Court of Fayette County (Tennessee), which dismissed the chief's petition for writ of certiorari after the board of mayor and aldermen (board) of appellee city affirmed the chief's termination by the city's administrator (administrator). The chief alleged, among other things, that the administrator was not authorized under the city charter to discharge him.


OVERVIEW: The chief was terminated by the administrator for failing to stay at a town square demonstration. The board affirmed the administrator's action, and the chief filed a petition for writ of certiorari with the lower court. The lower court dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed as modified and remanded. The court held that under the city's charter the administrator did not have the power to terminate the chief, because the chief was not a city employee but an officer who could only be terminated by the board. However, the administrator's act was ratified by the later actions of the board, which provided the chief with notice and a hearing before affirming the administrator's decision. Although there was sufficient evidence of the board's bias, under the "rule of necessity" the members were not required to recuse themselves because the board was the only agency authorized to make a decision as to the chief's employment. Under a heightened standard of review, the court found that an objective decisionmaker would have reached the same conclusion as the board. Because the chief was entitled to back pay, the action was remanded to assess the proper amount of compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the chief's petition for writ of certiorari, modifying such order only as to the chief's entitlement to back pay based on the effective date of his termination. The court remanded for a determination of the appropriate amount of compensation.

The Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) granted defendant Commissioner of Revenue's motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The consumers challenged the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: In addition to their request for recovery, the consumers sought a declaratory judgment that 1991 Tennessee Public Acts 80, § 3 was unconstitutional under the Tennessee and United States Constitutions because it limited the amount of time in which a taxpayer could file a claim for a refund of sales taxes paid on warranty contracts to within 30 days of March 26, 1991. In his motion to dismiss, the Commissioner of Revenue argued that the consumers' complaint lacked of subject matter jurisdiction and failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The trial court held that the consumers lacked standing to bring the suit. On appeal, the court held that the vendor, not the consumers, had standing to sue for the recovery of the taxes and therefore the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.

The order directed clerk to retain a sufficient amount of money out of the sale proceeds to pay certain costs and then to distribute the funds in certain percentages, including a one-third interest to the beneficiary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Harmon


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9306-CV-00252


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 630



September 24, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SEQUATCHIE COUNTY, AT DUNLAP, TENNESSEE. No. 6242. HONORABLE JOHN W. ROLLINS, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county executive and county commissioners, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Sequatchie County (Tennessee), which, in an action by plaintiff State of Tennessee on behalf of relator general sessions court judge seeking payment of a salary supplement to which the judge was allegedly entitled, entered judgment awarding such salary. Defendants argued that under state law the payment of the supplement was not required.


OVERVIEW: The judge was elected to his office as judge of the general sessions court. At the time, the general sessions court did not exercise jurisdiction over domestic relations matters. Years later, while the judge was still in office, the general sessions court was granted jurisdiction over domestic relations matters pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-3-601 (1991). The State on behalf of the judge brought an action against defendants to recover an annual salary supplement to which he was allegedly entitled under Tenn. The trial court entered judgment for the judge, and defendants appealed. The court held that based on a review of the language of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-3-601, it was clear that § 36-2-601 conferred upon the general sessions court jurisdiction to hear domestic relations cases. The court further found that the judge had exercised domestic relations jurisdiction. Thus, he was entitled to the annual salary supplement under Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-15-5003(d)(1)(C).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order entering judgment for the State on behalf of the judge and remanded for the implementation of the trial court's judgment, for the collection of costs assessed to defendants, and for any further necessary proceedings.

Thornton v. Dow Corning Wright Corp.


01A01-9210-CV-00422


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 513



August 4, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 18, 1993. Supplemental Opinion of September 15, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 602.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] SUMNAR COUNTY. HON. THOMAS GOODALL, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; PREVIOUS JUDGMENT REINSTATED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff woman brought an action against defendant, silicone breast implant distributor, seeking damages that she alleged resulted from a defective silicone breast implant distributed by the distributor but manufactured by another. The Circuit Court of Sumnar County (Tennessee) granted the woman's motion to set aside a summary judgment that it previously rendered in favor of the distributor. The distributor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The woman filed her suit more than 11 years after the initial implant. The distributor filed its motion for summary judgment, asserting that the applicable statutes of limitations barred the woman's causes of action. The trial court initially granted the motion without specifying the grounds and then granted the woman's motion to set aside the summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the woman had not met her burden of proof in order to obtain relief under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 60.02(2). Specifically, she failed to show how the distributor's alleged fraudulent conduct, namely its alleged fraudulent concealment about the unreasonable safety risks posed by breast implants, prevented her from timely filing her suit. It was arguable that there may have been grounds for tolling the statute had they been properly raised. However, it was likewise incumbent upon the woman to have raised the issue in a timely manner. In that regard, the record did not show that the woman was misled by the distributor's alleged wrongful acts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and reinstated the summary judgment that was previously entered in favor of the distributor.

State ex rel. Barker v. Harmon


SEQUATCHIE CIRCUIT NO. 01A01-9212-CV-00483


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 483



July 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court of Sequatchie County, Tennessee. The Honorable William H. Inman, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff relator, a general sessions judge, requested a writ of mandamus requiring defendants, a county executive and county commissioners, to resume paying a monthly expense allowance that was authorized under 1983 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 79. The Circuit Court of Sequatchie County (Tennessee) held that the law was unconstitutional, that the doctrine of elision did not apply, and that defendants were not to be reimbursed for amounts already paid.


OVERVIEW: The monthly allowance was paid to plaintiff by a separate check. Plaintiff was not required to document his expenses. The trial court held that the payment was really an increase in salary and was prohibited by Tenn. Const. art. 6, § 7. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded. It reasoned that an act's constitutionality depended on the ultimate end that the legislature intended the act to accomplish. 1983 Tenn. Priv. Acts, ch. 79 provided for the payment of a fixed sum without regard to a judge's actual expenses and was an unconstitutional increase in pay during the term of plaintiff's office. The doctrine of elision applied to save the statute because from the face of the act it appeared that the legislature would have enacted it even if it had known of a raise that was planned for five years later. The doctrine made the statute valid until the legislature provided otherwise and plaintiff was entitled to future monthly payments. Plaintiff was required to reimburse defendants for past monthly allowances because plaintiff did not act in good faith in receiving the supplement.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus. It affirmed in part and held that the statute was unconstitutional. The court reversed in part and held that the doctrine of elision applied to save statute and that plaintiff was entitled to monthly payments. It ordered that plaintiff reimburse defendants for past payments and remanded the case to the trial court.

Bervoets v. Hardy Ralls Pontiac-Olds, Inc.


No. 01A01-9210-CV-00415

OVERVIEW: The vehicle driver filed a third-party complaint against the bar owner after settling the underlying personal injury suit. On appeal, the court held that as a result of that decision, the Act had not been totally abolished, repealed, or found to be unconstitutional. Second, the principles set out in the decision were to be applied prospectively. Third, the court held that upon remand the vehicle driver's third-party claim against the bar owner was to be tried and determined in accordance with the provisions of the Act as written and in accordance with legal principles that existed prior to the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court, ruling that the vehicle driver did state a claim for contribution under the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act and that the Act was still viable after a recent Tennessee Supreme Court decision.

Nale v. Robertson


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9301-CV-00007


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 431



June 18, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTH CIRCUIT COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. A-1722. HONORABLE HARRY S. LESTER, SPECIAL JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the natural father of a child, appealed an order of the Fourth Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which sustained the petition of petitioners, putative adoptive parents, for the adoption of a child born to an unwed mother who surrendered the child to intervenor, the Tennessee Conference of Adoption Services, for adoption. The father also appealed the dismissal of his petition for legitimation.


OVERVIEW: Five days after the child was born, the father filed a notice of intent to claim paternity with the state's Putative Father Registry. The mother wanted to place the child for adoption. Intervenor filed a petition to terminate parental rights and notified the father by mail. He answered and counter-claimed seeking to legitimate the child. Several months later, the adoptive parents filed a petition seeking adoption of the child, a declaration of abandonment, and termination of the parental rights of the father. The father counter-petitioned for legitimation and custody. The court held that the trial court erred in granting the adoption and then dismissing the father's petition. The trial court should have ruled on the pending petition for legitimation prior to ruling on the petition for adoption. The father complied with Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-111(b)(3) by registering his notice of intent to claim paternity with the Putative Father Registry. Having done all he could to legitimize his son, the trial court on remand had to first consider the petition for legitimation, and could deny it only if it found that legitimization would harm the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the trial court's order and remanded with directions for the trial court to first consider and dispose of the father's application to legitimize before considering the application for adoption.

 

1744 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


King-Bradwall Partnership v. Johnson Controls


03A01-9208-CV-00284


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


865 S.W.2d 18; 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 416; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,673



June 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied Septeber 27, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 340.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] HAMBLEN COUNTY. HON. JOHN K. WILSON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motel owners challenged a judgment of the Hamblen County Court (Tennessee) which granted defendant wood product sellers' motion for summary judgment in the motel owners' action for their economic losses resulting from the failure of wood products used in the motel roof. The trial court found that the action was time-barred by Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-28-103 of the Tennessee Products Liability Act of 1978 (Act).


OVERVIEW: More than 10 years after they constructed a motel, the motel owners discovered that the wood products used in the roof had failed. They filed an action against the wood product sellers alleging negligence, failure to warn, breach of warranty, fraudulent misrepresentation, and unfair and deceptive trade practices. The trial court granted the sellers' motions for summary judgment, holding that the action was time-barred by § 29-28-103 of the Act. The motel owners appealed and the court affirmed. The action fell within the definition of products liability contained in the Act at Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-28-102(6) and was therefore barred by the 10-year limitations period. The motel owners had no standing for their claim that the limitations period was unconstitutional for failure to include a savings clause, but even if they did, it was rationally related to the reasonable goal of limiting the time period of liability to allow for reasonable calculation of insurance premiums. Fraudulent concealment did not toll the limitations period because the motel owners did not allege that the sellers knew of their product's defective nature or of potential problems at the motel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to wood product sellers because the action by motel owners for their economic losses from the failure of wood products used in the motel roof was time-barred by the Act's statute of limitations.

 

1745 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Cole Bros. Circus, Inc. v. Huddleston


APP. NO. 01-A-01-9301-CH-00004


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 386



June 4, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT, PART II, FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY TENNESSEE. Docket No. 90-3463-II. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court, Part II, for Davidson County (Tennessee), which upheld the assessment by defendant revenue commissioner that the taxpayer was not entitled to a refund of certain sales and use taxes and penalties that were assessed by the commissioner for the time the taxpayer conducted circus performances in the state.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner assessed sales and use taxes and imposed a penalty on the taxpayer, a circus, for the time it did business in the state. The taxpayer brought an action for a refund, but the trial court upheld the commissioner's assessment. On appeal the taxpayer claimed that its contacts with the state were de minimus and that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-6-203 exempted it from the tax. The court affirmed the judgment below, ruling that under the statutory scheme the use tax was due on the full cost of the items the taxpayer imported into the state and used there. There also was no statutory exception for a de minimus presence. The court also rejected the taxpayer's claim that it was an autonomous operation. The taxpayer used state roads, shopped in state stores, bought advertising space in state newspapers, and was entitled to police and fire protection. The tax was valid because the taxpayer had a substantial nexus within the state, credits were given for duplicative out-of-state payments, all taxpayers were subject to the same taxes, and the tax was reasonably related to the services provided by the state. The penalty was also validly imposed for failure to register as a dealer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which upheld the commissioner's assessment of sales and use taxes on the taxpayer and the imposition of a penalty.

 

1746 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Tennessee Dep't of Corrections


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9212-CH-00496


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 303



April 21, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 91-4140-II. HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged of a judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which dismissed his action regarding the calculation of his sentence reduction credits. He asserted that defendant Tennessee Department of Corrections incorrectly calculated his credits, and violated policies and procedures of law; the Department's Administrative Procedure Act was unconstitutional; and the Department falsified his records.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's complaint stated that "good time laws" were intended to be cumulative, so that inmates should not have been required to waive benefits under former laws in order to qualify for benefits under subsequent laws. Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-236(f)(3) stated that in no event could an inmate receive credits cumulatively under both systems or have received credits at a rate that was less than that provided by the section for felons. That statute was interpreted to prevent "stacking" good time credits provided by successive statutes. The trial judge correctly found as a fact that the inmate had received all the credits to which he was entitled. The court also held that the motion of the Department was properly a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim for which relief could be granted. Except for the "back credits" that were granted to the inmate, the complaint stated no claim for which relief could have been granted, and was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for enforcement of its judgment.

Rice v. Family Planning Clinic for Reproductive Health


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9210-CV-00391


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 265



April 7, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 89C-302 and 89C-3314. THE HONORABLE HAMILTON GAYDEN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which denied recovery in her action against defendants, clinic and physician, in her medical malpractice action in connection with an abortion in the second trimester of her pregnancy. The patient raised issues on the evidence, the jury instruction, and the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-4-201 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The patient brought a medical malpractice action against the clinic and the physician after an abortion and the jury returned a verdict for the clinic and the physician. The patient challenged the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-4-201 et seq. in a motion for a new trial, which the trial court overruled. The patient sought review. The court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) the patient was not entitled to a jury charge that violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-201 was negligence per se; (2) the patient had a choice to continue the action until the constitutionality issue was resolved but elected to go to trial and could not complain, Tenn. R. App. Proc. 36(a); (3) under Tenn. R. Evid. § 618, the physician's lawyer was properly allowed to refer to a treatise in the impeachment of an expert witness; (4) under Tenn. R. Evid. 403, the trial court properly determined the admissibility of evidence against the clinic, which did not appear at trial; (5) the physician properly highlighted excerpts from a voluminous exhibit; and (6) error could not be predicated on the exclusion of evidence unless the proponent made an offer of proof, Tenn. R. Evid. 103(a)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the clinic and physician in the patient's medical malpractice action and remanded the cause for any further necessary proceedings, and taxed the costs on appeal against the patient.

Taylor v. Neil


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9211-CH-00439


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 195



March 17, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 1, 1993. Petition to Rehear Denied April 16, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 270.
Rehearing denied by Taylor v. Neil, 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 270 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 16, 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY, AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 92-1159-I. HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR
State v. Taylor, 668 S.W.2d 681, 1984 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 2498 (Tenn. Crim. App., 1984)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which dismissed the inmate's petition seeking disclosure of public records from defendants, a court clerk and an attorney general, under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 10-7-503, 10-7-505 and the Freedom of Information Act, 5 U.S.C.S § 552. The chancery court held that the inmate failed to state a claim for which relief could have been granted.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted and sentenced to life imprisonment on a charge of second-degree murder. The minute entry of his conviction stated that defendant was rendered "infamous" by his crime. The inmate filed a petition seeking disclosure of public documents in the possession of the court clerk and the attorney general. The chancery court entered a judgment dismissing the inmate's petition on the ground that he failed to state a claim for which relief could have been granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that (1) under the Tennessee Public Records Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 10-7-503, public records were available to any "citizen of Tennessee"; (2) the inmate's second-degree murder conviction involved an infamous crime that rendered him infamous, which disqualified the inmate from exercising the right of suffrage; (3) an unrestored felon was not a "citizen of Tennessee" within the meaning of § 10-7-503; and (4) the Freedom of Information Act, 5 U.S.C.S. § 552, was a federal statute that had no application to state records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the inmate's petition seeking disclosure of public records. The court remanded the action to the chancery court for collection of the cost of the appeal.

Reid v. State


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9210-CH-00414


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 200



March 17, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 92-1209-II. HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed a judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which granted defendant State's motion to dismiss the inmate's action for a declaratory judgment that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-123(b)(i) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: While on a work release program, the inmate committed a felony to which he pleaded guilty. Pursuant to § 40-28-23(b)(1), his parole eligibility was revoked. On appeal of the granting of the State's motion to dismiss the declaratory judgment action, the court noted that the inmate received procedural due process in the proceeding wherein he was convicted of a felony. The remainder was mandated by the statute, and the inmate pointed out no advantage that could have accrued to him through some empty compliance with due process where no issues were available to be raised and resolved. The inmate did not deny his conviction or challenge the revocation of his work release. His only complaint was the alteration of his parole eligibility date. As to the process of recomputing the time of discharge, the inmate had the adequate relief of the Administrative Procedure Act and judicial review of the decision. Though the inmate asserted his right to the advice of counsel before signing a document leading to his work release, the result of sustaining the complaint would have been the invalidation of the document, which was not required by statute or indispensable to the validity of the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded for collection of costs from the inmate.

 

1750 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Long v. Blount County Election Comm'n


C/A NO. 03A01-9208-CH-00290


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


854 S.W.2d 894; 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 159



February 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied June 1, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 217.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CHANCERY COURT. BLOUNT COUNTY. HON. CHESTER S. RAINWATER, JR., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff constables challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Blount County (Tennessee) that held that a 1991 amendment to Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-10-101 was not special legislation in violation of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8.


OVERVIEW: The constables filed an action to review a 1991 amendment to Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-10-101, which abolished the office of constable in counties with a population between 77,700 and 77,800 people. The constables claimed that the amendment singled out their county in violation of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8, which prohibited special legislation. The chancellor entered a judgment holding that the amendment was constitutional. Affirming and remanding, the court found that the amendment did not violate § 8 because there was no general mandatory law or uniform state policy that the challenged amendment contravened. The constables alleged only that the amendment was unconstitutional without pointing to a statute that had been violated by the amendment's terms. The argument that the amendment applied solely to their county was not entirely accurate because other counties could subsequently fall within the population limits of the amendment. The statute as a whole was a "crazy guilt of differing provisions" on the existence and tenure of constables throughout Tennessee. There was no general "rule," only exceptions applying to various counties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of constitutionality.

 

1751 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Morris v. Snodgrass


No. 02A01-9250-CH-00149


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


871 S.W.2d 484; 1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 129



February 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Chancery Court. Shelby County. Hon. D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials were granted permission by the chancellor and the court to file an interlocutory appeal pursuant to Tenn. R. App. P. 9 from an order of the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied their motion to dismiss pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02 for improper venue. Plaintiff county officials sought a declaratory judgment holding that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-25-129, 55-10-403 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county officials alleged that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 55-10-403, 40-25-129 violated Tenn. Const. art. II, § 24 because the state failed to share the proper amount of increased county expenditures imposed by the statutes. The state officials argued that as heads of their respective state departments, proper venue was in Davidson County. The county officials argued that the action was a transitory one, so Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-4-101(a) controlled. The county officials' reliance on § 20-4-101 was misplaced, because Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-4-104, as interpreted for many years, established venue for suits against state officials in Davidson County. Such actions were not transitory, but local in nature. Even if Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-4-101 could apply, it was only a general statute, and Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-4-104 controlled as a statute of specific nature. The county officials also argued that § 4-4-104 governed only claims under the Administrative Procedures Act and merely fixed and defined the official residence of state agencies and officials. No authority was cited for this blanket statement, which the court rejected. The court reversed the judgment and dismissed the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the chancellor's decree denying the motion to dismiss for improper venue and dismissed the county officials' action.

Hardin County v. Adamsville


NO. 02A01-9203-CH-00084


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1993 Tenn. App. LEXIS 60



January 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Hardin County, Tennessee. The Honorable Joe Morris, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a county and some citizens, appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court of Hardin County (Tennessee) in favor of defendants, a city, a mayor, some commissioners, and an attorney general, and third-party defendant State. After a remand to the proper court, the trial court dismissed plaintiffs' case that sought to enjoin defendants from passing an annexation ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The county that was to be annexed incorporated itself into a town after the city had started annexation proceedings. The city had not given the county notice of its intent to hold the annexation proceedings nor a chance to vote to the issue. The court upheld the propriety of the annexation and held that the incorporation was invalid. The court found that (1) an annexing city was not required, under either the state or federal constitution, to give notice of and the right to vote on a proposed annexation to citizens within the proposed area of annexation when that area was in a contiguous county; (2) the procedural due process provided to the citizens of a territory that was the subject of a proposed annexation was the right to bring a quo warranto action to contest the validity of the annexation; (3) the federal constitution did not afford the county citizens the right to vote on or the right to notice of a proposed annexation; (4) a subsequent incorporation of a town did not take priority over another town's pending annexation ordinance; and (5) the "first in time rule" applied to incorporation and annexation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Williams v. State, Dep't of Safety


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9206-CH-00250


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


854 S.W.2d 102; 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 972



December 2, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. No. 90-3887-I



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owner sought review of a judgment by the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, which affirmed the administrative decision of the commissioner of respondent, the State of Tennessee, Department of Safety, directing the forfeiture of the owner's automobile after police found cocaine inside the vehicle.


OVERVIEW: The owner and a female passenger were in his automobile parked in the lot of a night club. The police officers noticed the automobile's occupants were in an argument. When the officer knocked on the window, the owner opened the door and the officer saw a whiskey bottle. The owner produced his license and consented to a search of the automobile. The officer found cocaine in a compartment in the driver's door and arrested the owner. The trial court affirmed the commissioner's decision to forfeit the automobile. On appeal, the court held that drugs previously discovered in other vehicles in the same parking lot did not constitute probable cause for the actions of the officers. The court noted that the owner's automobile was legally parked on private property and that there was no reason for the officer to intervene in a non-violent argument of its occupants. Because the "stop and search" was without reasonable suspicion, the fruits of the search were inadmissible and the forfeiture was unsupported. Reversing the judgment of the trial court and vacating the decision of the commissioner, the court taxed costs against the commissioner and remanded the case for collection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and vacated the commissioner's decision to forfeit the owner's automobile. Taxing costs against the commissioner, the court remanded the case for collection.

Lee v. Ellis


No. 01A01-9206-CV-00230


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 940



November 18, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Fifth Circuit Court for Davidson County. Honorable Walter C. Kurtz, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the judgment from the Fifth Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee mother in the mother's paternity action, alleging that the father was the natural father of her child.


OVERVIEW: After the mother told the father that she was pregnant, the father broke off their relationship and had no communications with her. The mother than moved in with another man whom she later married after the birth of her son. The other man was listed as the father on the birth certificate. After the mother divorced the other man, she filed her paternity petition against the father. A blood test indicated that the father was most likely the father of the child. The jury found in favor of the mother and the father appealed. In affirming, the court held that the mother's testimony was clearly a willful contradiction of that given in her divorce proceeding from the other man and her testimony that the father was the father of her child should have been excluded by the trial court. However, the evidence was probably more helpful to the father than harmful. The inconsistent testimony was presented to the jury and thus considered by the jury in terms of the mother's credibility. Further, she was still able to testify as to the sexual relationship between herself and the father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the judgment from the trial court.

Underwood v. Webber


C/A NO. 03A01-9206-CH-213


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 817



October 8, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHANCERY COURT. ANDERSON COUNTY. HON. WILLIAM E. LANTRIP, CHANCELLOR



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVISED IN PART, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a decision of the Chancery Court of Anderson County (Tennessee), which, in his action for a breach of employment contract, determined that the employee had not completed three years of employment as a supervisor, so was not entitled to tenure for his work for defendants, a school board and superintendent of schools.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a supervisor and an employee-at-will of the board until he signed his first yearly employment contract. More than two years later, in December 1986, the superintendent offered the employee the position of maintenance foreman at the same salary. The employee agreed, but when the board transferred him to the new position, his salary was drastically reduced. In his action for breach of his employment contract, the trial court determined that he had not completed three years of employment as a supervisor, so was not entitled to tenure under the Private Tenure Act, 1941 Tenn. Priv. Acts ch. 465. On appeal, the court affirmed the part of the trial court's decision holding that the employee's transfer became effective when the board approved the superintendent's recommendation, in December 1986, so he had served approximately two weeks less than three years as a supervisor. The court reversed and remanded, however, with respect to the breach of the employee's 1986-1987 contract, finding that it appeared beyond dispute that the employee was not demoted for cause and had not agreed to a reduction in pay, so he was entitled to submit proof of damages as to the breach.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the employee was not entitled to tenure, but reversed on the issue of the board's breach of the employee's contract and remanded for proof of damages from the breach.

Pierson v. Carobene


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9204-CV-00141


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 839



October 2, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 91C-2253. HONORABLE HAMILTON GAYDEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which dismissed her suit against defendant state employer, Superintendent of the Middle Tennessee Mental Health Institute, for wrongful discharge from state employment.


OVERVIEW: The state employee filed a suit against the state employer for a declaration that certain state policies were unconstitutional, that she was wrongfully discharged, that she be reinstated with back pay, and that she be provided a due process hearing on her discharge. The state employer filed a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim and a summary judgment. The circuit court granted the state employer's motion to dismiss on the merits. On appeal, the state employee asserted that the circuit court committed reversible error by granting the state employer's motion to dismiss. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The court held that: (1) the circuit court had no jurisdiction of a challenge to a state regulation prior to the exhaustion of administrative remedies; (2) whether the state employee was a permanent civil service employee entitled to a hearing before discharge or a probationary employee dischargeable without a hearing was subject to review by the appropriate state agency before the state employee could seek relief in the courts; and (3) because of sovereign immunity, relief the nature of reinstatement and back pay was available only as provided by statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment dismissing the state employee's wrongful discharge suit.

 

1757 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Newton v. Cox


No. 02A01-9202-CH-000041


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 758



September 14, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Chancery Court. Shelby County. No. 95025-3. Hon. Joe C. Morris, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former client filed an action against defendant attorney in the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) and alleged that the attorney charged him a contingent fee in excess of the statutory maximum. He also alleged a violation of consumer protection law. The attorney general intervened. The trial court entered a judgment in the attorney's favor and the former client and attorney general appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the statute regarding contingent fees, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-120, was unconstitutional because it violated the Due Process and Equal Protection clauses of the U.S. and the Tennessee Constitutions and the separation of powers provision of the Tennessee Constitution, and that the Tennessee Consumer Protection Act ("Act"), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-101, et seq. did not apply to the practice of law and was time-barred. The former client and attorney general alleged error. The court held that § 29-26-120 did not apply to or control the conduct of individual attorneys, but was directed to the judiciary. As for the claim asserted under the Act, the court opined that the Act did not apply, but if it did, by the terms of the Act itself the action was time-barred. The court further held that the trial court erred in allowing into evidence opinion testimony of an active and a retired judge as to the constitutionality of § 29-26-120. Thus, the court reversed as to the declaration that § 29-26-120 was unconstitutional, but otherwise affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order declaring the provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-120 to be unconstitutional and, in all other respects, affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Warren v. Scott


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9203-CH-00093


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


845 S.W.2d 780; 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 779



September 4, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF MAURY COUNTY AT COLUMBIA, TENNESSEE. No. 90-623. THE HONORABLE WILLIAM DENDER, JUDGE, SITTING BY DESIGNATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court of Maury County at Columbia (Tennesse), which denied his application for certification of his case as a class action and held that his claim was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court clerk, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 18-5-106(a), was charged with holding and disbursing funds from the condemnation of property in which plaintiff had an interest. Plaintiff sought to bring a class action under 42 U.S.C. § 1983, alleging that the clerk had deprived him of the interest earned on his money without due process of law. Plaintiff claimed to represent a class of persons whose funds were held by the courts against a defendant's class comprised of all court clerks in the state. The complaint also alleged that the clerk violated his duty as a trustee of the funds by diverting the interest to the county general fund. The appellate court held that (1) the court below had correctly surmised that the composition of the proposed class was too greatly varied to permit certification as a class; (2) the one-year statute of limitations began to run when plaintiff received the funds from the clerk, and his action commencing more than a year later had thus expired; and (3) the clerk operating under the authorization of § 18-5-106(a) to keep the interest earned from funds invested as part of the fees of the office did not violate a fiduciary duty to plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court held that the circuit court did not violate a fiduciary duty to plaintiff by keeping the interest earned from plaintiff's money. The judgment of the court below was affirmed.
