Turner v. Moss


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9206-CH-00218


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 749



August 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Denied September 23, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 771.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF MARION COUNTY, TENNESSEE, AT JASPER. HONORABLE JEFFREY F. STEWART, CHANCELLOR. No. 5540



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a county executive, sought review of an order from the Chancery Court of Marion County at Jasper (Tennessee), which authorized plaintiff, a county register, to increase the salary and expenses of certain employees of her office and which ordered the executive to pay for the increase out of the county general funds.


OVERVIEW: The register sought to compel the executive to pay an increase in the expenses of her office, including an increase in the salary of the chief deputy and deputy clerks and expenses related thereto. On appeal, the court held that, under the statutory law, the trial court erred in mandating the payment of the approved expenses out of the country treasury. The register was not permitted to receive more than the statutory minimum salary, regardless of her need for a deputy or an assistant. The register had to pay any expenses deemed necessary for her office with the fees collected by her office or out of her statutory minimum compensation. The evidence showed that during a one and a half-year period the total fees collected by the register did not meet or exceed her expenses and that she was operating the office at a deficit. The fees collected by her office were not sufficient to pay the approved salaries; therefore, under statutory law, the executor could not have been compelled to supplement fees except to the extent of the register's minimum compensation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1760 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


O'Brien v. Bainbridge


APP. NO. 01-A-01-9201-PB-00002


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 565



July 8, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE PROBATE COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE JAMES R. EVERETT, JR., JUDGE. Docket No. R 6990



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed a decision of the Probate Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which dismissed her petition for support against defendant father filed pursuant to the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act (URESA), 1992 Tenn. Acts ch. 1013.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered an order dismissing the URESA petition for lack of jurisdiction. The order stated that it was without jurisdiction under the URESA statutes to determine paternity for the purpose of establishing a duty of support and then to enforce that duty. The mother argued that a duty of support, including a determination of paternity, could have been established in a consolidated action initiated under URESA. The court agreed concluding that at all times relevant to the case, the father's paternity of the minor child could have been properly established in an action brought pursuant to in-state procedures set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-101, et seq. The court stated that under 1992 Tenn. Acts ch. 1013, it was equally clear that the case could have been maintained under the URESA statutes as well. The court further concluded that retrospective application of ch. 1013 would not have violated the father's right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment.

 

1761 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Lee's Home Center, Inc. v. Akins


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9202-CH-00047


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 492



June 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Chancery Court. Robertson County. No. 11489.

Original Opinion of June 3, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 480.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the court reversed an order of The Chancery Court of Robertson County (Tennessee) holding against defendant homeowners in plaintiff materialman's action to recover costs of materials ordered by a general contractor, the court reconsidered its opinion in view of a prior opinion on the same issues involving the materialman and another party.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners hired a general contractor to build on their property. The contractor purchased materials from the materialman, who made deliveries of materials. The materialman later sued the homeowners to recover costs of the materials. The trial court held for the materialman. On appeal, the court reversed. The court subsequently agreed to reconsider its opinion after it was brought to the court's attention that a conflict might exist between its opinion and a prior opinion involving the materialman and another party. The court noted that in the prior case, the court held that the materialman acquired liens on a homeowner's property under Tenn. Code Ann. § 66-11-115 (1982) pursuant to its contract with the general contractor to furnish materials; thus, the materialman had a vested right under § 66-11-115 as it existed prior to amendment of mechanic's lien laws. The court found that in the instant case, the record did not show any contract between the materialman and the contractor; however, the materialman claimed a valid contract. The court thus vacated the trial court's ruling and remanded for a determination based on evidence of a contract predating the amendments.


OUTCOME: The court issued a supplemental opinion vacating the trial court's order, remanding for a determination of the value of materials delivered pursuant to a contract or contracts entered into by the materialman and the general contractor on or before a certain date, and ordering entry of a judgment authorizing enforcement of the materialman' lien against the homeowner's property based on evidence of such a contract or contracts.

 

1762 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Tennessee Small School Systems v. McWherter


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9111-CH-00433


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 486



June 5, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 10, 1992.
Reversed by, Remanded by Tennessee Small Sch. Sys. v. McWherter, 851 S.W.2d 139, 1993 Tenn. LEXIS 114 (Tenn., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. No. 88-1812-II. HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, DISMISSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed the declaratory judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which held that Tennessee's public education funding system, which generated funds pursuant to the Education Finance Act, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 49-3-301, et seq., and the Distribution of Locally Assessed Sales Tax, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-6-712, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The lower court held that Tennessee's system for funding education violated the equal protection requirements of the state's constitution. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the education clause of the constitution, Tenn. Const. Art. XI, § 12, required the general assembly to provide for a system of free public schools, not actually provide them. By provide for, the court explained that the general assembly had a constitutional duty to enact laws governing the standards of a system of public schools. Under the general assembly's fragmented system, which was operated by state and local government, achieving an exact equality of education was impossible, but the principle of fairness should apply. The court held that the state constitution did not guarantee that every child in every county would receive an education exactly equal to that received by children in all other counties. While it may be true that some children did not have access to the required opportunities, the school districts presented no evidence as to the officials, regulations or laws which denied the access, and the court could not grant relief without evidence of the producing cause of the denial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court which held that Tennessee's public education funding system violated the equal protection requirements of the state constitution and dismissed the action, and remanded the action for the collection of trial court costs.

 

1763 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cordova Area Residents for Environment v. City of Memphis


02A01-9109-CH-00212


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


862 S.W.2d 525; 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 361



April 24, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Chancery Court of Shelby County, Tennessee. The Honorable Floyd Peete, Jr., Chancellor



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens' group sought a quo warranto petition in the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) that contested the annexation ordinance adopted by appellee city. The group proceeded in the matter on the relation of the State of Tennessee. The trial court found that the group lacked standing to bring the action and dismissed the suit. The group sought review.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted an annexation ordinance that concerned about a 455 acre tract in the county. No member of the group, which consisted of residents and homeowners of the county, owned land within the property subject to the annexation ordinance. The trial court found that as bordering landowners, the group had no standing. Upon review, the court found that the only property owners that were allowed to contest the annexation ordinance by way of a quo warranto proceeding as described in Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103 were those whose property was within the annexed area. The group argued that it commenced its suit under the general quo warranto statute at Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-35-101 et seq. and that they were not suing the city as adjoining landowners but as representatives of the State, which gave them standing. The court held that the annexation statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103, provided the exclusive means to challenge an annexation ordinance. The group's action could only lie by way of that statute, and they had no standing to bring such an action under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the group did not have standing to challenge the city's annexation ordinance.

 

1764 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Abernathy v. Whitley


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9112-CH-00469


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


838 S.W.2d 211; 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 364



April 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Rehear Overruled May 8, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 413.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY, AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR. No. 91-1891-III



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of an order of the Chancery Court Of Davidson County (Tennessee), which denied that part of her petition against defendant attorney general that sought investigative records of the Tennessee Bureau of Investigation (TBI) and denied her request for attorney's fees. The individual sought access to public records regarding the prosecution of another individual, pursuant to the Tennessee Public Records Act.


OVERVIEW: The trial court allowed the individual access to the public records she requested except those belonging to the TBI. She contended that Tenn. Code Ann. § 10-7-504(a)(2), which exempted the TBI's investigative records from disclosure and investigation constituted a prohibited restraint on the public's right to public records in violation of Tenn. Const. art. I, §§ 8 and 19. On appeal the court affirmed because the statute was constitutional and the individual was not due attorney's fees. The court found that there was no generally recognized state or federal constitutional right of access to public records. The individual's right to examine public records arose from the statute. The court found that the court properly denied the individual's request for attorney's fees pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 10-7-505(g) because that section granted fees to a claimant only when a governmental entity wilfully refused to disclose a public record. The attorney general's position with regard to the individual's request was consistent with that of the state in a pending appeal regarding the availability of the records, thus the attorney general's denial was not wilful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny the individual's request for TBI investigative records pursuant to the state public records act and to deny the individual an award of attorney's fees. Costs of the appeal were taxed against the individual and the cause was remanded to the trial court for the collection of costs.

James v. State, Dep't of Correction


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9110-CH-00376


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 331



April 8, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR. No. 90-3440-II



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant correctional officer sought review of a decision from the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee) which affirmed the civil service commission's denial of the officer's grievance that sought attorney's fees and back pay.


OVERVIEW: The correctional officer was indicted for aggravated rape of his five-year old son. Respondent correction facility terminated the officer because his effectiveness as a correctional officer was impaired by the charges. The charges were retired and he was hired at another state correctional facility. The trial court affirmed the commission's denial of the officer's request for attorney's fees and back pay. The court stated that there was substantial and material evidence in the record that supported a conclusion that the charge against the officer had adversely affected his ability to do his job. The court stated that there were no errors that affected the validity of the process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the correctional officer's request for attorney's fees and back pay.

 

1766 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Lee's Home Center, Inc. v. Hoy


No. 01A01-9112-CH00464


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 332



April 8, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Robertson County Chancery Court at Springfield. Honorable Alex W. Darnell, Judge



DISPOSITION: VACATED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed the order from the Robertson County Chancery Court at Springfield (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment enforcing the materialmen's liens filed against the property owner's land by plaintiff materialmen and awarded the materialmen personal judgments against the property owners.


OVERVIEW: The property owners entered into a contract with a general contractor for the construction of a single-family dwelling. The general contractor then contracted with the materialmen to furnish the necessary materials. When the general contractor filed bankruptcy prior to paying the materialmen, they filed materialmen's liens against the property owners' land and sought to enforce the liens. The trial court granted summary judgments for the materialmen enforcing their liens and awarding them personal judgments. The court vacated the personal judgments and, otherwise, affirmed the judgments. Under their contracts with the general contractor, and, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 66-11-115 (1982), the materialmen acquired liens on the property, which, by virtue of Tenn. Code Ann. § 66-11-104 (1982), attached as of the date of the visible commencement of operations. Thus, the materialmen had vested rights under the law as it existed prior to July 1, 1990, and the 1990 amendments to the law, codified at Tenn. Code Ann. § 66-11-146 (Supp. 1990), did not divest them of those rights. Because the materialmen did not have contracts with the property owners, the personal judgments were erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court vacated that portion of the trial court's order, which awarded the materialmen personal judgments against the property owners. In all other respects, the order was affirmed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for any further proceedings deemed necessary.

Huntsville Utility Dist. of Scott County v. General Trust Co.


APP. No. 01-A-01-9108-CH-00295, Docket No. 90-1610-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


839 S.W.2d 397; 1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 238



March 6, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE CHANCERY COURT, PART I, FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY, TENNESSEE. THE HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff utility filed a declaratory action against defendants, registrar, attorney general, and utility's customer, to have a legislative act declared unconstitutional. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee dismissed the action. The utility appealed.


OVERVIEW: The utility and registrar entered into a fiscal agency agreement to have the utility's bonds re-financed. The bond resolution required that there was to be no change in how the utility's board members were to be elected. The legislature passed an act to change the board's size and method of selection. The utility filed an action to have the Act declared unconstitutional. Although the registrar admitted that the act was unconstitutional, the attorney general contended that indispensable parties had to be joined. The court affirmed the dismissal of the action because the utility failed to join indispensable parties. Because the right of the customers to elect their own utility board members was to be affected, they were indispensable parties. Also, the bondholders were indispensable parties because their rights were to have been affected. Because the registrar had no authority to enforce the bond resolution, there would have been no parties to enforce the bondholders' rights under the resolution. As a result, the relief would have been incomplete without the bondholders' joinder. The names of the bondholders were not confidential under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 9-19-109, 10-7-504.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the utility's claim to have declared unconstitutional a legislative act which changed how the utility's board was elected.

Drake v. Tennessee Dep't of Corrections


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9109-CH-00332


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1992 Tenn. App. LEXIS 45



January 17, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY, TENNESSEE. AT NASHVILLE. HONORABLE C. ALLEN HIGH, CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 90-1452-II



DISPOSITION: MODIFIED, AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tennessee Supreme Court transferred to the court the record of petitioner inmate's appeal from a judgment of a trial court, which dismissed the inmate's petition for writ of certiorari to review an agency decision. Defendants were the Tennessee Department of Corrections (TDC) and others.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a petition for writ of certiorari to review an agency decision, seeking review of a disciplinary board decision and the resulting decision of the TDC in delaying the inmate's date of eligibility for release. No copy or details of the decisions were furnished in or with the petition. The court found that the petition did not allege that the TDC had exceeded its jurisdiction, or that it had acting illegally and there was no other plain, speedy, or adequate remedy, or that the TDC was acting in a judicial capacity. Thus, the court held that the petition failed to state a ground for issuance of the writ of certiorari.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court to provide that all costs were taxed against the inmate, for which execution was to issue. As modified, the judgment was affirmed. The case was remanded for such further proceedings, if any, as were necessary and proper.

Sprint Petroleum, Inc. v. Collierville Beer Bd.


NO. 02A01-9106-CV-00104


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 981



December 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court of Shelby County, Tennessee. The Honorable Robert A. Lanier, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which upheld a decision from defendant City of Collierville, Tennessee, in which the City refused to issue the applicant an off-premises beer permit. The applicant was first refused by the City's Beer Board, and then by the City's Mayor and Board of Aldermen. The applicant sought review in the trial court by a statutory writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The applicant owned property 271 feet from a church, and the Beer Board refused to issue the applicant a permit for an off-premises beer license, pursuant to the City's beer ordinance, Collierville, TN., City Ordinance 88-29 § 2-211(12), because the applicant's place of business was within 500 feet of a church. The decision was upheld by the Mayor and Board of Aldermen, and thereafter, the applicant presented a proposed amendment to the beer ordinance to change the mode of measuring distances between properties, which proposal was rejected by the Beer Board and the Mayor and Board of Aldermen. The applicant sought review of the denial of the permit, and the trial court upheld the decision. The applicant appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that the beer ordinance was constitutional and had not been discriminatorily applied to the applicant. The court determined that similar businesses within close proximity to churches had valid off-premises beer permits by virtue of the beer ordinance's grandfather clause and that because the beer ordinance's distance requirement was promulgated under the authority of a valid statute, the beer ordinance itself was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which upheld a decision by the City, in which it refused to issue the applicant an off-premises beer permit. The court taxed costs of the appeal to the applicant.

Clay County Manor, Inc. v. State, Dep't of Health & Environment


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9106-CH-00228


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 984



December 13, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT OF DAVIDSON COUNTY, TENNESSEE AT NASHVILLE. HONORABLE IRVIN H. KILCREASE, JR., CHANCELLOR. Davidson Chancery No. 89-3203-I



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursing home sought review of the judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which affirmed the action of the Tennessee Board for Licensing Health Care Facilities in continuing a suspension of admissions against the nursing home until certain specified conditions were met.


OVERVIEW: Following several complaints against the nursing home regarding conditions there and the standard of care given to patients, the board attempted an inspection which the nursing home staff refused. Sanctions were imposed and the nursing home filed suit against appellee, Tennessee Department of Health and Environment. The court held that (1) the nursing home was part of a pervasively regulated industry, and therefore was not immune to warrantless searches, (2) the underlying cause or justification for the questioned inspection was the general responsibility of the Department of Health and Environment to protect the health, safety and welfare of the patients, (3) the statement made by the nursing home's representative which terminated the inspection was unjustified and constituted a general refusal to be inspected, and (4) absent a showing of specific danger to patients resulting from the refusal, suspension of admissions was not available as a device to compel submission to inspection.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the order of the board continuing a suspension of admissions against the nursing home was vacated.

Cofer v. Industrial Dev. Bd.


C/A No. 03A01-9107-CH-00228


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Eastern Section


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 895



November 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court, Roane County, Hon. Frank V. Williams, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed suit against defendants, a factory owner and a county industrial development board, alleging that the board's composition was unconstitutional and that it had no right to pursue an environmentally unsound course of action. The taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court of Roane County (Tennessee), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The owner wanted to convert the factory into a hazardous waste reclamation center. The board authorized the issuance of industrial revenue bonds to finance the operation. The complaint alleged that the board's composition from members of civic organizations was unconstitutional and that its financial support of the proposed operation contradicted its anti-pollution mandate. None of the owner's current activities were alleged to have harmed the taxpayer, and the complaint alleged no specific injury to him resulting from the board's action. The gravamen of the complaint was that once the factory was converted to its proposed use, it might again become a nuisance. That argument was directed at the owner and the court ruled that it stated no cause of action. The taxpayer simply sought to forestall a speculative wrong that had not occurred by attacking the legitimacy of the alleged future wrongdoers' financier. The taxpayer lacked standing to sue the board for its issuance of the bonds because the issuance alone did not impact him differently from other taxpayers. The taxpayer's constitutional attack was waived pursuant to Tenn. R. App. P. 27(a)(7) because it was unsupported.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case.

Anderson County v. Remote Landfill Services, Inc.


CA No. 03A01-9106-CH-215


Court of Appeals of Tennessee


833 S.W.2d 903; 1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 852



October 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied March 30, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 296.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Chancery Court, Anderson County, Hon. William E. Lantrip, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, DISMISSED, AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landfill company sought review of a decision of the Chancery Court, Anderson County (Tennessee), which enjoined it from further development of its sanitary landfill until it received approval of the governing board of the county pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-33-103.


OVERVIEW: The county filed an action to enjoin the landfill company from further development of its sanitary landfill in the county. The trial court ruled for the county holding that the landfill company was enjoined from further development until it received approval of the governing body of the county, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-33-103. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the landfill company had received the required approval of the governing body through its Planning Commission and its Board of Zoning Appeals. The court found that the record showed that the landfill company had complied with all of the requirements of the County Zoning Ordinance and Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-33-101, et seq., except it had not gone before the governing body of the county to secure additional approval. The court held that it was error for the trial court to find that approval could not be given for the location of the landfill by an administrative agency of the governing body, the Board of Zoning Appeals, but that consent could be given only by the governing body because a governing body may delegate administrative powers to a planning commission or a board of zoning appeals.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had enjoined the landfill company from further development of its sanitary landfill until it received approval of the governing board of the county.

Clark v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville & Davidson County


Court of Appeals No. 01-A-01-9104-CV-00151


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


827 S.W.2d 312; 1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 815



October 11, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Second Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee, No. 90C-3399, Honorable Marietta M. Shipley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen sought review of the decision of the Second Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which denied her petition for certiorari wherein she sought interlocutory relief from a Metropolitan General Sessions Court's decision that allowed respondent government to amend an affidavit supporting a citation.


OVERVIEW: The citizen was issued a citation for interfering with a police officer in violation of Metropolitan Code § 34-1-1. Thereafter, the citizen filed a motion to dismiss the charge on the ground that there were defects in the citation. The government filed a motion to amend the affidavit supporting the citation, and the Session Court's granted its request. The citizen then filed her interlocutory appeal challenging the Session Court's decision on the ground that the Session Court erred when it allowed the government to amend the affidavit supporting the citation. The court held that the original affidavit was constitutionally sufficient to bring the citizen's actions within the scope of Metropolitan Code § 34-1-1. Moreover, the court held that the original affidavit gave the citizen sufficient notice of the charge against her. Furthermore, the court held that the amended affidavit filed did not change the nature of the offense or add a new offense. Therefore, the court found that trial court properly denied the citizen's petition because the Session Court was correct in allowing the government to amend the affidavit to the citation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision and remanded the cause for collection of costs.

Shaw v. Tennessee Bd. of Architectural & Engineering Examiners

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff engineer appealed from the decision of the Chancery Court of Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which affirmed the decision of the state's board of architecture and engineering (board), which revoked the engineer's license to practice engineering, and which found him guilty of violating Tenn. Code Ann. § 62-2-306(b) and Tenn. Code Ann. § 62-2-308(a) (1)(B).


OVERVIEW: The engineer used plans and drawings prepared by other persons, none of whom had a relationship with the engineer. The board determined that the engineer had violated Tenn. Code Ann. § 62-2-306(b) and § 62-2-308(a)(1)(B) by acts of gross negligence, incompetence and misconduct. The board also charged him with violating its rule 0120-2-.03 by affixing his seal to a document dealing with subject matter outside his competence; and violating Rule 0120-2-.02 of its rules by failing to recognize his primary obligation to protect safety, health and welfare of the public. After a hearing, the board found the engineer guilty. The trial court affirmed that decision on appeal. The engineer appealed and the court affirmed. Code Ann. § 4-5-322(h). The court held that the engineer's constitutional rights had not been violated, and that the plans that he had approved contained several deficiencies which, to the knowledgeable members of the board, indicated incompetence.

Crites v. Smith


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9101-CH-00002


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


826 S.W.2d 459; 1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 721



September 4, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied February 24, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court of Davidson County, Tennessee at Nashville; No. 89-2824-I; Honorable Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents filed an 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendant board of education seeking designation as a class action, a declaration that the "practices and policies" of the board of education were unconstitutional and in violation of civil rights, and injunctive relief. The Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed the parents' suit. The parents sought review of the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The parents wanted to teach their children at home rather than send them to a public or private school for instruction. Section 49-6-3050(b) of the Tennessee Code required that a parent teacher conducting a home school must comply with certain requirements. As a result of § 49-6-3050(b), four parents that lacked the required degree were denied exemption from the degree requirement. Two other parents were denied a variation of the deadline reporting requirement. The court affirmed and held that the trial court did not err in its finding that the commissioner's blanket denial of all requests for statutory waiver of the baccalaureate degree requirement was not arbitrary, capricious, or unconstitutional. Next, the court held that trial court did not err in refusing to find that the commissioner's rigid enforcement of the reporting deadline did not result in a denial of the rights to travel and did not violate the standards of equal protection. Moreover, the court held that trial court did not err in refusing to certify as two classes of plaintiffs those requesting waivers from the bachelor's degree requirement and those seeking relief from the notice requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision dismissing the parents' case.

 

1777 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Crown Colony Homeowners Ass'n v. Ramsey


CA No. 293


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Knoxville


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 609



August 7, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Sullivan County, Tennessee; The Honorable Richard E. Ladd, Chancellor. 



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association appealed a decision by the Chancery Court of Sullivan County (Tennessee), which held that defendant county commission's passage of the resolution rezoning defendant landowner's property was a valid legislative act and dismissed the association's complaint to have rescinded and declared null and void a resolution passed by the county commission rezoning the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The association contended that the resolution was unconstitutional because it was spot zoning, it was a legislative action solely for the landowner's gain rather than for the public welfare, and it was arbitrary and capricious. The court found that the resolution changed the zoning of the landowner's property to a business zoning, but left the surrounding property zoned residential. However, since the passage of that ordinance, numerous lots on the Highway 11-W corridor had been rezoned for business use, the nearest being approximately 0.4 miles from the association. Thus, there was a growing trend toward business zoning in the area surrounding the association. The evidence demonstrated a growing trend toward business zoning along Highway 11-W in the area surrounding the association and, therefore, the court found that the resolution was not an exercise of spot zoning nor was it arbitrary and capricious or unreasonable. To the contrary, the court found that the validity of the zoning resolution was fairly debatable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1778 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. McNamee v. Knoxville


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Eastern Section


824 S.W.2d 550; 1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 552



July 11, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Chancery Court, Knox County, No. 03A01-9103-CH-108, Hon. Frederick D. McDonald, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Knox County (Tennessee), which granted the motion to dismiss of appellee City of Knoxville, Tennessee. The property owners filed the quo warranto proceeding under Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103 to challenge the annexation ordinance passed by the City.


OVERVIEW: The property owners owned property within the annexation area at the time they initiated the action. Two of the property owners sold their property prior to trial and the third sold his property after a mistrial was declared due to a deadlocked jury. The property owners contended that the action should survive the transfer of the property. Affirming, the court concluded that the action did not survive after the property owners transferred their interests. Judicial review of the City's annexation was available only through the statute, § 6-51-103, which provided only limited rights. The provision for the substitution of parties under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 25.03 did not apply to the annexation statute. The court adopted the trial court's conclusion that the action abated when the property owners sold their property. The judiciary's only role in reviewing annexation actions was provided by the statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103. Although the action was brought in the name of the state, it could not continue the action once the property owners' interests had been transferred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for the collection of costs.

State v. Armstrong


No. 01-A-01-9104-CV-00149


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 530



July 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County, Tennessee at Franklin, No. 90425; Honorable Henry Denmark Bell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a minor, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Williamson County at Franklin (Tennessee), which adjudged defendant to be a delinquent in committing the offense of using a minor for obscene purposes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with committing the offense of using a minor for obscene purposes. Defendant contended that he and the victim had been dating and that the victim, then 14, consented to the sexual activity with defendant, then 17. The victim's mother reported the incident to authorities two days later. Defendant contended that Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-915(a), which prohibited the acts of promoting, employing, or using a minor to engage in or assist in sexual conduct by the minor alone or with some person, did not prohibit the promotion of sexual conduct between the minor and the promoter. Defendant was acquitted of a charge of rape but adjudged a delinquent for using a minor for obscene purposes. Affirming, the court held that a sexual encounter with any person, the instigator or a third person, was within the legislative concept of an "obscene purpose." The court found that the subsequent repeal of § 39-17-915 did not exonerate defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The court remanded the cause for any necessary further proceedings.

Ferguson v. Union City Daily Messenger, Inc.


No. 6437


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Jackson


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 515



July 2, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Ferguson v. Union City Daily Messenger, Inc., 845 S.W.2d 162, 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 665 (Tenn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court of Obion County, Tennessee. The Honorable David G. Hayes.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part, and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county purchasing agent (agent) sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Obion County (Tennessee) which granted summary judgment to defendants, newspaper and reporter, in the agent's suit for defamation, statutory interference with a contractual relationship, common law interference with an employment relationship, and outrageous conduct. The agent did not appeal the grant of summary judgment on the outrageous conduct claim.


OVERVIEW: The agent was originally elected by a county government committee to act as "finance director" but his position was later changed to "purchasing agent". The newspaper, through articles written by the reporter, published numerous articles regarding the financial problems of the county government and holding the agent responsible for the county's bills going unpaid. The agent filed suit against the newspaper and reporter, alleging defamation, statutory interference with a contractual relationship, and common law interference with an employment relationship. The trial court granted the newspaper and reporter's motion for summary judgment on all issues. On appeal, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court found that, regarding the defamation claim, a genuine issue of material fact existed regarding the scope of the agent's responsibilities, which was determinative of his status as a public official. Therefore, the court remanded for a trial on that issue. The court affirmed with respect to the issues of statutory and common law interference with a contractual relationship, finding that no factual issues existed as to those claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the newspaper and reporter on the agent's defamation suit but affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the newspaper and reporter on all other claims.

 

1781 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Dial-A-Page, Inc. v. Bissell


No. 01A01-9008-BC-00280


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


823 S.W.2d 202; 1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 453



June 5, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected. Second Correction.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Tennessee Public Service Commission of Nashville, Tennessee. The Honorable Mack Cherry. 



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pager corporation sought review of the order of appellee, the Tennessee Public Service Commission, which was issued in response to a motion for a declaratory ruling regarding the Commission's interpretation of Tenn. Code. Ann. § 65-30-105 of the Tennessee Radio Common Carrier (RCC) Act. The Commission held that pursuant to the Act, only one applicant could obtain authority to operate as a RCC in a given market at one time.


OVERVIEW: A large company acquired another company's paging operation which included four RCCs servicing Tennessee. These four RCCs were located in three separate markets. The Commission approved the transfer of these RCCs upon the condition that if an RCC applicant sought to enter any of the markets served by the RCCs, the Commission would find that the existing services in that market were inadequate because there may not be fully effective competition between the carriers regulated by the Commission, and the public interests would be served by such competition. Numerous RCCs, including the pager corporation, applied for authority to service the three markets involved. The court held that: (1) the administrative judge's interpretation of the Act was correct; (2) the Act was constitutional in that it created a regulated monopoly the purpose of which was rationally related to the public welfare as stated in Tenn. Code. Ann. § 65-30-102; and (3) the Act allowed a rebuttable preference in favor of existing RCCs in contiguous areas and this preference did not render the Act unconstitutional as it was only one factor to be considered in the granting of certificates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's order.

 

1782 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Locke v. Tollman


Shelby Juvenile No. 3


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Jackson


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 344



May 14, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Juvenile Court of Memphis, Shelby County, Tennessee; The Honorable Kenneth A. Turner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant natural father appealed from a judgment of the Juvenile Court of Memphis, Shelby County (Tennessee), which determined that he was the natural and biological father of plaintiff mother's child in the mother's paternity action. The juvenile court ordered him to pay birth expenses, child support, and future medical expenses, and granted him visitation that did not include overnight visitation.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought a paternity action against the father and a blood test established the likelihood of parentage. A juvenile court referee determined parentage, ordered payment of expenses of birth, medical expenses in the future, and child support. On appeal to the judge, the judgment was the same and included visitation on every other weekend on Saturday and Sunday, but with no overnight visitation. The father appealed and claimed that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-108(b) violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment and of the Tennessee Constitution. The court affirmed. Section 36-2-108(b) required the juvenile court to make provision for the birth expenses in an order as a result of a paternity action. It did not require the father to pay all of the expenses. The judgment was supported by substantial evidence, and the juvenile court did not abuse its discretion in ordering the payment under the facts submitted. The child visitation order was also supported by substantial evidence and was subject to change as the child grew older.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State ex rel. Smith v. Church Hill


03A01-9102-CH-00048


Court of Appeals of Tennessee


828 S.W.2d 385; 1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 354



May 9, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Chancery Court, Hawkins, County, Hon. Dennis H. Inman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a decree of the Chancery Court of Hawkins County (Tennessee) upholding the annexation of their property by defendant, the Town of Church Hill.


OVERVIEW: The Town, as requested by the property owners, annexed a long, narrow strip on the north side of the property owners' farm. After the annexation, the property owners subdivided the portion of the farm which lay to the north of the annexed tract. By referendum pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-51-104 and 6-51-105, the Town annexed territory beginning at the corporate limits line along the north end of the subdivision thence east across a river to its east bank, then south, crossing back over the river to the Town corporate limits, encompassing all of the property owners' farm. On appeal, the court rejected the property owners' contention that the previously annexed strip of land created a corridor or a narrow strip of land which was included in the annexation for the sole purpose of making the land in the subdivision contiguous with the property owners' farm. Since the Town correctly followed the statutes in its annexation referendum, the court rejected the property owners' equal protection and due process argument which challenged their farm's being included in the same referendum with the subdivision.


OUTCOME: The decree was affirmed. The case was remanded for any further necessary proceedings.

Spurlock v. Pioneer Credit Co.


C.A. No. 1386


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Eastern Section, at Knoxville


1991 Tenn. App. LEXIS 249



April 11, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Permission to Appeal Denied September 9, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tenn. LEXIS 351.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Law Court, Knox County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtors sought review of a judgment from the Law Court of Knox County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a lender and attorney, which dismissed the debtors' action for malicious prosecution.


OVERVIEW: The debtors borrowed a sum of money from the lender secured by a lien on an automobile, the agreement providing that the collateral was not to have been relocated outside the State without the lender's written authorization. The debtors relocated the automobile to the State of Ohio, and the lender urged the institution of criminal proceedings under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-3-927, which dealt with the concealment of collateral or its removal from the State. The criminal charges were dismissed on the ground that § 39-3-927 was unconstitutional, and the debtors then filed an action against the lender and the attorney for malicious prosecution. The trial court granted the motions for summary judgment filed by the lender and the attorney, from which the debtors appealed. On appeal, the court upheld the trial court's grant of the motions for summary judgment because the dismissal of the criminal proceedings on grounds of alleged unconstitutionality failed to constitute proof that the prosecution "terminated in favor of the accused," which was required for a successful malicious prosecution action. The court construed "terminated in favor of the accused" as consistent with innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment dismissing the debtors' action for malicious prosecution.

Rogers v. Donelson-Hermitage Chamber of Commerce


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9003-CV-00112


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


807 S.W.2d 242; 1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 816



November 21, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Circuit Court of Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee; The Honorable Hamilton Gayden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, race sponsors and race director, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which held that to allow the sponsors and director to assert Tenn. Code Ann. § 70-1-102 as a statutory defense to the wrongful death action filed by appellee parents was an unconstitutional retroactive application of that legislation.


OVERVIEW: The race sponsors and director held a horse racing event in which the daughter of the parents participated. The daughter obtained a written release of liability from her mother. As the daughter crossed the finish line, she turned the horse's head hard to avoid vehicles that crossed her path and the horse fell and rolled over the daughter. She died two days later. The parents brought a wrongful death action against the sponsors and the director. The trial court held that to allow the sponsors and director to assert § 70-1-102 as a statutory defense was an unconstitutional retroactive application of that legislation. On appeal, the court affirmed and remanded. The law in effect on May 16, 1987, at the time of the daughter's injuries which later resulted in her death, was to be applied to establish the liability for the injuries. Section 70-1-102 became law on May 17, 1987 and there was no retroactive application of the statute for the sponsors and directors to use as a statutory defense. The mother could not execute a valid release as to the rights of her daughter to sue for injuries suffered from the alleged negligent acts of the sponsors and director.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which held that to allow the sponsors and director to assert a property owner's immunity statute as a statutory defense to the wrongful death action of the parents was an unconstitutional retroactive application of that legislation.

Hardin County ex rel. Harris v. Adamsville


No. 2


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Jackson


1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 801



November 9, 1990, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court of Hardin County, Tennessee; The Honorable W. Walton West, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, annexing city, its mayor, and its commissioners, sought review of an order from the Chancery Court of Hardin County (Tennessee), which denied its motion to dismiss for improper venue, a suit disputing the annexation of a town filed by plaintiffs, county, a county resident, and town incorporators.


OVERVIEW: The annexing city annexed a town in a different county. Defendants filed suit in the county in which the town was located to dispute the annexation. Plaintiffs filed a motion to dismiss the suit for improper venue and the trial court denied it. Upon review, the court reversed, holding that under Tenn. The court held that § 29-35-111 had since been amended to provide different venue rules, but § 29-35-111 was a procedural statute; thus it could only be applied retrospectively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendants' motion to dismiss for improper venue plaintiffs' suit disputing the annexation of a town.

 

1788 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Ezell v. Graves


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9002-CV-00086


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


807 S.W.2d 700; 1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 746



October 10, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Perry County Circuit Court at Linden, Tennessee; The Honorable Cornelia Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of the judgment of the Perry County Circuit Court (Tennessee), which granted the summary judgment motion of defendant real estate agents dismissing the libel of title action of the landowners, concluding that the landowners failed to establish the existence of any special damages.


OVERVIEW: The landowners brought a successful action to quiet title against the real estate brokers for advertising land for sale that included the landowners' property. They then brought an action against the real estate brokers for libel of title. The trial court summarily dismissed the action, holding that the landowners were required to prove that an actual purchaser was deterred by the real estate brokers' actions and that the landowners' earlier expenses were not recoverable as special damages. On review, the court reversed the summary judgment. The court held that a particular purchaser's being deterred from purchasing the property was not a prerequisite because the landowners could show that the actions caused them actual pecuniary loss and they should not have to sell property they wished to keep in order to be made whole. Expenses incurred in the action to quiet title were recoverable as special damages because they were directly and proximately caused by the real estate brokers' conduct. The complaint was sufficient because it put the real estate brokers on notice as to the claim against them and gave rise to a reasonable inference that the real estate agents acted maliciously.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary dismissal of the landowners' libel of title action against the real estate agents. The court remanded the cause for further consistent proceedings.

 

1789 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Tennessee Manufactured Housing Ass'n v. Metropolitan Government of Nashville


Appeal No. 01-A-01-9001-CH-00018


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


798 S.W.2d 254; 1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 605



August 24, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville, Tennessee; The Honorable Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a landowner and an advocacy group, sought review of an order of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that found in favor of defendant city in an action challenging Nashville, Tenn., zoning ordinance § 22.10, which prohibited placing manufactured housing in residential districts. The trial court held that Tenn. Code Ann. §13-24-201 (1987) did not protect the landowner's double-wide manufactured home.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought to place a double-wide manufactured home on property zoned for single-family residences. When the city refused his permit and refused to rezone his property to allow the manufactured home, he and an advocacy group filed an action against the city. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in its interpretation of § 13-24-201. Because the statute could be interpreted two ways, the court looked to legislative intent to determine whether the statute excluded all structures coming within the definition of a manufactured home under § 68-36-202(4), as well as mobile homes constructed as a single, self-contained unit. The court found that the legislators intended to exempt structures that were manufactured and transported in at least two sections and then joined together at the site. The completed structure had to have the same general appearance as a site built home. Although the landowner's double-wide came within the city zoning ordinance's definition of mobile home, the court held that to construe the ordinance that way would have violated the statute; therefore, the landowner's home was not prohibited by the zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that the city could refuse to allow the landowner to locate a double-wide manufactured home on his property. The court remanded the case to the trial court to enter a decision in accordance with the court's opinion. The court taxed the costs of the appeal to the city.
