Crigger v. Columbia Power & Water Systems


No. 01-A-01-9001-CV-00036


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 606; 119 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,665



August 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 21, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 669.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Law Court, Maury County, Honorable Jim T. Hamilton, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a judgment entered in the Law Court of Maury County (Tennessee) that determined that it had breached an employment contract with plaintiff employee and awarded her reinstatement to her job with full back pay and benefits.


OVERVIEW: After 18 years, the employer discharged the employee for chronic abuse of sick leave and because of her past employment history. The trial court determined that the employer had breached the employment contract and ordered the employee reinstated to her job with full back pay and benefits. On appeal, the employee argued that a policy manual issued by the employer constituted an employment contract. The employer argued that the policy manual did not constitute an employment contract and that the employment relationship was terminable at will. The court agreed with the employer. The court pointed out that the express language found in the policy manual indicated that it was not a contract between the employer and its employees. The court then noted that employment for an indefinite period of time was a contract at-will, and could be terminated by either party with or without cause. In this case, the court found that the employment contract was a contract at-will. The court reviewed the record and found that the preponderance of the evidence established more than reasonable cause for the employer to discharge the employee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the employee's case.

 

1791 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Burris v. Ikard


C.A. No. 89-340-II


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Nashville


798 S.W.2d 246; 1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 443



June 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Circuit Court, Davidson County, No. 88C-157, Hon. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to and dismissed the administrator's wrongful death suit against defendant surgeon. The trial court also found Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-116 to be constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's wife underwent surgery in which pieces of Teflon felt called "pledgets" were used to close her lung. The "pledgets" enhanced infection, which required removal of the lung and caused her death. The administrator filed suit nine years later. The trial court granted the surgeon's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the administrator's suit since the case was not filed within one year as was required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-116(a)(4). On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that an exception to the one-year limitations period did not apply since the surgeon had intentionally, and not negligently, placed the "pledgets" into the body. The court further held that the evidence was insufficient to toll the statute of limitations for fraudulent concealment since "pledgets" were the best devices known at the time to support the wife's procedure, the surgeon was not aware of any warnings against their use, and the operation was discussed with the wife. The court concluded that Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-116(a) was constitutional, and was not persuaded by the administrator's argument that it barred his right to seek redress before the injury was known.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the surgeon and upholding the constitutionality of the statute. The court remanded the case for a determination of what costs to tax to the administrator.

 

1792 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Robertson County v. Browning-Ferris Industries of Tennessee, Inc.


Appeal No. 89-384-II


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


799 S.W.2d 662; 1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 343



May 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Custom Land Dev., Inc. v. Town of Coopertown, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 861 (Tenn. Ct. App., Dec. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Circuit Court for Robertson County, Tennessee; The Honorable James E. Walton, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a lessee and a lessor, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Robertson County (Tennessee) granted in favor of plaintiff county. The judgment permanently enjoined the lessee from using leased real property as a sanitary landfill without zoning approval from the county, a violation of a zoning ordinance of the county.


OVERVIEW: The county filed an action to declare that its ordinance was legal. Defendants filed an action seeking injunctive relief from the ordinance. After the county enacted the ordinance, defendants entered into their lease agreement. The lessee operated a landfill on the lessor's property with knowledge that this violated the ordinance. Although the court upheld the injunction for defendants, the contested judgment of the trial court was reversed for the county. The action was remanded for the county to cure a defect in the ordinance by adding a zoning classification for sanitary landfills. The trial court improperly granted the county's request for relief because it was a legislative matter of zoning that the judiciary could not have performed. The court decided not to engage in "spot zoning" until after the ordinance was amended. The court found no evidence proving that a total exclusion of sanitary landfills from a county would have promoted the public health, safety, and morals. The court found no evidence that the lessee was misled to believe that a landfill was permitted. The court found that the lessee did not have a vested right to operate the landfill based on the facts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment challenged by defendants and entered for the county. The court upheld the permanent injunction against the lessee's use of the property as a sanitary landfill and in violation of an ordinance. Costs were imposed on the county.

 

1793 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Shelby County Government


Shelby Law No. 19


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Jackson


1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 301



April 27, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Law Court, Shelby County, The Honorable Joe C. Riley, Judge By Designation.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judge sought review of an order of the Law Court of Shelby County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment on behalf of defendants, a county and a mayor, in the judge's action to recover unpaid salary and other damages.


OVERVIEW: The judge had been convicted of mail fraud, perjury, and obstruction of justice. The judge's salary payments were immediately terminated. The judge remained imprisoned while his convictions were on appeal. Thereafter, the judge was officially removed from office.The judge filed suit to recover the unpaid salary, arguing that he had a constitutional entitlement to his salary until he was officially removed from office, including the period of time in which he was imprisoned. The trial court granted summary judgment for the county and the mayor. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that that the judge was entitled to his full salary until formally removed from the bench by constitutionally required procedures.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for entry of a judgment in favor of the judge.

 

1794 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of Griggs


No. 89-159-II


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


1990 Tenn. App. LEXIS 35



January 26, 1990, Filed; As Corrected February 7, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court, Giles County, Honarable James L. Weatherford, Judge .



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother challenged a judgment from the Chancery Court of Giles County (Tennessee), which found that it was in the best interest of her child not to allow the mother to revoke her surrender of the child for adoption by plaintiff adoptive parents. The mother argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-117(b) unconstitutionally denied certain natural parents the right to automatically revoke their surrender of parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother decided to surrender her infant, conceived as a result of rape, for adoption. She signed the surrender form before the trial court in the company of her mother and the adoptive parents' attorney. What she was told about her right to revoke the surrender was disputed. The mother testified that she was told she had an absolute right to revoke the surrender within 15 days. She also testified that she did not know that the adoptive parents could contest her right of revocation. She did understand, however, that after the surrender the child would become a ward of the court and that if she revoked the surrender, the trial court would have to decide what was in the best interest of the child. The mother argued that when she timely revoked the surrender, the trial court erred in finding that it was in the best interest of the child not to allow the mother's revocation of her surrender. The court affirmed the judgment because where a petition for adoption was filed, the state had an interest in seeing that such an action was not nullified unless it was in the best interest of the child to do so. The court upheld the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-117(b).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1795 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Eatherly v. Board of Zoning Appeals


App. No. 89-56-II


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


1989 Tenn. App. LEXIS 760



November 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CHANCERY COURT FOR DAVIDSON COUNTY AT NASHVILLE, TENNESSEE, THE HONORABLE ROBERT S. BRANDT, CHANCELLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of a judgment by the Chancery Court for Davidson County at Nashville (Tennessee), which affirmed a decision of defendant board of zoning appeals denying the owner's application for a conditional use permit to build an asphalt plant in an industrial area.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed an application for a conditional use permit to build an asphalt plant on property in an industrial area. The board denied the permit on the ground that the property did not have direct access to a street designated on a major street plan as required by Nashville, Tenn., Zoning Reg. § 103.71. The trial court affirmed the decision of the board. On appeal the court held that the language of § 103.71 was clear and unambiguous, requiring direct access to a street designated on the major street plan and not merely access. The court noted that the phrase "direct access" was not an arcane or technical term and that its significance could be discerned from the ordinary and natural meaning of its words. The court found that § 103.71 was not unconstitutional because there was a rational basis for its classification. By requiring asphalt plants to be located on major roads, those roads would be able to accommodate the traffic more safely and would be better able to withstand the wear and tear of the heavy trucks going to and from the plants. The court concluded, therefore, that the property owner had failed to demonstrate the regulation's unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1796 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Minor Child A. Doe v. Chattanooga


C. A. No. 876


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Knoxville


1989 Tenn. App. LEXIS 744



November 6, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied In Part and Granted In Part January 24, 1990 and Reported at 1990 Tenn App. LEXIS 82. Application for Permission to Appeal Denied October 29, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tenn. LEXIS 397.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court, Hamilton County, Honorable Samuel H. Payne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mother and daughter, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Hamilton County (Tennessee), which dismissed their complaint against defendants, police officers and a city, alleging that defendants violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for failing to conduct a proper investigation into the alleged rape of the daughter.


OVERVIEW: The daughter and the mother were white, and the mother resided with a African American male. They alleged that because of that association, defendants negligently failed to investigate an alleged rape incident that happened to the daughter. It was alleged that defendants violated § 1983 for failing to conduct a proper investigation and deprived plaintiffs of their equal protection. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court held that as to the equal protection exception, the daughter and the mother alleged that defendants' failure to arrest the rapist and to continue the investigation was a result of her being a woman. That allegation was sufficient to state a claim under § 1983. The complaint alleged that the city tolerated a policy or custom which encouraged, promoted, and permitted disparate treatment based upon race. That allegation was sufficient to state a cause of action against the city. The part of the order of the trial court dismissing plaintiffs' action based on negligence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the complaint of the mother and the daughter against the police officers and the city, which alleged that defendants failed to conduct a proper investigation into the daughter's alleged rape.

 

1797 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Hull v. Lawson


No. 89-206-II


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Middle Section, at Nashville


1989 Tenn. App. LEXIS 733



November 3, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Chancery Court, Davidson County, The Honorable C. Allen High, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of the judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee), which upheld respondent Commissioner of Safety's decision ordering forfeiture of certain currency that had been seized pursuant to the Drug Control Act, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 53-11-101 to -415 (1988) and upheld the Commissioner's order requiring the claimant to pay storage fees and administrative costs for the seizure of his vehicle.


OVERVIEW: After police seized the claimant's currency and vehicle, the claimant's attorney requested a hearing on the vehicle forfeiture. The Commissioner ordered the forfeiture of the currency by default, required the claimant to pay storage fees and administrative costs, and restored the vehicle to the claimant upon payment of $ 500 to a drug fund. On review, the trial court determined that the currency was properly forfeited by the Commissioner, but that there was no authority to support the Commissioner's conditioning the return of the seized vehicle on payment into a drug fund. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the trial court did not err in upholding the forfeiture of the currency because under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-322(b)(1), the claimant lost his right to appeal the forfeiture order 60 days after it was issued; and (2) the trial court did not err in upholding the Commissioner's order requiring the claimant to pay storage fees and administrative costs for the claimant's vehicle because the court was required to assume that the costs assessed to the claimant were reasonable and there was nothing in the record to compel a conclusion that the costs were not reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding the Commissioner's decision ordering forfeiture of the currency and remanded the cause to the trial court for any other further proceedings necessary.

 

1798 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Johnson


CA No. 262


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, At Knoxville


1989 Tenn. App. LEXIS 681



October 17, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Law Court, Sullivan County, Honorable Roger E. Thayer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Law Court, Sullivan County (Tennessee) granted visitation rights to appellee paternal grandparents. Appellant mother sought a review of the order of the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The stepfather had adopted the two minor children. The mother alleged that the grandparents' visitation rights statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-301 (Supp. 1988),was unconstitutionally vague, but that it did not apply because the father had terminated his parental rights. The mother alleged that the grandparents failed to prove that their visitation rights were in the best interests of the children and that the trial court's order for visitation rights was excessive. The court affirmed the trial court and held that the grandparents' visitation rights statute applied and that the grandparents met their burden of proof in a previous proceeding. The court modified the trial court's visitation schedule to provide for visitation the first Saturday of each month. The legislative intent was that the paternal grandparents had visitation rights even though the children had been adopted by their stepfather. The father's termination of his parental rights did not affect his parents' right to visit their grandchildren. The paternal grandparents had established a close relationship with the minor children and it was in the best interests of the children to continue that relationship.


OUTCOME: The court modified the visitation schedule ordered by the trial court. The court affirmed the trial court's order, as modified, that granted visitation rights to the paternal grandparents.

 

1799 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Wildridge v. Wildridge


No. 1


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Jackson


1989 Tenn. App. LEXIS 586



September 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the Circuit Court, Gibson County, No. 2778, HON. MARION H. HOLMES, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ex-husband appealed from a judgment by the Circuit Court of Gibson County (Tennessee), which ordered the husband to pay child support as set out in a property settlement agreement entered into with plaintiff ex-wife and determined that a farm indebtedness was an obligation of the ex-husband that was not obviated by a subsequent transfer of the title to the farm to the ex-wife and the assumption by her of the indebtedness.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband and ex-wife entered into a property settlement agreement that dealt with child custody, child support, property division, and alimony. The agreement was incorporated by reference into their final decree. The ex-wife sought to hold the ex-husband in contempt for the absence of payments since their last separation and payment of the child support as a matter of contract. The ex-husband requested a modification of the decree to eliminate his obligation for two of his daughters who had attained the age of 18. The trial court continued the support as detailed in the agreement. On appeal, the court held that the father was relieved of his obligation to provide support for his oldest child because she was emancipated, living in a common law marriage apart from her mother, and had abandoned formal education. The court determined from the context and content of the agreement that there was no agreement to pay support to the ex-wife for the emancipated adult child for whom no support was being provided. The court held that the farm property was not alimony in solido material. The original indebtednesses were assumed by the ex-wife, and new indebtednesses negotiated.


OUTCOME: The court reduced the child support payments the ex-husband was required to pay the ex-wife and reversed that part of the judgement requiring the ex-husband to pay an indebtedness on a farm. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

1800 of 2007 DOCUMENTS


Childress v. Bennett


C.A. No. 89-45-II


Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Western Section, at Nashville


1989 Tenn. App. LEXIS 546



August 16, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal Granted January 2, 1989
Reversed by, Remanded by Childress v. Bennett, 816 S.W.2d 314, 1991 Tenn. LEXIS 318 (Tenn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Coffee County Circuit Court, Honorable Gerald L. Ewell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice case against defendant doctor, plaintiff patient filed an interlocutory appeal in which he challenged an order that was entered by the Coffee County Circuit Court (Tennessee). The order denied his motions to allow portions of his expert witness' deposition testimony into evidence and to waive the requirements for expert witnesses set out in Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-115 (b).


OVERVIEW: The trial court excluded the admission of all or portions of the patient's medical expert's deposition under the provisions of § 29-26-115(b), which provided that no health care professional was competent to testify in court as to the standard of care in a medical malpractice action unless he was licensed in Tennessee or a contiguous bordering state and he practiced his profession or specialty in one of these states during the year preceding the date that the alleged injury or wrongful act occurred. The court reversed the exclusion of portions of the deposition. The court held that the trial court erred in excluding the deposition of the patient's expert in its entirety. The court stated that § 29-26-115 was explicit that the requirements of § 29-26-115(b) applied to witnesses who were required to prove the three elements of the cause of action set out in § 29-26-115(a). However, this did not necessarily mean that all other medical expert witnesses were excluded. Only medical expert witnesses who were called to establish the § 29-26-115(a) standard of care requirements were required to be licensed and practicing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that excluded the patient's medical expert's deposition testimony into evidence.
